I be condemn to do this , for neither I nor any of my kindred can die till I have root up this great tree , ' reply the king of the eagle .
` But it be now even , and I need work no more to-day .
Come to my house with me , and be my guest for the night . '
The prince accept gratefully the eagle 's invitation , for he be tire and hungry .
They be receive at the palace by the king 's beautiful daughter , who give order that dinner should be lay for them at once .
While they be eat , the eagle question his guest about his travel , and if he be wander for pleasure 's sake , or with any special aim .
Then the prince tell him everything , and how he could never turn back till he have discover the Land of Immortality .
` Dear brother , ' say the eagle , ` you have discover it already , and it rejoice my heart to think that you will stay with u .
Have you not just hear me say that death have no power either over myself or any of my kindred till that great tree be root up ?
It will take me six hundred year ' hard work to do that ; so marry my daughter and let u all live happily together here .
After all , six hundred year be an eternity ! '
` Ah , dear king , ' reply the young man , ` your offer be very tempting !
But at the end of six hundred year we should have to die , so we should be no good off !
No , I must go on till I find the country where there be no death at all . '
Then the princess speak , and try to persuade the guest to change his mind , but he sorrowfully shake his head .
At length , see that his resolution be firmly fix , she take from a cabinet a little box which contain her picture , and give it to him say : ` As you will not stay with u , prince , accept this box , which will sometimes recall u to your memory .
If you be tire of travel before you come to the Land of Immortality , open this box and look at my picture , and you will be bear along either on earth or in the air , quick a thought , or swift a the whirlwind . '
The prince thank her for her gift , which he place in his tunic , and sorrowfully bid the eagle and his daughter farewell .
Never be any present in the world as useful a that little box , and many time do he bless the kind thought of the princess .
One even it have carry him to the top of a high mountain , where he saw a man with a bald head , busily engage in dig up spadeful of earth and throw them in a basket .
When the basket be full he take it away and return with an empty one , which he likewise fill .
The prince stand and watch him for a little , till the bald-headed man look up and say to him : ` Dear brother , what surprise you so much ? ' '
I be wonder why you be fill the basket , ' reply the prince .
` Oh ! '
reply the man , ' I be condemn to do this , for neither I nor any of my family can die till I have dig away the whole of this mountain and make it level with the plain .
But , come , it be almost dark , and I shall work no longer . '
And he pluck a leaf from a tree close by , and from a rough digger he be change into a stately bald-headed king .
` Come home with me , ' he add ; ` you must be tire and hungry , and my daughter will have supper ready for u . '
The prince accept gladly , and they go back to the palace , where the bald-headed king 's daughter , who be still more beautiful than the other princess , welcome them at the door and lead the way into a large hall and to a table cover with silver dish .
While they be eat , the bald-headed king ask the prince how he have happen to wander so far , and the young man tell him all about it , and how he be seek the Land of Immortality .
` You have find it already , ' answer the king , ` for , a I say , neither I nor my family can die till I have level this great mountain ; and that will take full eight hundred year longer .
Stay here with u and marry my daughter .
Eight hundred year be surely long enough to live . '
` Oh , certainly , ' answer the prince ; ` but , all the same , I would rather go and seek the land where there be no death at all . '
So next morning he bid them farewell , though the princess beg him to stay with all her might ; and when she find that she could not persuade him she give him a a remembrance a gold ring .
This ring be still more useful than the box , because when one wish oneself at any place one be there directly , without even the trouble of fly to it through the air .
The prince put it on his finger , and thank her heartily , go his way .
He walk on for some distance , and then he recollect the ring and thought he would try if the princess have speak truly a to it power . '
I wish I be at the end of the world , ' he say , shut his eye , and when he open them he be stand in a street full of marble palace .
The men who pass him be tall and strong , and their clothes be magnificent .
He stop some of them and ask in all the twenty-seven language he know what be the name of the city , but no one answer him .
Then his heart sank within him ; what should he do in this strange place if nobody could understand anything ?
he say .
Suddenly his eye fell upon a man dress after the fashion of his native country , and he run up to him and speak to him in his own tongue .
` What city be this , my friend ? '
he inquire .
` It be the capital city of the Blue Kingdom , ' reply the man , ` but the king himself be dead , and his daughter be now the ruler . '
With this news the prince be satisfy , and beg his countryman to show him the way to the young queen 's palace .
The man lead him through several street into a large square , one side of which be occupy by a splendid building that seem bear up on slender pillar of soft green marble .
In front be a flight of step , and on these the queen be sit wrap in a veil of shin silver mist , listen to the complaint of her people and deal out justice .
When the prince come up she saw directly that he be no ordinary man , and tell her chamberlain to dismiss the rest of her petitioner for that day , she sign to the prince to follow her into the palace .
Luckily she have be teach his language a a child , so they have no difficulty in talk together .
The prince tell all his story and how he be journey in search of the Land of Immortality .
When he have finish , the princess , who have listen attentively , rise , and take his arm , lead him to the door of another room , the floor of which be make entirely of needle , stick so close together that there be not room for a single needle more .
` Prince , ' she say , turn to him , ` you see these needle ?
Well , know that neither I nor any of my family can die till I have wear out these needle in sewing .
It will take at least a thousand year for that .
Stay here , and share my throne ; a thousand year be long enough to live ! '
` Certainly , ' answer he ; ` still , at the end of the thousand year I should have to die !
No , I must find the land where there be no death . '
The queen do all she could to persuade him to stay , but a her word prove useless , at length she give it up .
Then she say to him : ` As you will not stay , take this little golden rod a a remembrance of me .
It have the power to become anything you wish it to be , when you be in need . '
So the prince thank her , and put the rod in his pocket , go his way .
Scarcely have he leave the town behind him when he come to a broad river which no man might pass , for he be stand at the end of the world , and this be the river which flow round it .
Not know what to do next , he walk a little distance up the bank , and there , over his head , a beautiful city be float in the air .
He long to get to it , but how ?
neither road nor bridge be anywhere to be see , yet the city draw him upwards , and he felt that here at last be the country which he seek .
Suddenly he remember the golden rod which the mist-veiled queen have give him .
With a beating heart he fling it to the ground , wish with all his might that it should turn into a bridge , and fear that , after all , this might prove beyond it power .
But no , instead of the rod , there stand a golden ladder , lead straight up to the city of the air .
He be about to enter the golden gate , when there spring at him a wondrous beast , whose like he have never see .
` Out sword from the sheath , ' cry the prince , spring back with a cry .
And the sword leapt from the scabbard and cut off some of the monster 's head , but others grow again directly , so that the prince , pale with terror , stand where he be , call for help , and put his sword back in the sheath again .
The queen of the city hear the noise and look from her window to see what be happen .
Summoning one of her servant , she bid him go and rescue the stranger , and bring him to her .
The prince thankfully obey her order , and enter her presence .
The moment she look at him , the queen also felt that he be no ordinary man , and she welcome him graciously , and ask him what have bring him to the city .
In answer the prince tell all his story , and how he have travel long and far in search of the Land of Immortality .
` You have find it , ' say she , ` for I be queen over life and over death .
Here you can dwell among the immortal . '
A thousand year have pass since the prince first enter the city , but they have fly so fast that the time seem no more than six month .
There have not be one instant of the thousand year that the prince be not happy till one night when he dream of his father and mother .
Then the longing for his home come upon him with a rush , and in the morning he tell the Queen of the Immortals that he must go and see his father and mother once more .
The queen star at him with amazement , and cry : ` Why , prince , be you out of your sens ?
It be more than eight hundred year since your father and mother die !
There will not even be their dust remain . ' '
I must go all the same , ' say he .
` Well , do not be in a hurry , ' continue the queen , understand that he would not be prevent .
` Wait till I make some preparation for your journey . '
So she unlock her great treasure chest , and take out two beautiful flask , one of gold and one of silver , which she hang round his neck .
Then she show him a little trap-door in one corner of the room , and say : ` Fill the silver flask with this water , which be below the trap-door .
It be enchant , and whoever you sprinkle with the water will become a dead man at once , even if he have live a thousand year .
The golden flask you must fill with the water here , ' she add , point to a well in another corner .
` It spring from the rock of eternity ; you have only to sprinkle a few drop on a body and it will come to life again , if it have be a thousand year dead . '
The prince thank the queen for her gift , and , bid her farewell , go on his journey .
He soon arrive in the town where the mist-veiled queen reign in her palace , but the whole city have change , and he could scarcely find his way through the street .
In the palace itself all be still , and he wander through the room without meet anyone to stop him .
At last he enter the queen 's own chamber , and there she lay , with her embroidery still in her hand , fast asleep .
He pull at her dress , but she do not waken .
Then a dreadful idea come over him , and he run to the chamber where the needle have be keep , but it be quite empty .
The queen have break the last over the work she hold in her hand , and with it the spell be break too , and she lay dead .
Quick a think the prince pull out the golden flask , and sprinkle some drop of the water over the queen .
In a moment she move gently , and raise her head , open her eye .
` Oh , my dear friend , I be so glad you waken me ; I must have sleep a long while ! '
` You would have sleep till eternity , ' answer the prince , ` if I have not be here to waken you . '
At these word the queen remember about the needle .
She know now that she have be dead , and that the prince have restore her to life .
She give him thanks from her heart for what he have do , and vow she would repay him if she ever get a chance .
The prince take his leave , and set out for the country of the bald-headed king .
As he draw near the place he saw that the whole mountain have be dig away , and that the king be lie dead on the ground , his spade and bucket beside him .
But as soon a the water from the golden flask touch him he yawn and stretch himself , and slowly rise to his foot .
` Oh , my dear friend , I be so glad to see you , ' cry he , ' I must have sleep a long while ! '
` You would have sleep till eternity if I have not be here to waken you , ' answer the prince .
And the king remember the mountain , and the spell , and vow to repay the service if he ever have a chance .
Further along the road which lead to his old home the prince find the great tree tear up by it root , and the king of the eagle sit dead on the ground , with his wing outspread a if for flight .
A flutter run through the feather a the drop of water fell on them , and the eagle lift his beak from the ground and say : ` Oh , how long I must have slept !
How can I thank you for have awaken me , my dear , good friend ! '
` You would have sleep till eternity if I have not be here to waken you ' ; answer the prince .
Then the king remember about the tree , and know that he have be dead , and promise , if ever he have the chance , to repay what the prince have do for him .
At last he reach the capital of his father 's kingdom , but on reach the place where the royal palace have stand , instead of the marble gallery where he use to play , there lay a great sulphur lake , it blue flame dart into the air .
How be he to find his father and mother , and bring them back to life , if they be lie at the bottom of that horrible water ?
He turn away sadly and wander back into the street , hardly know where he be go ; when a voice behind him cry : ` Stop , prince , I have catch you at last !
It be a thousand year since I first begin to seek you . '
And there beside him stand the old , white-bearded , figure of Death .
Swiftly he draw the ring from his finger , and the king of the eagle , the bald-headed king , and the mist-veiled queen , hasten to his rescue .
In an instant they have seize upon Death and hold him tight , till the prince should have time to reach the Land of Immortality .
But they do not know how quickly Death could fly , and the prince have only one foot across the border , when he felt the other grasped from behind , and the voice of Death call : ` Halt !
now you be mine . '
The Queen of the Immortals be watch from her window , and cry to Death that he have no power in her kingdom , and that he must seek his prey elsewhere .
` Quite true , ' answered Death ; ` but his foot be in my kingdom , and that belong to me ! '
` At any rate half of him be mine , ' reply the Queen , ` and what good can the other half do you ?
Half a man be no use , either to you or to me !
But this once I will allow you to cross into my kingdom , and we will decide by a wager whose he be . '
And so it be settle .
Death step across the narrow line that surround the Land of Immortality , and the queen propose the wager which be to decide the prince 's fate . '
I will throw him up into the sky , ' she say , ` right to the back of the morning star , and if he fall down into this city , then he be mine .
But if he should fall outside the wall , he shall belong to you . '
In the middle of the city be a great open square , and here the queen wish the wager to take place .
When all be ready , she put her foot under the foot of the prince and swung him into the air .
Up , up , he go , high amongst the star , and no man 's eye could follow him .
Had she throw him up straight ?
the queen wonder anxiously , for , if not , he would fall outside the wall , and she would lose him for ever .
The moment seem long while she and Death stand gaze up into the air , wait to know whose prize the prince would be .
Suddenly they both catch sight of a tiny speck no big than a wasp , right up in the blue .
Was he come straight ?
No !
Yes !
But a he be near the city , a light wind spring up , and sway him in the direction of the wall .
Another second and he would have fall half over it , when the queen sprang forward , seize him in her arm , and fling him into the castle .
Then she command her servant to cast Death out of the city , which they do , with such hard blow that he never dare to show his face again in the Land of Immortality .

The Stone-Cutter Once upon a time there live a stone-cutter , who go every day to a great rock in the side of a big mountain and cut out slab for gravestone or for house .
He understand very well the kind of stone want for the different purpose , and a he be a careful workman he have plenty of customer .
For a long time he be quite happy and content , and ask for nothing good than what he have .
Now in the mountain dwell a spirit which now and then appear to men , and help them in many way to become rich and prosperous .
The stone-cutter , however , have never see this spirit , and only shake his head , with an unbelieving air , when anyone spoke of it .
But a time be come when he learn to change his opinion .
One day the stone-cutter carry a gravestone to the house of a rich man , and saw there all sort of beautiful thing , of which he have never even dream .
Suddenly his daily work seem to grow harder and heavy , and he say to himself : ` Oh , if only I be a rich man , and could sleep in a bed with silken curtain and golden tassel , how happy I should be ! '
And a voice answer him : ` Your wish be hear ; a rich man you shall be ! '
At the sound of the voice the stone-cutter look round , but could see nobody .
He think it be all his fancy , and pick up his tool and go home , for he do not feel inclined to do any more work that day .
But when he reach the little house where he live , he stand still with amazement , for instead of his wooden hut be a stately palace fill with splendid furniture , and most splendid of all be the bed , in every respect like the one he have envy .
He be nearly beside himself with joy , and in his new life the old one be soon forget .
It be now the beginning of summer , and each day the sun blaze more fiercely .
One morning the heat be so great that the stone-cutter could scarcely breathe , and he determine he would stay at home till the evening .
He be rather dull , for he have never learn how to amuse himself , and be peep through the closed blind to see what be go on in the street , when a little carriage pass by , draw by servant dress in blue and silver .
In the carriage sit a prince , and over his head a golden umbrella be hold , to protect him from the sun 's ray .
` Oh , if I be only a prince ! '
say the stone-cutter to himself , a the carriage vanish round the corner .
` Oh , if I be only a prince , and could go in such a carriage and have a golden umbrella hold over me , how happy I should be ! '
And the voice of the mountain spirit answer : ` Your wish be hear ; a prince you shall be . '
And a prince he be .
Before his carriage ride one company of men and another behind it ; servant dress in scarlet and gold bore him along , the coveted umbrella be hold over his head , everything heart could desire be his .
But yet it be not enough .
He look round still for something to wish for , and when he saw that in spite of the water he pour on his grass the ray of the sun scorch it , and that in spite of the umbrella held over his head each day his face grow brown and browner , he cry in his anger : ` The sun be mighty than I ; oh , if I be only the sun ! '
And the mountain spirit answer : ` Your wish be hear ; the sun you shall be . '
And the sun he be , and felt himself proud in his power .
He shoot his beam above and below , on earth and in heaven ; he burn up the grass in the field and scorch the face of prince as well a of poorer folk .
But in a short time he begin to grow tired of his might , for there seem nothing left for him to do .
Discontent once more filled his soul , and when a cloud cover his face , and hide the earth from him , he cry in his anger : ` Does the cloud hold captive my ray , and be it mighty than I ?
Oh , that I be a cloud , and mighty than any ! '
And the mountain spirit answer : ` Your wish be hear ; a cloud you shall be ! '
And a cloud he be , and lay between the sun and the earth .
He catch the sun 's beam and hold them , and to his joy the earth grow green again and flower blossom .
But that be not enough for him , and for day and week he pour forth rain till the river overflow their bank , and the crop of rice stand in water .
Towns and village be destroy by the power of the rain , only the great rock on the mountain side remain unmoved .
The cloud be amaze at the sight , and cry in wonder : ` Is the rock , then , mighty than I ?
Oh , if I be only the rock ! '
And the mountain spirit answer : ` Your wish be hear ; the rock you shall be !
And the rock he be , and glory in his power .
Proudly he stand , and neither the heat of the sun nor the force of the rain could move him .
` This be good than all ! '
he say to himself .
But one day he hear a strange noise at his foot , and when he look down to see what it could be , he saw a stone-cutter driving tool into his surface .
Even while he look a tremble feeling run all through him , and a great block break off and fell upon the ground .
Then he cry in his wrath : ` Is a mere child of earth mighty than a rock ?
Oh , if I be only a man ! '
And the mountain spirit answer : ` Your wish be hear .
A man once more you shall be ! '
And a man he be , and in the sweat of his brow he toil again at his trade of stone-cutting .
His bed be hard and his food scanty , but he have learn to be satisfy with it , and do not long to be something or somebody else .
And a he never ask for thing he have not get , or desire to be great and mighty than other people , he be happy at last , and hear the voice of the mountain spirit no longer .

The Gold-Bearded Man Once upon a time there live a great king who have a wife and one son whom he love very much .
The boy be still young when , one day , the king say to his wife : ' I feel that the hour of my death draw near , and I want you to promise that you will never take another husband but will give up your life to the care of our son . '
The queen burst into tear at these word , and sob out that she would never , never marry again , and that her son 's welfare should be her first thought as long a she live .
Her promise comfort the troubled heart of the king , and a few day after he die , at peace with himself and with the world .
But no sooner be the breath out of his body , than the queen say to herself , ` To promise be one thing , and to keep be quite another . '
And hardly be the last spadeful of earth flung over the coffin than she marry a noble from a neighbouring country , and get him make king instead of the young prince .
Her new husband be a cruel , wicked man , who treat his stepson very badly , and give him scarcely anything to eat , and only rag to wear ; and he would certainly have kill the boy but for fear of the people .
Now by the palace ground there run a brook , but instead of be a water-brook it be a milk-brook , and both rich and poor flock to it daily and draw as much milk a they choose .
The first thing the new king do when he be seat on the throne , be to forbid anyone to go near the brook , on pain of be seize by the watchman .
And this be purely spite , for there be plenty of milk for everybody .
For some day no one dare venture near the bank of the stream , but at length some of the watchman notice that early in the morning , just at dawn , a man with a gold beard come down to the brook with a pail , which he fill up to the brim with milk , and then vanish like smoke before they could get near enough to see who he be .
So they go and tell the king what they have see .
At first the king would not believe their story , but a they persist it be quite true , he say that he would go and watch the stream that night himself .
With the early streak of dawn the gold-bearded man appear , and fill his pail a before .
Then in an instant he have vanish , a if the earth have swallow him up .
The king stand star with eye and mouth open at the place where the man have disappear .
He have never see him before , that be certain ; but what matter much more be how to catch him , and what should be do with him when he be catch ?
He would have a cage build a a prison for him , and everyone would talk of it , for in other country thief be put in prison , and it be long indeed since any king have use a cage .
It be all very well to plan , and even to station a watchman behind every bush , but it be of no use , for the man be never catch .
They would creep up to him softly on the grass , a he be stoop to fill his pail , and just a they stretch out their hand to seize him , he vanish before their eye .
Time after time this happen , till the king grow mad with rage , and offer a large reward to anyone who could tell him how to capture his enemy .
The first person that come with a scheme be an old soldier who promise the king that if he would only put some bread and bacon and a flask of wine on the bank of the stream , the gold-bearded man would be sure to eat and drink , and they could shake some powder into the wine , which would send him to sleep at once .
After that there be nothing to do but to shut him in the cage .
This idea please the king , and he order bread and bacon and a flask of drugged wine to be place on the bank of the stream , and the watcher to be redouble .
Then , full of hope , he await the result .
Everything turn out just a the soldier have say .
Early next morning the gold-bearded man come down to the brook , ate , drank , and fell sound asleep , so that the watcher easily bound him , and carry him off to the palace .
In a moment the king have him fast in the golden cage , and show him , with ferocious joy , to the stranger who be visit his court .
The poor captive , when he awake from his drunken sleep , try to talk to them , but no one would listen to him , so he shut himself up altogether , and the people who come to stare take him for a dumb man of the wood .
He weep and moan to himself all day , and would hardly touch food , though , in dread that he should die and escape his tormentor , the king order his head cook to send him dish from the royal table .
The gold-bearded man have be in captivity about a month , when the king be force to make war upon a neighbouring country , and leave the palace , to take command of his army .
But before he go he call his stepson to him and say : ` Listen , boy , to what I tell you .
While I be away I trust the care of my prisoner to you .
See that he have plenty to eat and drink , but be careful that he do not escape , or even walk about the room .
If I return and find him go , you will pay for it by a terrible death . '
The young prince be thankful that his stepfather be go to the war , and secretly hop he might never come back .
Directly he have ride off the boy go to the room where the cage be keep , and never leave it night and day .
He even play his game beside it .
One day he be shoot at a mark with a silver bow ; one of his arrow fell into the golden cage .
` Please give me my arrow , ' say the prince , run up to him ; but the gold-bearded man answer : ` No , I shall not give it to you unless you let me out of my cage . ' '
I may not let you out , ' reply the boy , ` for if I do my stepfather say that I shall have to die a horrible death when he return from the war .
My arrow can be of no use to you , so give it to me . '
The man hand the arrow through the bar , but when he have do so he beg hard than ever that the prince would open the door and set him free .
Indeed , he pray so earnestly that the prince 's heart be touch , for he be a tender-hearted boy who pity the sorrow of other people .
So he shoot back the bolt , and the gold-bearded man step out into the world . '
I will repay you a thousand fold for that good deed . '
say the man , and then he vanish .
The prince begin to think what he should say to the king when he come back ; then he wonder whether it would be wise to wait for his stepfather 's return and run the risk of the dreadful death which have be promise him .
` No , ' he say to himself , ' I be afraid to stay .
Perhaps the world will be kinder to me than he have be . '
Unseen he steal out when twilight fell , and for many day he wander over mountain and through forest and valley without know where he be go or what he should do .
He have only the berry for food , when , one morning , he saw a wood-pigeon sitting on a bough .
In an instant he have fit an arrow to his bow , and be take aim at the bird , think what a good meal he would make off him , when his weapon fell to the ground at the sound of the pigeon 's voice : ` Do not shoot , I implore you , noble prince !
I have two little son at home , and they will die of hunger if I be not there to bring them food . '
And the young prince have pity , and unstring his bow .
` Oh , prince , I will repay your deed of mercy , say the grateful wood-pigeon .
` Poor thing !
how can you repay me ? '
ask the prince .
` You have forget , ' answer the wood-pigeon , ` the proverb that run , `` mountain and mountain can never meet , but one living creature can always come across another . '' '
The boy laugh at this speech and go his way .
By-and-by he reach the edge of a lake , and fly towards some rush which grow near the shore he behold a wild duck .
Now , in the day that the king , his father , be alive , and he have everything to eat he could possibly wish for , the prince always have wild duck for his birthday dinner , so he quickly fit an arrow to his bow and take a careful aim .
` Do not shoot , I pray you , noble prince ! '
cry the wild duck ; ' I have two little son at home ; they will die of hunger if I be not there to bring them food . '
And the prince have pity , and let fall his arrow and unstring his bow .
` Oh , prince !
I will repay your deed of mercy , ' exclaim the grateful wild duck .
` You poor thing !
how can you repay me ? '
ask the prince .
` You have forget , ' answer the wild duck , ` the proverb that run , `` mountain and mountain can never meet , but one living creature can always come across another . '' '
The boy laugh at this speech and go his way .
He have not wander far from the shore of the lake , when he notice a stork stand on one leg , and again he raise his bow and prepared to take aim .
` Do not shoot , I pray you , noble prince , ' cry the stork ; ' I have two little son at home ; they will die of hunger if I be not there to bring them food . '
Again the prince be fill with pity , and this time also he do not shoot .
` Oh , prince , I will repay your deed of mercy , ' cry the stork .
` You poor stork !
how can you repay me ? '
ask the prince .
` You have forget , ' answer the stork , ` the proverb that run , `` mountain and mountain can never meet , but one living creature can always come across another . '' '
The boy laugh at hear these word again , and walk slowly on .
He have not go far , when he fell in with two discharged soldier .
` Where be you go , little brother ? '
ask one . '
I be seek work , ' answer the prince .
` So be we , ' reply the soldier .
` We can all go together . '
The boy be glad of company and they go on , and on , and on , through seven kingdom , without find anything they be able to do .
At length they reach a palace , and there be the king stand on the step .
` You seem to be look for something , ' say he .
` It be work we want , ' they all answer .
So the king tell the soldier that they might become his coachman ; but he make the boy his companion , and give him room near his own .
The soldier be dreadfully angry when they hear this , for of course they do not know that the boy be really a prince ; and they soon begin to lay their head together to plot his ruin .
Then they go to the king .

` If you succeed , ' he add , ` you shall be my steward , but if you fail , I will put you to death on the spot . '
The unfortunate prince declare that he have never make any such boast a be report ; but it be all in vain .
The king do not believe him , and turn him into an empty room , bid his servant carry in the huge sack fill with wheat and barley , and scatter them in a heap on the floor .
The prince hardly know where to begin , and indeed if he have have a thousand people to help him , and a week to do it in , he could never have finish his task .
So he fling himself on the ground in despair , and cover his face with his hand .
While he lay thus , a wood-pigeon flew in through the window .
` Why be you weep , noble prince ? '
ask the wood-pigeon .
` How can I help weep at the task set me by the king .
For he say , if I fail to do it , I shall die a horrible death . '
` Oh , there be really nothing to cry about , ' answer the wood-pigeon soothingly . '
I be the king of the wood-pigeons , whose life you spar when you be hungry .
And now I will repay my debt , a I promise . '
So say he fly out of the window , leave the prince with some hope in his heart .

When the king come back he could not believe his eye ; but search a he might through the two heap , he could not find any barley among the wheat , or any wheat amongst the barley .
So he praise the prince for his industry and cleverness , and make him his steward at once .

say a voice just above him , and raise his head , he saw the wild duck .

The Three Robes Long , long ago , a king and queen reign over a large and powerful country .
What their name be nobody know , but their son be call Sigurd , and their daughter Lineik , and these young people be famed throughout the whole kingdom for their wisdom and beauty .
There be only a year between them , and they love each other so much that they could do nothing apart .
When they begin to grow up the king give them a house of their own to live in , with servant and carriage , and everything they could possibly want .
For many year they all live happily together , and then the queen fell ill , and know that she would never get good .
` Promise me two thing , ' she say one day to the king ; ` one , that if you marry again , a indeed you must , you will not choose a your wife a woman from some small state or distant island , who know nothing of the world , and will be take up with thought of her grandeur .

` That show a good heart , ' think the prince ; ` and when she be happy her beauty will soon come back . '
And without any further delay he beg the queen to consent to their betrothal , for the marriage must take place in his own country .
The queen be enchant .
She have hardly expect to succeed so soon , and she at once set about her preparation .
Indeed she wish to travel with the young couple , to make sure that nothing should go wrong ; but here the prince be firm , that he would take no one with him but Laufer , whom he think be Lineik .
They soon take leave of the queen , and set sail in a splendid ship ; but in a short time a dense fog come on , and in the dark the captain steer out of his course , and they find themselves in a bay which be quite strange to all the crew .
The prince order a boat to be lower , and go on shore to look about him , and it be not long before he notice the two beautiful tree , quite different from any that grow in Greece .
Calling one of the sailor , he bid him cut them down , and carry them on board the ship .
This be do , and a the sky be now clear they put out to sea , and arrive in Greece without any more adventure .
The news that the prince have bring home a bride have go before them , and they be greet with flowery arch and crown of coloured light .
The king and queen meet them on the step of the palace , and conduct the girl to the woman 's house , where she would have to remain until her marriage .
The prince then go to his own room and order that the tree should be bring in to him .
The next morning the prince bid his attendant bring his future bride to his own apartment , and when she come he give her silk which she be to weave into three robe -- one red , one green , and one blue -- and these must all be ready before the wedding .
The blue one be to be do first and the green last , and this be to be the most splendid of all , ` for I will wear it at our marriage , ' say he .
Left alone , Laufer sit and star at the heap of shin silk before her .
She do not know how to weave , and burst into tear a she think that everything would be discover , for Lineik 's skill in weave be as famous a her beauty .
As she sit with her face hidden and her body shake by sob , Sigurd in his tree heard her and be move to pity .
` Lineik , my sister , ' he call , softly , ` Laufer be weep ; help her , I pray you . '
` Have you forget the wrong her mother do to u ' answered Lineik , ` and that it be owe to her that we be banish from home ? '
But she be not really unforgiving , and very soon she slide quietly out of her hiding-place , and take the silk from Laufer 's hand begin to weave it .
So quick and clever be she that the blue dress be not only woven but embroider , and Lineik be safe back in her tree before the prince return .
` It be the most beautiful work I have ever see , ' say he , take up a bit .
` And I be sure that the red one will be still well , because the stuff be rich , ' and with a low bow he leave the room .
Laufer have hop secretly that when the prince have see the blue dress finish he would have let her off the other two ; but when she find she be expect to fulfil the whole task , her heart sank and she begin to cry loudly .
Again Sigurd hear her , and beg Lineik to come to her help , and Lineik , feel sorry for her distress , wove and embroider the second dress a she have do the first , mix gold thread and precious stone till you could hardly see the red of the stuff .
When it be do she glide into her tree just a the prince come in .
` You be as quick a you be clever , ' say he , admiringly .
` This look a if it have be embroider by the fairy !
But a the green robe must outshine the other two I will give you three day in which to finish it .
After it be ready we will be marry at once . '
Now , a he speak , there rise up in Laufer 's mind all the unkind thing that she and her mother have do to Lineik .
Could she hope that they would be forget , and that Lineik would come to her rescue for the third time ?
And perhaps Lineik , who have not forget the past either , might have leave her alone , to get on a best she could , have not Sigurd , her brother , implore her to help just once more .
So Lineik again slide out of her tree , and , to Laufer 's great relief , set herself to work .
When the shin green silk be ready she catch the sun 's ray and the moon 's beam on the point of her needle and weave them into a pattern such a no man have ever see .
But it take a long time , and on the third morning , just a she be put the last stitch into the last flower the prince come in .
Lineik jump up quickly , and try to get past him back to her tree ; but the fold of the silk be wrapped round her , and she would have fall have not the prince catch her . '
I have think for some time that all be not quite straight here , ' say he .
` Tell me who you be , and where you come from ? '
Lineik then tell her name and her story .
When she have end the prince turn angrily to Laufer , and declare that , a a punishment for her wicked lie , she deserve to die a shameful death .
But Laufer fell at his foot and beg for mercy .
It be her mother 's fault , she say : ` It be she , and not I , who pass me off a the Princess Lineik .
The only lie I have ever tell you be about the robe , and I do not deserve death for that . '
She be still on her knee when Prince Sigurd enter the room .
He pray the Prince of Greece to forgive Laufer , which he do , on condition that Lineik would consent to marry him .
` Not till my stepmother be dead , ' answer she , ` for she have bring misery to all that come near her . '
Then Laufer tell them that Blauvor be not the wife of a king , but an ogress who have steal her from a neighbouring palace and have bring her up a her daughter .
And besides be an ogress she be also a witch , and by her black art have sink the ship in which the father of Sigurd and Lineik have set sail .
It be she who have cause the disappearance of the courtier , for which no one could account , by eat them during the night , and she hop to get rid of all the people in the country , and then to fill the land with ogre and ogress like herself .
So Prince Sigurd and the Prince of Greece collect an army swiftly , and march upon the town where Blauvor have her palace .
They come so suddenly that no one knew of it , and if they have , Blauvor have eat most of the strong men ; and others , fearful of something they could not tell what , have secretly leave the place .
Therefore she be easily capture , and the next day be behead in the market-place .
Afterwards the two prince march back to Greece .
Lineik have no longer any reason for put off her wedding , and marry the Prince of Greece at the same time that Sigurd marry the princess .
And Laufer remain with Lineik a her friend and sister , till they find a husband for her in a great nobleman ; and all three couple live happily until they die .

The Six Hungry Beasts Once upon a time there live a man who dwell with his wife in a little hut , far away from any neighbour .
But they do not mind be alone , and would have be quite happy , if it have not be for a marten , who come every night to their poultry yard , and carry off one of their fowl .
The man lay all sort of trap to catch the thief , but instead of capture the foe , it happen that one day he get catch himself , and fall down , strike his head against a stone , and be kill .
Not long after the marten come by on the look out for his supper .
Seeing the dead man lie there , he say to himself : ` That be a prize , this time I have do well ' ; and drag the body with great difficulty to the sledge which be wait for him , drive off with his booty .
He have not drive far when he meet a squirrel , who bow and say : ` Good-morning , godfather !
what have you get behind you ? '
The marten laugh and answer : ` Did you ever hear anything so strange ?
The old man that you see here set trap about his hen-house , think to catch me but he fell into his own trap , and break his own neck .
He be very heavy ; I wish you would help me to draw the sledge . '
The squirrel do a he be ask , and the sledge move slowly along .
By-and-by a hare come run across a field , but stop to see what wonderful thing be come .
` What have you get there ? '
she ask , and the marten tell his story and beg the hare to help them pull .
The hare pull her hard , and after a while they be join by a fox , and then by a wolf , and at length a bear be add to the company , and he be of more use than all the other five beast put together .
Besides , when the whole six have sup off the man he be not so heavy to draw .
The bad of it be that they soon begin to get hungry again , and the wolf , who be the hungry of all , say to the rest : ` What shall we eat now , my friend , a there be no more man ? ' '
I suppose we shall have to eat the small of u , ' reply the bear , and the marten turn round to seize the squirrel who be much small than any of the rest .
But the squirrel run up a tree like lightning , and the marten remembering , just in time , that he be the next in size , slip quick a thought into a hole in the rock .
` What shall we eat now ? '
ask the wolf again , when he have recover from his surprise .
` We must eat the small of u , ' repeat the bear , stretch out a paw towards the hare ; but the hare be not a hare for nothing , and before the paw have touch her , she have dart deep into the wood .
Now that the squirrel , the marten , and the hare have all go , the fox be the small of the three who be leave , and the wolf and the bear explain that they be very sorry , but they would have to eat him .
Michael , the fox , do not run away a the others have do , but smile in a friendly manner , and remark : ` Things taste so stale in a valley ; one 's appetite be so much good up on a mountain . '
The wolf and the bear agree , and they turn out of the hollow where they have be walk , and choose a path that lead up the mountain side .
The fox trot cheerfully by his two big companion , but on the way he manage to whisper to the wolf : ` Tell me , Peter , when I be eaten , what will you have for your next dinner ? '
This simple question seem to put out the wolf very much .
What would they have for their next dinner , and , what be more important still , who would there be to eat it ?
They have make a rule always to dine off the small of the party , and when the fox be go , why of course , he be small than the bear .
These thought flash quickly through his head , and he say hastily : ` Dear brother , would it not be good for u to live together a comrade , and everyone to hunt for the common dinner ?
Is not my plan a good one ? '
` It be the best thing I have ever hear , ' answer the fox ; and a they be two to one the bear have to be content , though in his heart he would much have prefer a good dinner at once to any friendship .
For a few day all go well ; there be plenty of game in the forest , and even the wolf have as much to eat a he could wish .
One morning the fox a usual be go his round when he notice a tall , slender tree , with a magpie 's nest in one of the top branch .
Now the fox be particularly fond of young magpie , and he set about make a plan by which he could have one for dinner .
At last he hit upon something which he think would do , and accordingly he sit down near the tree and begin to stare hard at it .
` What be you look at , Michael ? '
ask the magpie , who be watch him from a bough .
` I 'm look at this tree .
It have just strike me what a good tree it would be to cut my new snow-shoes out of . '
But at this answer the magpie screech loudly , and exclaim : ` Oh , not this tree , dear brother , I implore you !
I have build my nest on it , and my young one be not yet old enough to fly . '
` It will not be easy to find another tree that would make such good snow-shoes , ' answer the fox , cock his head on one side , and gaze at the tree thoughtfully ; ` but I do not like to be ill-natured , so if you will give me one of your young one I will seek my snow-shoes elsewhere . '
Not know what to do the poor magpie have to agree , and fly back , with a heavy heart , he throw one of his young one out of the nest .
The fox seize it in his mouth and run off in triumph , while the magpie , though deeply grieve for the loss of his little one , find some comfort in the thought that only a bird of extraordinary wisdom would have dream of save the rest by the sacrifice of the one .
But what do you think happen ?
Why , a few day later , Michael the fox might have be see sit under the very same tree , and a dreadful pang shot through the heart of the magpie a he peep at him from a hole in the nest .
` What be you look at ? '
he ask in a trembling voice .
` At this tree .
I be just think what good snowshoe it would make , ' answer the fox in an absent voice , a if he be not think of what he be say .
` Oh , my brother , my dear little brother , do n't do that , ' cry the magpie , hop about in his anguish .
` You know you promise only a few day ago that you would get your snow-shoes elsewhere . '
` So I do ; but though I have search through the whole forest , there be not a single tree that be as good a this .
I be very sorry to put you out , but really it be not my fault .
The only thing I can do for you be to offer to give up my snow-shoes altogether if you will throw me down one of your young one in exchange . '
And the poor magpie , in spite of his wisdom , be oblige to throw another of his little one out of the nest ; and this time he be not able to console himself with the thought that he have be much clever than other people .
He sit on the edge of his nest , his head drooping and his feather all ruffle , look the picture of misery .
Indeed he be so different from the gay , jaunty magpie whom every creature in the forest knew , that a crow who be fly past , stop to inquire what be the matter .
` Where be the two young one who be not in the nest ? '
ask he . '
I have to give them to the fox , ' reply the magpie in a quivering voice ; ` he have be here twice in the last week , and want to cut down my tree for the purpose of make snow-shoes out of it , and the only way I could buy him off be by give him two of my young one . '
Oh , you fool , ' cry the crow , ` the fox be only try to frighten you .
He could not have cut down the tree , for he have neither axe nor knife .
Dear me , to think that you have sacrifice your young one for nothing !
Dear , dear !
how could you be so very foolish ! '
And the crow fly away , leave the magpie overcome with shame and sorrow .
The next morning the fox come to his usual place in front of the tree , for he be hungry , and a nice young magpie would have suit him very well for dinner .
But this time there be no cowering , timid magpie to do his bidding , but a bird with his head erect and a determined voice .
` My good fox , ' say the magpie put his head on one side and look very wise -- ` my good fox , if you take my advice , you will go home as fast a you can .
There be no use your talk about make snow-shoes out of this tree , when you have neither knife nor axe to cut it down with ! '
` Who have be teach you wisdom ? '
ask the fox , forget his manner in his surprise at this new turn of affair .
` The crow , who pay me a visit yesterday , ' answer the magpie .
` The crow be it ? '
say the fox , ` well , the crow have well not meet me for the future , or it may be the bad for him . '
As Michael , the cunning beast , have no desire to continue the conversation , he leave the forest ; but when he come to the high road he lay himself at full length on the ground , stretch himself out , just a if he be dead .
Very soon he notice , out of the corner of his eye , that the crow be fly towards him , and he keep stiller and stiffer than ever , with his tongue hang out of his mouth .
The crow , who want her supper very badly , hop quickly towards him , and be stoop forward to peck at his tongue when the fox give a snap , and catch him by the wing .
The crow know that it be of no use struggle , so he say : ` Ah , brother , if you be really go to eat me , do it , I beg of you , in good style .
Throw me first over this precipice , so that my feather may be strew here and there , and that all who see them may know that your cunning be great than mine . '
This idea please the fox , for he have not yet forgive the crow for deprive him of the young magpie , so he carry the crow to the edge of the precipice and throw him over , intend to go round by a path he know and pick him up at the bottom .
But no sooner have the fox let the crow go than he soar up into the air , and hover just out of teach of his enemy 's jaw , he cry with a laugh : ` Ah , fox !
you know well how to catch , but you can not keep . '
With his tail between his leg , the fox slunk into the forest .
He do not know where to look for a dinner , a he guess that the crow would have fly back before him , and put every one on their guard .
The notion of go to bed supperless be very unpleasant to him , and he be wonder what in the world he should do , when he chance to meet with his old friend the bear .
This poor animal have just lose his wife , and be go to get some one to mourn over her , for he felt her loss greatly .
He have hardly leave his comfortable cave when he have come across the wolf , who inquire where he be go . '
I be go to find a mourner , ' answer the bear , and tell his story .
` Oh , let me mourn for you , ' cry the wolf .
` Do you understand how to howl ? '
say the bear .
` Oh , certainly , godfather , certainly , ' reply the wolf ; but the bear say he should like to have a specimen of his howling , to make sure that he know his business .
So the wolf break forth in his song of lament : ` Hu , hu , hu , hum , hoh , ' he shout , and he make such a noise that the bear put up his paw to his ear , and beg him to stop .
` You have no idea how it be do .
Be off with you , ' say he angrily .
A little further down the road the hare be rest in a ditch , but when she saw the bear , she come out and speak to him , and inquire why he look so sad .
The bear tell her of the loss of his wife , and of his search after a mourner that could lament over her in the proper style .
The hare instantly offer her service , but the bear take care to ask her to give him a proof of her talent , before he accept them .
` Pu , pu , pu , pum , poh , ' pip the hare ; but this time her voice be so small that the bear could hardly hear her .
` That be not what I want , ' he say , ' I will bid you good morning . '
It be after this that the fox come up , and he also be strike with the bear 's altered look , and stop .
` What be the matter with you , godfather ? '
ask he , ` and where be you go ? ' '
I be go to find a mourner for my wife , ' answer the bear .
` Oh , do choose me , ' cry the fox , and the bear look at him thoughtfully .
` Can you howl well ? '
he say .
` Yes , beautifully , just listen , ' and the fox lift up his voice and sang weeping : ` Lou , lou , lou !
the famous spinner , the baker of good cake , the prudent housekeeper be torn from her husband !
Lou , lou , lou !
she be go !
she be go ! '
` Now at last I have find some one who know the art of lamentation , ' exclaim the bear , quite delight ; and he lead the fox back to his cave , and bid him begin his lament over the dead wife who be lie stretch out on her bed of grey moss .
But this do not suit the fox at all .
` One can not wail properly in this cave , ' he say , ` it be much too damp .
You have good take the body to the storehouse .
It will sound much finer there . '
So the bear carry his wife 's body to the storehouse , while he himself go back to the cave to cook some pap for the mourner .
From time to time he pause and listen for the sound of wailing , but he hear nothing .
At last he go to the door of the storehouse , and call to the fox : ` Why do n't you howl , godfather ?
What be you about ? '
And the fox , who , instead of weep over the dead bear , have be quietly eat her , answer : ` There only remain now her leg and the sol of her foot .

When the bear heard that he run back for the kitchen ladle , to give the traitor the beating he deserve .
But a he open the door of the storehouse , Michael be ready for him , and slip between his leg , dash straight off into the forest .
The bear , see that the traitor have escape , fling the ladle after him , and it just catch the tip of his tail , and that be how there come to be a spot of white on the tail of all fox .

How The Beggar Boy Turned Into Count Piro Once upon a time there live a man who have only one son , a lazy , stupid boy , who would never do anything he be tell .
When the father be die , he send for his son and tell him that he would soon be leave alone in the world , with no possession but the small cottage they live in and a pear tree which grow behind it , and that , whether he like it or not , he would have to work , or else he would starve .
Then the old man die .
But the boy do not work ; instead , he idle about a before , content himself with eat the pear off his tree , which , unlike other pear tree before or since , bore fruit the whole year round .
Indeed , the pear be so much fine than any you could get even in the autumn , that one day , in the middle of the winter , they attract the notice of a fox who be creep by .
` Dear me ; what lovely pears ! '
he say to the youth .
` Do give me a basket of them .
It will bring you luck ! '
` Ah , little fox , but if I give you a basketful , what be I to eat ? '
ask the boy .
` Oh , trust me , and do what I tell you , ' say the fox ; ' I know it will bring you luck . '
So the boy get up and pick some of the ripest pear and put them into a rush basket .
The fox thank him , and , take the basket in his mouth , trot off to the king 's palace and make his way straight to the king .
` Your Majesty , my master send you a few of his best pear , and begs you will graciously accept them , ' he say , lay the basket at the foot of the king .
` Pears !
at this season ? '
cry the king , peer down to look at them ; ` and , pray , who be your master ? '
` The Count Piro , ' answer the fox .
` But how do he manage to get pear in midwinter ? '
ask the king .
` Oh , he have everything he want , ' reply the fox ; ` he be rich even than you be , your Majesty . '
` Then what can I send him in return for his pear ? '
say the king .
` Nothing , your Majesty , or you would hurt his feeling , ' answer the fox .
` Well , tell him how heartily I thank him , and how much I shall enjoy them . '
And the fox go away .
He trot back to the cottage with his empty basket and tell his tale , but the youth do not seem a pleased to hear a the fox be to tell .
` But , my dear little fox , ' say he , ` you have bring me nothing in return , and I be so hungry ! '
` Let me alone , ' reply the fox ; ' I know what I be do .
You will see , it will bring you luck . '
A few day after this the fox come back again . '
I must have another basket of pear , ' say he .
` Ah , little fox , what shall I eat if you take away all my pear ? '
answer the youth .
` Be quiet , it will be all right , ' say the fox ; and take a big basket than before , he fill it quite full of pear .
Then he pick it up in his mouth , and trot off to the palace .
` Your Majesty , a you seem to like the first basket of pear , I have bring you some more , ' say he , ` with my master , the Count Piro 's humble respect . '
` Now , surely it be not possible to grow such pear with deep snow on the ground ? '
cry the king .
` Oh , that never affect them , ' answer the fox lightly ; ` he be rich enough to do anything .
But to-day he send me to ask if you will give him your daughter in marriage ? '
` If he be so much rich than I be , ' say the king , ' I shall be oblige to refuse .
My honour would not permit me to accept his offer . '
` Oh , your Majesty , you must not think that , ' reply the fox ; ` and do not let the question of a dowry trouble you .
The Count Piro would not dream of ask anything but the hand of the princess . '
` Is he really so rich that he can do without a dowry ? '
ask the king .
` Did I not tell your Majesty that he be rich than you ? '
answer the fox reproachfully .
` Well , beg him to come here , that we may talk together , ' say the king .
So the fox go back to the young man and say : ' I have tell the king that you be Count Piro , and have ask his daughter in marriage . '
` Oh , little fox , what have you do ? '
cry the youth in dismay ; ` when the king see me he will order my head to be cut off . '
` Oh , no , he wo n't ! '
reply the fox ; ` just do a I tell you . '
And he go off to the town , and stop at the house of the best tailor .
` My master , the Count Piro , beg that you will send him at once the fine coat that you have in your shop , ' say the fox , put on his grand air , ` and if it fit him I will call and pay for it to-morrow !
Indeed , a he be in a great hurry , perhaps it might be as well if I take it round myself . '
The tailor be not accustom to serve count , and he at once get out all the coat he have ready .
The fox choose out a beautiful one of white and silver , bid the tailor tie it up in a parcel , and carry the string in his teeth , he leave the shop , and go to a horse-dealer 's , whom he persuade to send his fine horse round to the cottage , say that the king have bid his master to the palace .
Very unwillingly the young man put on the coat and mount the horse , and ride up to meet the king , with the fox run before him .
` What be I to say to his Majesty , little fox ? '
he ask anxiously ; ` you know that I have never speak to a king before . '
` Say nothing , ' answer the fox , ` but leave the talk to me .
`` Good morning , your Majesty , '' will be all that be necessary for you . '
By this time they have reach the palace , and the king come to the door to receive Count Piro , and lead him to the great hall , where a feast be spread .
The princess be already seat at the table , but be as dumb a Count Piro himself .
` The Count speak very little , ' the king say at last to the fox , and the fox answer : ` He have so much to think about in the management of his property that he can not afford to talk like ordinary people . '
The king be quite satisfied , and they finish dinner , after which Count Piro and the fox take leave .
The next morning the fox come round again .
` Give me another basket of pear , ' he say .
` Very well , little fox ; but remember it may cost me my life , ' answer the youth .
` Oh , leave it to me , and do a I tell you , and you will see that in the end it will bring you luck , ' answer the fox ; and pluck the pear he take them up to the king .
` My master , Count Piro , send you these pear , ' he say , ` and ask for an answer to his proposal . '

` But I ca n't bring the princess here , little fox ? '
cry the young man in dismay .
` You leave everything to me , ' answer the fox ; ` have I not manage well so far ? '
And up at the palace preparation be make for a grand wedding , and the youth be marry to the princess .
After a week of feasting , the fox say to the king : ` My master wish to take his young bride home to his own castle . '
` Very well , I will accompany them , ' reply the king ; and he order his courtier and attendant to get ready , and the best horse in his stable to be bring out for himself , Count Piro and the princess .
So they all set out , and rode across the plain , the little fox run before them .
He stop at the sight of a great flock of sheep , which be feed peacefully on the rich grass .
` To whom do these sheep belong ? '

If they ask , just say the sheep belong to Count Piro ; it will be good for everybody . '
And the fox run hastily on , a he do not wish to be see talk to the shepherd .
Very soon the king come up .
` What beautiful sheep ! '
he say , draw up his horse . '
I have none so fine in my pasture .
Whose be they ? '
` Count Piro 's , ' answer the shepherd , who do not know the king .
` Well , he must be a very rich man , ' think the king to himself , and rejoice that he have such a wealthy son-in-law .
Meanwhile the fox have meet with a huge herd of pig , snuffle about the root of some tree .
` To whom do these pig belong ? '
he ask of the swineherd .
` To an ogre , ' reply he .
` Hush ! '
whisper the fox , though nobody could hear him ; ` do you see that troop of arm men rid towards u ?
If you tell them that the pig belong to the ogre they will kill them , and then the ogre will kill you !
If they ask , just say that the pig belong to Count Piro ; it will be good for everybody . '
And he run hastily on .
Soon after the king rode up .
` What fine pig ! '
he say , rein in his horse .
` They be fatter than any I have get on my farm .
Whose be they ? '
` Count Piro 's , ' answer the swineherd , who do not know the king ; and again the king felt he be lucky to have such a rich son-in-law .
This time the fox run fast than before , and in a flowery meadow he find a troop of horse feed .
` Whose horse be these ? '
he ask of the man who be watch them .
` An ogre 's , ' reply he .
` Hush ! '
whisper the fox , ` do you see that crowd of arm men come towards u ?
If you tell them the horse belong to an ogre they will drive them off , and then the ogre will kill you !
If they ask , just say they be Count Piro 's ; it will be good for everybody . '
And he run on again .
In a few minute the king rode up .
` Oh , what lovely creatures !
how I wish they be mine ! '
he exclaim .
` Whose be they ? '
Count Piro 's , ' answer the man , who do not know the king ; and the king 's heart leapt a he think that if they belong to his rich son-in-law they be as good a his .
At last the fox come to the castle of the ogre himself .
He run up the step , with tear fall from his eye , and cry : ` Oh , you poor , poor people , what a sad fate be yours ! '
` What have happen ? '
ask the ogre , tremble with fright .
` Do you see that troop of horseman who be rid along the road ?
They be send by the king to kill you ! '
` Oh , dear little fox , help u , we implore you ! '
cry the ogre and his wife .
` Well , I will do what I can , ' answer the fox .
` The best place be for you both to hide in the big oven , and when the soldier have go by I will let you out . '
The ogre and ogress scramble into the oven as quick a thought , and the fox bang the door on them ; just a he do so the king come up .
` Do u the honour to dismount , your Majesty , ' say the fox , bow low .
` This be the palace of Count Piro ! '
` Why it be more splendid than my own ! '
exclaim the king , look round on all the beautiful thing that fill the hall .
But why be there no servant ? '
` His Excellency the Count Piro wish the princess to choose them for herself , ' answer the fox , and the king nod his approval .
He then ride on , leave the bridal pair in the castle .
But when it be dark and all be still , the fox crept downstairs and light the kitchen fire , and the ogre and his wife be burn to death .
The next morning the fox say to Count Piro : ` Now that you be rich and happy , you have no more need of me ; but , before I go , there be one thing I must ask of you in return : when I die , promise me that you will give me a magnificent coffin , and bury me with due honour . '
` Oh , little , little fox , do n't talk of dying , ' cry the princess , nearly weeping , for she have take a great liking to the fox .
After some time the fox think he would see if the Count Piro be really grateful to him for all he have do , and go back to the castle , where he lay down on the door-step , and pretend to be dead .
The princess be just go out for a walk , and directly she saw him lie there , she burst into tear and fell on her knee beside him .
` My dear little fox , you be not dead , ' she wail ; ` you poor , poor little creature , you shall have the fine coffin in the world ! ' '
A coffin for an animal ? '
say Count Piro .
` What nonsense !
just take him by the leg and throw him into the ditch . '
Then the fox spring up and cry : ` You wretched , thankless beggar ; have you forget that you owe all your rich to me ? '
Count Piro be frighten when he hear these word , a he think that perhaps the fox might have power to take away the castle , and leave him as poor a when he have nothing to eat but the pear off his tree .
So he try to soften the fox 's anger , say that he have only speak in joke , a he have know quite well that he be not really dead .
For the sake of the princess , the fox let himself be soften , and he live in the castle for many year , and play with Count Piro 's child .
And when he actually do die , his coffin be make of silver , and Count Piro and his wife follow him to the grave .
