The Rogue And The Herdsman In a tiny cottage near the king 's palace there once live an old man , his wife , and his son , a very lazy fellow , who would never do a stroke of work .
He could not be get even to look after their one cow , but leave her to look after herself , while he lay on a bank and go to sleep in the sun .
For a long time his father bore with him , hop that a he grow old he might gain more sense ; but at last the old man 's patience be wear out , and he tell his son that he should not stay at house in idleness , and must go out into the world to seek his fortune .
The young man saw that there be no help for it , and he set out with a wallet full of food over his shoulder .
At length he come to a large house , at the door of which he knock .
` What do you want ? '
ask the old man who open it .
And the youth tell him how his father have turn him out of his house because he be so lazy and stupid , and he need shelter for the night .
` That you shall have , ' reply the man ; ` but to-morrow I shall give you some work to do , for you must know that I be the chief herdsman of the king . '
The youth make no answer to this .
He felt , if he be to be make to work after all , that he might as well have stay where he be .
But a he do not see any other way of get a bed , he go slowly in .
The herdsman 's two daughter and their mother be sit at supper , and invite him to join them .
Nothing more be say about work , and when the meal be over they all go to bed .
In the morning , when the young man be dress , the herdsman call to him and say : ` Now listen , and I will tell you what you have to do . '
` What be it ? '
ask the youth , sulkily .
` Nothing less than to look after two hundred pig , ' be the reply .
` Oh , I be use to that , ' answer the youth .
` Yes ; but this time you will have to do it properly , ' say the herdsman ; and he take the youth to the place where the pig be feed , and tell him to drive them to the wood on the side of the mountain .
This the young man do , but as soon a they reach the outskirt of the mountain they grow quite wild , and would have run away altogether , have they not luckily go towards a narrow ravine , from which the youth easily drive them home to his father 's cottage .
` Where do all these pig come from , and how do you get them ? '
ask the old man in surprise , when his son knock at the door of the hut he have leave only the day before .
` They belong to the king 's chief herdsman , ' answer his son .
` He give them to me to look after , but I know I could not do it , so I drive them straight to you .
Now make the best of your good fortune , and kill them and hang them up at once . '
` What be you talk about ? '
cry the father , pale with horror .
` We should certainly both be put to death if I do any such thing . '
` No , no ; do a I tell you , and I will get out of it somehow , ' reply the young man .
And in the end he have his way .
The pig be kill , and laid side by side in a row .
Then he cut off the tail and tie them together with a piece of cord , and swing the bundle over his back , he return to the place where they should have be feed .
Here there be a small swamp , which be just what he want , and find a large stone , he fasten the rope to it , and sink it in the swamp , after which he arrange the tail carefully one by one , so that only their point be see stick out of the water .
When everything be in order , he hasten home to his master with such a sorrowful face that the herdsman saw at once that something dreadful have happen .
` Where be the pig ? '
ask he .
` Oh , do n't speak of them ! '
answer the young man ; ' I really can hardly tell you .
The moment they get into the field they become quite mad , and each ran in a different direction .
I run too , hither and thither , but as fast a I catch one , another be off , till I be in despair .
At last , however , I collect them all and be about to drive them back , when suddenly they rush down the hill into the swamp , where they vanish completely , leave only the point of their tail , which you can see for yourself . '
` You have make up that story very well , ' reply the herdsman .
` No , it be the real truth ; come with me and I 'll prove it . '
And they go together to the spot , and there sure enough be the point of the tail stick up out of the water .
The herdsman lay hold of the near , and pull at it with all his might , but it be no use , for the stone and the rope hold them all fast .
He call to the young man to help him , but the two do not succeed any good than the one have do .
` Yes , your story be true after all ; it be a wonderful thing , ' say the herdsman .
` But I see it be no fault of yours , and I must put up with my loss as well a I can .
Now let u return home , for it be time for supper .
Next morning the herdsman say to the young man : ' I have get some other work for you to do .
To-day you must take a hundred sheep to graze ; but be careful that no harm befall them . ' '
I will do my best , ' reply the youth .
And he open the gate of the fold , where the sheep have be all night , and drive them out into the meadow .
But in a short time they grow as wild a the pig have do , and scatter in all direction .
The young man could not collect them , try a he would , and he think to himself that this be the punishment for his laziness in refuse to look after his father 's one cow .
At last , however , the sheep seem tired of run about , and then the youth manage to gather them together , and drive them , a before , straight to his father 's house .
` Whose sheep be these , and what be they do here ? '
ask the old man in wonder , and his son tell him .
But when the tale be end the father shake his head .
` Give up these bad way and take them back to your master , ' say he .
` No , no , ' answer the youth ; ' I be not so stupid a that !
We will kill them and have them for dinner . '
` You will lose your life if you do , ' reply the father .
` Oh , I be not sure of that ! '
say the son , ` and , anyway , I will have my will for once . '
And he kill all the sheep and lay them on the grass .
But he cut off the head of the ram which always lead the flock and have bell round it horn .
This he take back to the place where they should have be feed , for here he have notice a high rock , with a patch of green grass in the middle and two or three thick bush grow on the edge .
Up this rock he climb with great difficulty , and fasten the ram 's head to the bush with a cord , leave only the tip of the horn with the bell visible .
As there be a soft breeze blowing , the bush to which the head be tie move gently , and the bell rang .
When all be do to his like he hasten quickly back to his master .
` Where be the sheep ? '
ask the herdsman a the young man run pant up the step .
` Oh !
do n't speak of them , ' answer he .
` It be only by a miracle that I be here myself . '
` Tell me at once what have happen , ' say the herdsman sternly .
The youth begin to sob , and stammer out : ` I -- I hardly know how to tell you !
They -- they -- they be so -- so troublesome -- that I could not manage them at all .
They -- run about in -- in all direction , and I -- I -- run after them and nearly die of fatigue .
Then I hear a -- a noise , which I -- I think be the wind .
But -- but -- it be the sheep , which , be -- before my very eyes , be carry straight up -- up into the air .
I stand watch them a if I be turn to stone , but there keep ring in my ear the sound of the bell on the ram which lead them . '
` That be nothing but a lie from begin to end , ' say the herdsman .
` No , it be as true a that there be a sun in heaven , ' answer the young man .
` Then give me a proof of it , ' cry his master .
` Well , come with me , ' say the youth .
By this time it be even and the dusk be fall .
The young man bring the herdsman to the foot of the great rock , but it be so dark you could hardly see .
Still the sound of sheep bell ring softly from above , and the herdsman know them to be those he have hang on the horn of his ram .
` Do you hear ? '
ask the youth .
` Yes , I hear ; you have speak the truth , and I can not blame you for what have happen .
I must bear the loss as best a I can . '
He turn and go home , follow by the young man , who felt highly please with his own cleverness . '
I should not be surprise if the task I set you be too difficult , and that you be tire of them , ' say the herdsman next morning ; ` but to-day I have something quite easy for you to do .
You must look after forty ox , and be sure you be very careful , for one of them have gold-tipped horn and hoof , and the king reckons it among his great treasure . '
The young man drive out the ox into the meadow , and no sooner have they get there than , like the sheep and the pig , they begin to scamper in all direction , the precious bull be the wild of all .
As the youth stand watch them , not know what to do next , it come into his head that his father 's cow be put out to grass at no great distance ; and he forthwith make such a noise that he quite frighten the ox , who be easily persuade to take the path he wish .
When they hear the cow low they gallop all the faster , and soon they all arrive at his father 's house .
The old man be stand before the door of his hut when the great herd of animal dash round a corner of the road , with his son and his own cow at their head .
` Whose cattle be these , and why be they here ? '
he ask ; and his son tell him the story .
` Take them back to your master as soon a you can , ' say the old man ; but the son only laugh , and say : ` No , no ; they be a present to you !
They will make you fat ! '
For a long while the old man refuse to have anything to do with such a wicked scheme ; but his son talk him over in the end , and they kill the ox a they have kill the sheep and the pig .
Last of all they come to the king 's cherished ox .
The son have a rope ready to cast round it horn , and throw it to the ground , but the ox be strong than the rope , and soon tear it in piece .
Then it dash away to the wood , the youth follow ; over hedge and ditch they both go , till they reach the rocky pas which border the herdsman 's land .
Here the ox , think itself safe , stop to rest , and thus give the young man a chance to come up with it .
Not know how to catch it , he collect all the wood he could find and make a circle of fire round the ox , who by this time have fall asleep , and do not wake till the fire have catch it head , and it be too late for it to escape .
Then the young man , who have be watch , run home to his master .
` You have be away a long while , ' say the herdsman .
` Where be the cattle ? '
The young man gasp , and seem a if he be unable to speak .
At last he answer : ` It be always the same story !
The ox be -- go -- go ! '
` G-g-gone ? '
cry the herdsman .
` Scoundrel , you lie ! ' '
I be tell you the exact truth , ' answer the young man .
` Directly we come to the meadow they grow so wild that I could not keep them together .
Then the big ox break away , and the others follow till they all disappear down a deep hole into the earth .
It seem to me that I hear sound of bellowing , and I think I recognise the voice of the golden horned ox ; but when I get to the place from which the sound have come , I could neither see nor hear anything in the hole itself , though there be trace of a fire all round it . '
` Wretch ! '
cry the herdsman , when he have hear this story , ` even if you do not lie before , you be lie now . '
` No , master , I be speak the truth .
Come and see for yourself . '
` If I find you have deceive me , you be a dead man , say the herdsman ; and they go out together .
` What do you call that ? '
ask the youth .
And the herdsman look and saw the trace of a fire , which seem to have spring up from under the earth .
` Wonder upon wonder , ' he exclaim , ` so you really do speak the truth after all !
Well , I can not reproach you , though I shall have to pay heavily to my royal master for the value of that ox .
But come , let u go home !
I will never set you to herd cattle again , henceforward I will give you something easy to do . ' '
I have think of exactly the thing for you , ' say the herdsman a they walk along , ` and it be so simple that you can not make a mistake .
Just make me ten scythe , one for every man , for I want the grass mown in one of my meadow to-morrow . '
At these word the youth 's heart sank , for he have never be train either a a smith or a joiner .
However , he dare not say no , but smile and nod .
Slowly and sadly he go to bed , but he could not sleep , for wonder how the scythe be to be make .
All the skill and cunning he have show before be of no use to him now , and after think about the scythe for many hour , there seem only one way open to him .
So , listen to make sure that all be still , he steal away to his parent , and tell them the whole story .
When they have hear everything , they hide him where no one could find him .
Time pass away , and the young man stay at home do all his parent bid him , and show himself very different from what he have be before he go out to see the world ; but one day he say to his father that he should like to marry , and have a house of his own .
` When I serve the king 's chief herdsman , ' add he , ' I saw his daughter , and I be resolve to try if I can not win her for my wife . '
` It will cost you your life , if you do , ' answer the father , shake his head .
` Well , I will do my best , ' reply his son ; ` but first give me the sword which hang over your bed ! '
The old man do not understand what good the sword would do , however he take it down , and the young man go his way .
Late in the evening he arrive at the house of the herdsman , and knock at the door , which be open by a little boy . '
I want to speak to your master , ' say he .
` So it be you ? '
cry the herdsman , when he have receive the message .
` Well , you can sleep here to-night if you wish . ' '
I have come for something else besides a bed , ' reply the young man , draw his sword , ` and if you do not promise to give me your young daughter a my wife I will stab you through the heart . '
What could the poor man do but promise ?
And he fetch his young daughter , who seem quite pleased at the propose match , and give the youth her hand .
Then the young man go home to his parent , and bid them get ready to welcome his bride .
And when the wedding be over he tell his father-in-law , the herdsman , what he have do with the sheep , and pig , and cattle .
By-and-by the story come to the king 's ear , and he think that a man who be so clever be just the man to govern the country ; so he make him his minister , and after the king himself there be no one so great a he .

Eisenkopf Once upon a time there live an old man who have only one son , whom he love dearly ; but they be very poor , and often have scarcely enough to eat .
Then the old man fell ill , and thing grow bad than ever , so he call his son and say to him : ` My dear boy , I have no long any food to give you , and you must go into the world and get it for yourself .
It do not matter what work you do , but remember if you do it well and be faithful to your master , you will always have your reward . '
So Peter put a piece of black bread in his knapsack , and strap it on his back , take a stout stick in his hand , and set out to seek his fortune .
For a long while he travel on and on , and nobody seem to want him ; but one day he meet an old man , and be a polite youth , he take off his hat and say : ` Good morning , ' in a pleasant voice .
` Good morning , ' answer the old man ; ` and where be you go ? ' '
I be wander through the country try to get work , ' reply Peter .
` Then stay with me , for I can give you plenty , ' say the old man , and Peter stay .
His work do not seem hard , for he have only two horse and a cow to see after , and though he have be hire for a year , the year consist of but three day , so that it be not long before he receive his wage .
In payment the old man give him a nut , and offer to keep him for another year ; but Peter be home-sick ; and , besides , he would rather have be pay ever so small a piece of money than a nut ; for , think he , nuts grow on every tree , and I can gather as many a I like .
However , he do not say this to the old man , who have be kind to him , but just bid him farewell .
The nearer Peter draw to his father 's house the more ashamed he felt at have bring back such poor wage .
What could one nut do for him ?
Why , it would not buy even a slice of bacon .
It be no use take it home , he might as well eat it .
So he sit down on a stone and crack it with his teeth , and then take it out of his mouth to break off the shell .
But who could ever guess what come out of that nut ?
Why , horse and ox and sheep step out in such number that they seem a if they would stretch to the world 's end !
The sight give Peter such a shock that he wring his hand in dismay .
What be he to do with all these creature , where be he to put them ?
He stand and gaze in terror , and at this moment Eisenkopf come by .
` What be the matter , young man ? '
ask he .
` Oh , my friend , there be plenty the matter , ' answer Peter . '
I have gain a nut a my wage , and when I crack it this crowd of beast come out , and I do n't know what to do with them all ! '
` Listen to me , my son , ' say Eisenkopf .
` If you will promise never to marry I will drive them all back into the nut again . '
In his trouble Peter would have promise far hard thing than this , so he gladly give the promise Eisenkopf ask for ; and at a whistle from the stranger the animal all begin crowd into the nut again , nearly tumble over each other in their haste .
When the last foot have get inside , the two half of the shell shut close .
Then Peter put it in his pocket and go on to the house .
No sooner have he reach it than he crack his nut for the second time , and out come the horse , sheep , and oxen again .
Indeed Peter think that there be even more of them than before .
The old man could not believe his eye when he saw the multitude of horse , ox and sheep standing before his door .
` How do you come by all these ? '
he gasp , as soon a he could speak ; and the son tell him the whole story , and of the promise he have give Eisenkopf .
The next day some of the cattle be drive to market and sell , and with the money the old man be able to buy some of the field and garden round his house , and in a few month have grow the rich and most prosperous man in the whole village .
Everything seem to turn to gold in his hand , till one day , when he and his son be sit in the orchard watch their herd of cattle graze in the meadow , he suddenly say : ` Peter , my boy , it be time that you be think of marry . '
` But , my dear father , I tell you I can never marry , because of the promise I give to Eisenkopf . '
` Oh , one promise here and promise there , but no one ever think of keep such promise .
If Eisenkopf do not like your marrying , he will have to put up with it all the same !
Besides , there stand in the stable a grey horse which be saddle night and day ; and if Eisenkopf should show his face , you have only get to jump on the horse 's back and ride away , and nobody on earth can catch you .
When all be safe you will come back again , and we shall live as happily a two fish in the sea . '
And so it all happen .
The young man find a pretty , brown-skinned girl who be willing to have him for a husband , and the whole village come to the wedding feast .
The music be at it gay , and the dance at it merry , when Eisenkopf look in at the window .
` Oh , ho , my brother !
what be go on here ?
It have the air of be a wedding feast .
Yet I fancy -- be I mistaken ?
-- that you have give me a promise that you never would marry . '
But Peter have not wait for the end of this speech .
Scarcely have he see Eisenkopf than he dart like the wind to the stable and flung himself on the horse 's back .
In another moment he be away over the mountain , with Eisenkopf run fast behind him .
On they go through thick forest where the sun never shone , over river so wide that it take a whole day to sail across them , up hill whose side be all of glass ; on they go through seven time seven country till Peter rein in his horse before the house of an old woman .
` Good day , mother , ' say he , jump down and open the door .
` Good day , my son , ' answer she , ` and what be you do here , at the world 's end ? ' '
I be fly for my life , mother , fly to the world which be beyond all world ; for Eisenkopf be at my heel . '
` Come in and rest then , and have some food , for I have a little dog who will begin to howl when Eisenkopf be still seven mile off . '
So Peter go in and warm himself and eat and drink , till suddenly the dog begin to howl .
` Quick , my son , quick , you must go , ' cry the old woman .
And the lightning itself be not quick than Peter .
` Stop a moment , ' cry the old woman again , just a he be mount his horse , ` take this napkin and this cake , and put them in your bag where you can get hold of them easily . '
Peter take them and put them into his bag , and wave his thanks for her kindness , he be off like the wind .
Round and round he ride , through seven time seven country , through forest still thicker , and river still wider , and mountain still more slippery than the others he have pass , till at length he reach a house where dwelt another old woman .
` Good day , mother , ' say he .
` Good day , my son !
What be you seek here at the world 's end ? ' '
I be fly for my life , mother , fly to the world that be beyond all world , for Eisenkopf be at my heel . '
` Come in , my son , and have some food .
I have a little dog who will begin to howl when Eisenkopf be still seven mile off ; so lie on this bed and rest yourself in peace . '
Then she go to the kitchen and bake a number of cake , more than Peter could have eat in a whole month .
He have not finish a quarter of them , when the dog begin to howl .
` Now , my son , you must go , ' cry the old woman ` but first put these cake and this napkin in your bag , where you can easily get at them . '
So Peter thank her and be off like the wind .
On he ride , through seven time seven country , till he come to the house of a third old woman , who welcome him a the others have do .
But when the dog howl , and Peter spring up to go , she say , a she give him the same gift for his journey : ` You have now three cake and three napkin , for I know that my sister have each give you one .
Listen to me , and do what I tell you .
Ride seven day and night straight before you , and on the eighth morning you will see a great fire .
Strike it three time with the three napkin and it will part in two .
Then ride into the opening , and when you be in the middle of the opening , throw the three cake behind your back with your left hand . '
Peter thank her for her counsel , and be careful to do exactly all the old woman have tell him .
On the eighth morning he reach a fire so large that he could see nothing else on either side , but when he strike it with the napkin it part , and stand on each hand like a wall .
As he ride through the opening he throw the cake behind him .
From each cake there spring a huge dog , and he give them the name of World 's - weight , Ironstrong , and Quick-ear .
They bay with joy at the sight of him , and a Peter turn to pat them , he behold Eisenkopf at the edge of the fire , but the opening have close up behind Peter , and he could not get through .
` Stop , you promise-breaker , ' shriek he ; ` you have slip through my hand once , but wait till I catch you again ! '
Then he lay down by the fire and watch to see what would happen .
When Peter know that he have nothing more to fear from Eisenkopf , he ride on slowly till he come to a small white house .
Here he enter and find himself in a room where a gray-haired woman be spin and a beautiful girl be sit in the window comb her golden hair .
` What bring you here , my son ? '
ask the old woman . '
I be seek for a place , mother , ' answer Peter .
` Stay with me , then , for I need a servant , ' say the old woman .
` With pleasure , mother , ' reply he .
After that Peter 's life be a very happy one .
He sow and plough all day , except now and then when he take his dog and go to hunt .
And whatever game he bring back the maiden with the golden hair know how to dress it .
One day the old woman have go to the town to buy some flour , and Peter and the maiden be leave alone in the house .
They fell into talk , and she ask him where his home be , and how he have manage to come through the fire .
Peter then tell her the whole story , and of his strike the flame with the three napkin a he have be tell to do .
The maiden listen attentively and wonder in herself whether what he say be true .
So after Peter have go out to the field , she creep up to his room and steal the napkin and then set off as fast a she could to the fire by a path she know of over the hill .
At the third blow she give the flame divide , and Eisenkopf , who have be watch and hop for a chance of this kind , run down the opening and stood before her .
At this sight the maiden be almost frighten to death , but with a great effort she recover herself and run home as fast a her leg would carry her , closely pursue by Eisenkopf .
Panting for breath she rush into the house and fell faint on the floor ; but Eisenkopf enter behind her , and hid himself in the kitchen under the hearth .
Not long after , Peter come in and pick up the three napkin which the maiden have drop on the threshold .
He wonder how they get there , for he know he have leave them in his room ; but what be his horror when he saw the form of the fainting girl lie where she have drop , a still and white a if she have be dead .
He lift her up and carry her to her bed , where she soon revive , but she do not tell Peter about Eisenkopf , who have be almost crush to death under the hearth-stone by the body of World 's - weight .
The next morning Peter lock up his dog and go out into the forest alone .
Eisenkopf , however , have see him go , and follow so closely at his heel that Peter have barely time to clamber up a tall tree , where Eisenkopf could not reach him .
` Come down at once , you gallows bird , ' he cry .
` Have you forget your promise that you never would marry ? '
` Oh , I know it be all up with me , ' answer Peter , ` but let me call out three time . '
` You can call a hundred time if you like , ' return Eisenkopf , ` for now I have get you in my power , and you shall pay for what you have do . '
` Iron-strong , World 's - weight , Quick-ear , fly to my help ! '
cried Peter ; and Quick-ear heard , and say to his brother : ` Listen , our master be call u . '
` You be dream , fool , ' answer World 's - weight ; ` why he have not finish his breakfast . '
And he give Quick-ear a slap with his paw , for he be young and need to be taught sense .
` Iron-strong , World 's - weight , Quick-ear , fly to my help ! '
cry Peter again .
This time World 's - weight heard also , and he say , ` Ah , now our master be really call . '
` How silly you be ! '
answered Iron-strong ; ` you know that at this hour he be always eat . '
And he give World 's - weight a cuff , because he be old enough to know good .
Peter sit tremble on the tree dread l his dog have never hear , or else that , have hear , they have refuse to come .

The Death Of Abu Nowas And Of His Wife Once upon a time there live a man whose name be Abu Nowas , and he be a great favourite with the Sultan of the country , who have a palace in the same town where Abu Nowas dwelt .
One day Abu Nowas come weep into the hall of the palace where the Sultan be sit , and say to him : ` Oh , mighty Sultan , my wife be dead . '
` That be bad news , ' reply the Sultan ; ' I must get you another wife . '
And he bid his Grand Vizir send for the Sultana .
` This poor Abu Nowas have lose his wife , ' say he , when she enter the hall .

I have get a husband for you , ' say the Sultana .

Motiratika Once upon a time , in a very hot country , a man live with his wife in a little hut , which be surround by grass and flower .
They be perfectly happy together till , by-and-by , the woman fell ill and refuse to take any food .
The husband try to persuade her to eat all sort of delicious fruit that he have find in the forest , but she would have none of them , and grow so thin he fear she would die .
` Is there nothing you would like ? '
he say at last in despair .
` Yes , I think I could eat some wild honey , ' answer she .
The husband be overjoy , for he think this sounded easy enough to get , and he go off at once in search of it .
He come back with a wooden pan quite full , and give it to his wife . '
I ca n't eat that , ' she say , turn away in disgust .
` Look !
there be some dead bee in it !
I want honey that be quite pure . '
And the man throw the reject honey on the grass , and start off to get some fresh .
When he get back he offer it to his wife , who treat it a she have do the first bowlful .
` That honey have get ant in it : throw it away , ' she say , and when he bring her some more , she declare it be full of earth .
In his fourth journey he manage to find some that she would eat , and then she beg him to get her some water .
This take him some time , but at length he come to a lake whose water be sweeten with sugar .
He fill a pannikin quite full , and carry it home to his wife , who drink it eagerly , and say that she now felt quite well .
When she be up and have dress herself , her husband lay down in her place , say : ` You have give me a great deal of trouble , and now it be my turn ! '
` What be the matter with you ? '
ask the wife . '
I be thirsty and want some water , ' answer he ; and she take a large pot and carry it to the near spring , which be a good way off .
` Here be the water , ' she say to her husband , lift the heavy pot from her head ; but he turn away in disgust .
` You have draw it from the pool that be full of frog and willow ; you must get me some more . '
So the woman set out again and walk still further to another lake .
` This water taste of rush , ' he exclaim , ` go and get some fresh . '
But when she bring back a third supply he declare that it seem make up of water-lilies , and that he must have water that be pure , and not spoil by willow , or frog , or rush .
So for the fourth time she put her jug on her head , and pass all the lake she have hitherto try , she come to another , where the water be golden like honey .
She stoop down to drink , when a horrible head bob up on the surface .
` How dare you steal my water ? '
cry the head .
` It be my husband who have send me , ' she reply , tremble all over .
` But do not kill me !
You shall have my baby , if you will only let me go . '
` How be I to know which be your baby ? '
ask the Ogre .
` Oh , that be easily manage .
I will shave both side of his head , and hang some white bead round his neck .
And when you come to the hut you have only to call `` Motikatika ! ''
and he will run to meet you , and you can eat him . '
` Very well , ' say the ogre , ` you can go home . '
And after fill the pot she return , and tell her husband of the dreadful danger she have be in .
Now , though his mother do not know it , the baby be a magician and he have hear all that his mother have promise the ogre ; and he laugh to himself a he plan how to outwit her .
The next morning she shave his head on both side , and hang the white bead round his neck , and say to him : ' I be go to the field to work , but you must stay at home .
Be sure you do not go outside , or some wild beast may eat you . '
` Very well , ' answer he .
As soon a his mother be out of sight , the baby take out some magic bone , and place them in a row before him .
` You be my father , ' he tell one bone , ` and you be my mother .
You be the big , ' he say to the third , ` so you shall be the ogre who want to eat me ; and you , ' to another , ` be very little , therefore you shall be me .
Now , then , tell me what I be to do . '
` Collect all the baby in the village the same size a yourself , ' answer the bone ; ` shave the side of their head , and hang white bead round their neck , and tell them that when anybody call `` Motikatika , '' they be to answer to it .
And be quick for you have no time to lose . '
Motikatika go out directly , and bring back quite a crowd of baby , and shave their head and hung white bead round their little black neck , and just a he have finish , the ground begin to shake , and the huge ogre come stride along , cry : ` Motikatika !
Motikatika ! '
` Here we be !
here we be ! '
answer the baby , all run to meet him .
` It be Motikatika I want , ' say the ogre .
` We be all Motikatika , ' they reply .
And the ogre sit down in bewilderment , for he dare not eat the child of people who have do him no wrong , or a heavy punishment would befall him .
The child wait for a little , wonder , and then they go away .
The ogre remain where he be , till the evening , when the woman return from the field . '
I have not see Motikatika , ' say he .
` But why do you not call him by his name , a I tell you ? '
she ask . '
I do , but all the baby in the village seem to be name Motikatika , ' answer the ogre ; ` you can not think the number who come run to me . '
The woman do not know what to make of it , so , to keep him in a good temper , she enter the hut and prepare a bowl of maize , which she bring him . '
I do not want maize , I want the baby , ' grumble he ` and I will have him . '
` Have patience , ' answer she ; ' I will call him , and you can eat him at once . '
And she go into the hut and cry , ` Motikatika ! ' '
I be come , mother , ' reply he ; but first he take out his bone , and , crouch down on the ground behind the hut , ask them how he should escape the ogre .
` Change yourself into a mouse , ' say the bone ; and so he do , and the ogre grow tired of wait , and tell the woman she must invent some other plan .
` To-morrow I will send him into the field to pick some bean for me , and you will find him there , and can eat him . '
` Very well , ' reply the ogre , ` and this time I will take care to have him , ' and he go back to his lake .
Next morning Motikatika be send out with a basket , and tell to pick some bean for dinner .
On the way to the field he take out his bone and ask them what he be to do to escape from the ogre .
` Change yourself into a bird and snap off the bean , ' say the bone .
And the ogre chase away the bird , not know that it be Motikatika .
The ogre go back to the hut and tell the woman that she have deceive him again , and that he would not be put off any long .
` Return here this evening , ' answer she , ` and you will find him in bed under this white coverlet .
Then you can carry him away , and eat him at once . '
But the boy heard , and consult his bone , which say : ` Take the red coverlet from your father 's bed , and put yours on his , ' and so he do .
And when the ogre come , he seize Motikatika 's father and carry him outside the hut and eat him .
When his wife find out the mistake , she cry bitterly ; but Motikatika say : ` It be only just that he should be eat , and not I ; for it be he , and not I , who send you to fetch the water . '

Niels And The Giants On one of the great moor over in Jutland , where tree wo n't grow because the soil be so sandy and the wind so strong , there once live a man and his wife , who have a little house and some sheep , and two son who help them to herd them .
The elder of the two be call Rasmus , and the young Niels .
Rasmus be quite content to look after sheep , a his father have do before him , but Niels have a fancy to be a hunter , and be not happy till he get hold of a gun and learn to shoot .
It be only an old muzzle-loading flint-lock after all , but Niels think it a great prize , and go about shoot at everything he could see .
So much do he practice that in the long run he become a wonderful shot , and be hear of even where he have never be see .
Some people say there be very little in him beyond this , but that be an idea they find reason to change in the course of time .
The parent of Rasmus and Niels be good Catholics , and when they be get old the mother take it into her head that she would like to go to Rome and see the Pope .
The others do n't see much use in this , but she have her way in the end : they sell all the sheep , shut up the house , and set out for Rome on foot .
Niels take his gun with him .
` What do you want with that ? '
say Rasmus ; ` we have plenty to carry without it . '
But Niels could not be happy without his gun , and take it all the same .
It be in the hot part of summer that they begin their journey , so hot that they could not travel at all in the middle of the day , and they be afraid to do it by night l they might lose their way or fall into the hand of robber .
One day , a little before sunset , they come to an inn which lay at the edge of a forest .
` We have well stay here for the night , ' say Rasmus .
` What an idea ! '
say Niels , who be grow impatient at the slow progress they be make .
` We ca n't travel by day for the heat , and we remain where we be all night .
It will be long enough before we get to Rome if we go on at this rate . '
Rasmus be unwilling to go on , but the two old people side with Niels , who say , ` The night be n't dark , and the moon will soon be up .
We can ask at the inn here , and find out which way we ought to take . '
So they hold on for some time , but at last they come to a small opening in the forest , and here they find that the road split in two .
There be no sign-post to direct them , and the people in the inn have not tell them which of the two road to take .
` What 's to be do now ? '
say Rasmus . '
I think we have well have stay at the inn . '
` There 's no harm do , ' say Niels .
` The night be warm , and we can wait here till morning .
One of u will keep watch till midnight , and then waken the other . '
Rasmus choose to take the first watch , and the others lay down to sleep .
It be very quiet in the forest , and Rasmus could hear the deer and fox and other animal move about among the rustle leaf .
After the moon rise he could see them occasionally , and when a big stag come quite close to him he get hold of Niels ' gun and shot it .
Niels be waken by the report .
` What 's that ? '
he say .
` I 've just shoot a stag , ' say Rasmus , highly pleased with himself .
` That 's nothing , ' say Niels .
` I 've often shoot a sparrow , which be a much more difficult thing to do . '
It be now close on midnight , so Niels begin his watch , and Rasmus go to sleep .
It begin to get colder , and Niels begin to walk about a little to keep himself warm .
He soon find that they be not far from the edge of the forest , and when he climb up one of the tree there he could see out over the open country beyond .
At a little distance he saw a fire , and beside it there sit three giant , busy with broth and beef .
They be so huge that the spoon they use be as large a spade , and their fork as big a hay-forks : with these they lift whole bucketful of broth and great joint of meat out of an enormous pot which be set on the ground between them .
Niels be startle and rather scar at first , but he comfort himself with the thought that the giant be a good way off , and that if they come nearer he could easily hide among the bush .
After watch them for a little , however , he begin to get over his alarm , and finally slide down the tree again , resolve to get his gun and play some trick with them .
When he have climb back to his former position , he take good aim , and wait till one of the giant be just in the act of put a large piece of meat into his mouth .
Bang !
go Niels ' gun , and the bullet strike the handle of the fork so hard that the point go into the giant 's chin , instead of his mouth .
` None of your trick , ' growl the giant to the one who sit next him .
` What do you mean by hit my fork like that , and make me prick myself ? ' '
I never touch your fork , ' say the other .
` Do n't try to get up a quarrel with me . '
` Look at it , then , ' say the first .
` Do you suppose I stick it into my own chin for fun ? '
The two get so angry over the matter that each offer to fight the other there and then , but the third giant act a peace-maker , and they again fell to their eating .
While the quarrel be go on , Niels have load the gun again , and just a the second giant be about to put a nice tit-bit into his mouth , bang !
go the gun again , and the fork fly into a dozen piece .
This giant be even more furious than the first have be , and word be just come to blow , when the third giant again interpose .
` Do n't be fools , ' he say to them ; ` what 's the good of begin to fight among ourselves , when it be so necessary for the three of u to work together and get the upper hand over the king of this country .
It will be a hard enough task a it be , but it will be altogether hopeless if we do n't stick together .
Sit down again , and let u finish our meal ; I shall sit between you , and then neither of you can blame the other . '
Niels be too far away to hear their talk , but from their gesture he could guess what be happen , and think it good fun .
` Thrice be lucky , ' say he to himself ; ` I 'll have another shot yet . '
This time it be the third giant 's fork that catch the bullet , and snap in two .
` Well , ' say he , ` if I be as foolish a you two , I would also fly into a rage , but I begin to see what time of day it be , and I 'm go off this minute to see who it be that 's play these trick with u . '
So well have the giant make his observation , that though Niels climb down the tree a fast a he could , so a to hide among the bush , he have just get to the ground when the enemy be upon him .
` Stay where you be , ' say the giant , ` or I 'll put my foot on you , and there wo n't be much of you leave after that . '
Niels give in , and the giant carry him back to his comrade .
` You do n't deserve any mercy at our hand , ' say his captor ` but a you be such a good shot you may be of great use to u , so we shall spare your life , if you will do u a service .
Not far from here there stand a castle , in which the king 's daughter live ; we be at war with the king , and want to get the upper hand of him by carry off the princess , but the castle be so well guard that there be no get into it .
By our skill in magic we have cast sleep on every live thing in the castle , except a little black dog , and , as long a he be awake , we be no good off than before ; for , as soon a we begin to climb over the wall , the little dog will hear u , and it barking will waken all the others again .
Having get you , we can place you where you will be able to shoot the dog before it begin to bark , and then no one can hinder u from get the princess into our hand .
If you do that , we shall not only let you off , but reward you handsomely . '
Niels have to consent , and the giant set out for the castle at once .
It be surround by a very high rampart , so high that even the giant could not touch the top of it .
` How be I to get over that ? '
say Niels .
` Quite easily , ' say the third giant ; ` I 'll throw you up on it . '
` No , thanks , ' say Niels . '
I might fall down on the other side , or break my leg or neck , and then the little dog would n't get shoot after all . '
` No fear of that , ' say the giant ; ` the rampart be quite wide on the top , and cover with long grass , so that you will come down as softly a though you fell on a feather-bed . '
Niels have to believe him , and allow the giant to throw him up .
He come down on his foot quite unhurt , but the little black dog hear the dump , and rush out of it kennel at once .
It be just open it mouth to bark , when Niels fire , and it fell dead on the spot .
` Go down on the inside now , ' say the giant , ` and see if you can open the gate to u . '
Niels make his way down into the courtyard , but on his way to the outer gate he find himself at the entrance to the large hall of the castle .
The door be open , and the hall be brilliantly light , though there be no one to be see .
Niels go in here and look round him : on the wall there hang a huge sword without a sheath , and beneath it be a large drinking-horn , mount with silver .
Niels go close to look at these , and saw that the horn have letter engrave on the silver rim : when he take it down and turn it round , he find that the inscription be : -- Whoever drink the wine I hold Can wield the sword that hang above ; Then let him use it for the right , And win a royal maiden 's love .
Niels take out the silver stopper of the horn , and drink some of the wine , but when he try to take down the sword he find himself unable to move it .
So he hang up the horn again , and go far in to the castle .
` The giant can wait a little , ' he say .
Before long he come to an apartment in which a beautiful princess lay asleep in a bed , and on a table by her side there lay a gold-hemmed handkerchief .
Niels tear this in two , and put one half in his pocket , leave the other half on the table .
On the floor he saw a pair of gold-embroidered slipper , and one of these he also put in his pocket .
After that he go back to the hall , and take down the horn again .
` Perhaps I have to drink all that be in it before I can move the sword , ' he think ; so he put it to his lip again and drink till it be quite empty .
When he have do this , he could wield the sword with the great of ease , and felt himself strong enough to do anything , even to fight the giant he have leave outside , who be no doubt wonder why he have not open the gate to them before this time .
To kill the giant , he think , would be use the sword for the right ; but a to win the love of the princess , that be a thing which the son of a poor sheep-farmer need not hope for .
When Niels come to the gate of the castle , he find that there be a large door and a small one , so he open the latter .
` Ca n't you open the big door ? '
say the giant ; ` we shall hardly be able to get in at this one . '
` The bar be too heavy for me to draw , ' say Niels ; ` if you stoop a little you can quite well come in here . '

Shepherd Paul Once upon a time a shepherd be take his flock out to pasture , when he find a little baby lie in a meadow , leave there by some wicked person , who think it be too much trouble to look after it .
The shepherd be fond of child , so he take the baby home with him and give it plenty of milk , and by the time the boy be fourteen he could tear up oaks a if they be weed .
Then Paul , a the shepherd have call him , grow tire of living at home , and go out into the world to try his luck .
He walk on for many mile , see nothing that surprise him , but in an open space of the wood he be astonish at find a man comb tree a another man would comb flax .
` Good morning , friend , ' say Paul ; ` upon my word , you must be a strong man ! '
The man stop his work and laugh . '
I be Tree Comber , ' he answer proudly ; ` and the great wish of my life be to wrestle with Shepherd Paul . '
` May all your wish be fulfil a easily , for I be Shepherd Paul , and can wrestle with you at once , ' reply the lad ; and he seize Tree Comber and fling him with such force to the ground that he sink up to his knee in the earth .
However , in a moment he be up again , and catch hold of Paul , throw him so that he sink up to his waist ; but then it be Paul 's turn again , and this time the man be bury up to his neck .
` That be enough , ' cry he ; ' I see you be a smart fellow , let u become friend . '
` Very good , ' answer Paul , and they continue their journey together .
By-and-by they reach a man who be grind stone to powder in his hand , a if they have be nut .
` Good morning , ' say Paul politely ; ` upon my word , you must be a strong fellow ! ' '
I be Stone Crusher , ' answer the man , and the great wish of my life be to wrestle with Shepherd Paul . '
` May all your wish be a easily fulfil , for I be Shepherd Paul , and will wrestle with you at once , ' and the sport begin .
After a short time the man declare himself beat , and beg leave to go with them ; so they all three travel together .
A little further on they come upon a man who be knead iron a if it have be dough .
` Good morning , ' say Paul , ` you must be a strong fellow . ' '
I be Iron Kneader , and should like to fight Shepherd Paul , ' answer he .
` Let u begin at once then , ' reply Paul ; and on this occasion also , Paul get the good of his foe , and they all four continue their journey .
At midday they enter a forest , and Paul stop suddenly .
` We three will go and look for game , ' he say , ` and you , Tree Comber , will stay behind and prepare a good supper for u . '
So Tree Comber set to work to boil and roast , and when dinner be nearly ready , a little dwarf with a pointed beard stroll up to the place .
` What be you cook ? '
ask he , ` give me some of it . '
` I 'll give you some on your back , if you like , ' answer Tree Comber rudely .
The dwarf take no notice , but wait patiently till the dinner be cook , then suddenly throw Tree Comber on the ground , he eat up the content of the saucepan and vanish .
Tree Comber felt rather ashamed of himself , and set about boil some more vegetable , but they be still very hard when the hunter return , and though they complain of his bad cooking , he do not tell them about the dwarf .
Next day Stone Crusher be leave behind , and after him Iron Kneader , and each time the dwarf appear , and they fare no good than Tree Comber have do .
The fourth day Paul say to them : ` My friend , there must be some reason why your cooking have always be so bad , now you shall go and hunt and I will stay behind . '
So they go off , amuse themselves by think what be in store for Paul .
He set to work at once , and have just get all his vegetable simmer in the pot when the dwarf appear a before , and ask to have some of the stew .
` Be off , ' cry Paul , snatch up the saucepan a he speak .
The dwarf try to get hold of his collar , but Paul seize him by the beard , and tie him to a big tree so that he could not stir , and go on quietly with his cooking .
The hunter come back early , long to see how Paul have get on , and , to their surprise , dinner be quite ready for them .
` You be great useless creature , ' say he , ` who could n't even outwit that little dwarf .
When we have finish supper I will show you what I have do with him ! '
But when they reach the place where Paul have leave the dwarf , neither he nor the tree be to be see , for the little fellow have pull it up by the root and run away , drag it after him .
The four friend follow the track of the tree and find that it end in a deep hole .
` He must have go down here , ' say Paul , ` and I will go after him .
See !
there be a basket that will do for me to sit in , and a cord to lower me with .
But when I pull the cord again , lose no time in draw the basket up . '
And he step into the basket , which be lower by his friend .
At last it touch the ground and he jump out and look about him .
He be in a beautiful valley , full of meadow and stream , with a splendid castle standing by .
As the door be open he walk in , but a lovely maiden meet him and implore him to go back , for the owner of the castle be a dragon with six head , who have steal her from her home and bring her down to this underground spot .
But Paul refuse to listen to all her entreaty , and declare that he be not afraid of the dragon , and do not care how many head he have ; and he sit down calmly to wait for him .
In a little while the dragon come in , and all the long teeth in his six head chatter with anger at the sight of the stranger . '
I be Shepherd Paul , ' say the young man , ` and I have come to fight you , and a I be in a hurry we have well begin at once . '
` Very good , ' answer the dragon . '
I be sure of my supper , but let u have a mouthful of something first , just to give u an appetite . '
Whereupon he begin to eat some huge boulder a if they have be cake , and when he have quite finish , he offer Paul one .
Paul be not fond of boulder , but he take a wooden knife and cut one in two , then he snatch up both half in his hand and throw them with all his strength at the dragon , so that two out of the six head be smash in .
At this the dragon , with a mighty roar , rush upon Paul , but he spring on one side , and with a swing blow cut off two of the other head .
Then , seize the monster by the neck , he dash the remain head against the rock .
When the maiden heard that the dragon be dead , she thank her deliverer with tear in her eye , but tell him that her two young sister be in the power of dragon still fiercer and more horrible than this one .
He vow that his sword should never rest in it sheath till they be set free , and bid the girl come with him , and show him the way .
The maiden gladly consent to go with him , but first she give him a golden rod , and bid him strike the castle with it .
He do so , and it instantly change into a golden apple , which he put in his pocket .
After that , they start on their search .
They have not go far before they reach the castle where the second girl be confine by the power of the dragon with twelve head , who have steal her from her home .
She be overjoy at the sight of her sister and of Paul , and bring him a shirt belonging to the dragon , which make every one who wear it twice as strong a they be before .
Scarcely have he put it on when the dragon come back , and the fight begin .
Long and hard be the struggle , but Paul 's sword and his shirt help him , and the twelve head lay dead upon the ground .
Then Paul change the castle into an apple , which he put into his pocket , and set out with the two girl in search of the third castle .
It be not long before they find it , and within the wall be the third sister , who be young and pretty than either of the other two .
Her husband have eighteen head , but when he quit the low region for the surface of the earth , he leave them all at home except one , which he change for the head of a little dwarf , with a pointed beard .
The moment that Paul know that this terrible dragon be no other than the dwarf whom he have tie to the tree , he long more than ever to fly at his throat .
But the thought of the eighteen head warn him to be careful , and the third sister bring him a silk shirt which would make him ten time strong than he be before .
He have scarcely put it on , when the whole castle begin to shake violently , and the dragon fly up the step into the hall .
` Well , my friend , so we meet once more !
Have you forget me ?
I be Shepherd Paul , and I have come to wrestle with you , and to free your wife from your clutch . '
` Ah , I be glad to see you again , ' say the dragon .
` Those be my two brother whom you kill , and now your blood shall pay for them . '
And he go into his room to look for his shirt and to drink some magic wine , but the shirt be on Paul 's back , and a for the wine , the girl have give a cupful to Paul and then have allow the rest to run out of the cask .
At this the dragon grow rather frightened , but in a moment have recollect his eighteen head , and be bold again .
` Come on , ' he cry , rear himself up and prepare to dart all his head at once at Paul .
But Paul jump underneath , and give an upward cut so that six of the head go roll down .
They be the best head too , and very soon the other twelve lay beside them .
Then Paul change the castle into an apple , and put it in his pocket .
Afterwards he and the three girl set off for the opening which lead upwards to the earth .
The basket be still there , dangle from the rope , but it be only big enough to hold the three girl , so Paul send them up , and tell them to be sure and let down the basket for him .
Unluckily , at the sight of the maiden ' beauty , so far beyond anything they have ever see , the friend forget all about Paul , and carry the girl straight away into a far country , so that they be not much good off than before .
Meanwhile Paul , mad with rage at the ingratitude of the three sister , vow he would be revenge upon them , and set about find some way of get back to earth .
But it be not very easy , and for month , and month , and month , he wander about underground , and , at the end , seem no nearer to fulfil his purpose than he be at the beginning .
At length , one day , he happen to pass the nest of a huge griffin , who have leave her young one all alone .
Just a Paul come along a cloud contain fire instead of rain burst overhead , and all the little griffin would certainly have be kill have not Paul spread his cloak over the nest and save them .
When their father return the young one tell him what Paul have do , and he lose no time in fly after Paul , and ask how he could reward him for his goodness .
` By carry me up to the earth , ' answered Paul ; and the griffin agree , but first go to get some food to eat on the way , a it be a long journey .
` Now get on my back , ' he say to Paul , ` and when I turn my head to the right , cut a slice off the bullock that hang on that side , and put it in my mouth , and when I turn my head to the left , draw a cupful of wine from the cask that hang on that side , and pour it down my throat . '
For three day and three night Paul and the griffin fly upwards , and on the fourth morning it touch the ground just outside the city where Paul 's friend have go to live .
Then Paul thank him and bid him farewell , and he return home again .
At first Paul be too tired to do anything but sleep , but as soon a he be rest he start off in search of the three faithless one , who almost die from fright at the sight of him , for they have think he would never come back to reproach them for their wickedness .
` You know what to expect , ' Paul say to them quietly .
` You shall never see me again .
Off with you ! '
He next take the three apple out of his pocket and place them all in the prettiest place he could find ; after which he tap them with his golden rod , and they become castle again .
He give two of the castle to the eldest sister , and keep the other for himself and the young , whom he marry , and there they be live still .

How The Wicked Tanuki Was Punished The hunter have hunt the wood for so many year that no wild animal be any more to be find in it .
You might walk from one end to the other without ever see a hare , or a deer , or a boar , or hear the cooing of the dove in their nest .
If they be not dead , they have fly elsewhere .
Only three creature remain alive , and they have hide themselves in the thick part of the forest , high up the mountain .
These be a grey-furred , long-tailed tanuki , his wife the fox , who be one of his own family , and their little son .
The fox and the tanuki be very clever , prudent beast , and they also be skilled in magic , and by this mean have escape the fate of their unfortunate friend .
If they hear the twang of an arrow or saw the glitter of a spear , ever so far off , they lay very still , and be not to be tempt from their hiding-place , if their hunger be ever so great , or the game ever so delicious .
` We be not so foolish a to risk our life , ' they say to each other proudly .
But at length there come a day when , in spite of their prudence , they seem likely to die of starvation , for no more food be to be have .
Something have to be do , but they do not know what .
Suddenly a bright thought strike the tanuki . '
I have get a plan , ' he cry joyfully to his wife . '
I will pretend to be dead , and you must change yourself into a man , and take me to the village for sale .
It will be easy to find a buyer , tanukis ' skin be always want ; then buy some food with the money and come home again .
I will manage to escape somehow , so do not worry about me . '
The fox laugh with delight , and rub her paw together with satisfaction .
` Well , next time I will go , ' she say , ` and you can sell me . '
And then she change herself into a man , and pick up the stiff body of the tanuki , set off towards the village .
She find him rather heavy , but it would never have do to let him walk through the wood and risk his be see by somebody .
As the tanaki have foretell , buyer be many , and the fox hand him over to the person who offer the large price , and hurry to get some food with the money .
The buyer take the tanuki back to his house , and throw him into a corner go out .
Directly the tanaki find he be alone , he creep cautiously through a chink of the window , think , a he do so , how lucky it be that he be not a fox , and be able to climb .
Once outside , he hide himself in a ditch till it grow dusk , and then gallop away into the forest .
While the food last they be all three as happy a king ; but there soon arrive a day when the larder be as empty a ever .
` It be my turn now to pretend to be dead , ' cry the fox .
So the tanuki change himself into a peasant , and start for the village , with his wife 's body hanging over his shoulder .
A buyer be not long in come forward , and while they be make the bargain a wicked thought dart into the tanuki 's head , that if he get rid of the fox there would be more food for him and his son .
So a he put the money in his pocket he whisper softly to the buyer that the fox be not really dead , and that if he do not take care she might run away from him .
The man do not need twice tell .
He give the poor fox a blow on the head , which put an end to her , and the wicked tanuki go smile to the near shop .
In former time he have be very fond of his little son ; but since he have betray his wife he seem to have change all in a moment , for he would not give him as much a a bite , and the poor little fellow would have starve have he not find some nut and berry to eat , and he wait on , always hop that his mother would come back .
At length some notion of the truth begin to dawn on him ; but he be careful to let the old tanuki see nothing , though in his own mind he turn over plan from morning till night , wonder how best he might avenge his mother .
One morning , a the little tanuki be sit with his father , he remember , with a start , that his mother have teach him all she know of magic , and that he could work spell as well a his father , or perhaps well . '
I be as good a wizard a you , ' he say suddenly , and a cold chill run through the tanuki a he hear him , though he laugh , and pretend to think it a joke .
But the little tanaki stick to his point , and at last the father propose they should have a wager .
` Change yourself into any shape you like , ' say he , ` and I will undertake to know you .
I will go and wait on the bridge which lead over the river to the village , and you shall transform yourself into anything you please , but I will know you through any disguise . '
The little tanuki agree , and go down the road which his father have point out .
But instead of transform himself into a different shape , he just hide himself in a corner of the bridge , where he could see without be see .
He have not be there long when his father arrive and take up his place near the middle of the bridge , and soon after the king come by , follow by a troop of guard and all his court .
` Ah !
he think that now he have change himself into a king I shall not know him , ' think the old tanuki , and a the king pass in his splendid carriage , borne by his servant , he jump upon it cry : ' I have win my wager ; you can not deceive me . '
But in reality it be he who have deceive himself .
The soldier , conceive that their king be be attack , seize the tanuki by the leg and fling him over into the river , and the water close over him .
And the little tanoki saw it all , and rejoice that his mother 's death have be avenge .
Then he go back to the forest , and if he have not find it too lonely , he be probably live there still .

The Crab And The Monkey There be once a crab who live in a hole on the shady side of a mountain .
She be a very good housewife , and so careful and industrious that there be no creature in the whole country whose hole be so neat and clean a hers , and she take great pride in it .
One day she saw lie near the mouth of her hole a handful of cooked rice which some pilgrim must have let fall when he be stop to eat his dinner .
Delighted at this discovery , she hasten to the spot , and be carry the rice back to her hole when a monkey , who live in some tree near by , come down to see what the crab be do .
His eye shone at the sight of the rice , for it be his favourite food , and like the sly fellow he be , he propose a bargain to the crab .
She be to give him half the rice in exchange for the kernel of a sweet red kaki fruit which he have just eat .
He half expect that the crab would laugh in his face at this impudent proposal , but instead of do so she only look at him for a moment with her head on one side and then say that she would agree to the exchange .
So the monkey go off with his rice , and the crab return to her hole with the kernel .
For some time the crab saw no more of the monkey , who have go to pay a visit on the sunny side of the mountain ; but one morning he happen to pass by her hole , and find her sit under the shadow of a beautiful kaki tree .
` Good day , ' he say politely , ` you have some very fine fruit there !
I be very hungry , could you spare me one or two ? '
` Oh , certainly , ' reply the crab , ` but you must forgive me if I can not get them for you myself .
I be no tree-climber . '
` Pray do not apologise , ' answer the monkey .
` Now that I have your permission I can get them myself quite easily . '
And the crab consent to let him go up , merely say that he must throw her down half the fruit .
In another moment he be swing himself from branch to branch , eat all the ripe kaki and fill his pocket with the rest , and the poor crab saw to her disgust that the few he throw down to her be either not ripe at all or else quite rotten .
` You be a shock rogue , ' she call in a rage ; but the monkey take no notice , and go on eating as fast a he could .
The crab understood that it be no use her scolding , so she resolve to try what cunning would do .
` Sir Monkey , ' she say , ` you be certainly a very good climber , but now that you have eat so much , I be quite sure you would never be able to turn one of your somersault . '
The monkey pride himself on turn good somersault than any of his family , so he instantly go head over heel three time on the bough on which he be sit , and all the beautiful kaki that he have in his pocket roll to the ground .
Quick a lightning the crab pick them up and carry a quantity of them into her house , but when she come up for another the monkey sprang on her , and treat her so badly that he leave her for dead .
When he have beat her till his arm ache he go his way .
It be a lucky thing for the poor crab that she have some friend to come to her help or she certainly would have die then and there .
The wasp fly to her , and take her back to bed and look after her , and then he consult with a rice-mortar and an egg which have fall out of a nest near by , and they agree that when the monkey return , a he be sure to do , to steal the rest of the fruit , that they would punish him severely for the manner in which he have behave to the crab .
So the mortar climb up to the beam over the front door , and the egg lay quite still on the ground , while the wasp set down the water-bucket in a corner .
Then the crab dig itself a deep hole in the ground , so that not even the tip of her claw might be see .
Soon after everything be ready the monkey jump down from his tree , and creep to the door begin a long hypocritical speech , ask pardon for all he have do .
He wait for an answer of some sort , but none come .
He listen , but all be still ; then he peep , and saw no one ; then he go in .
He peer about for the crab , but in vain ; however , his eye fell on the egg , which he snatch up and set on the fire .
But in a moment the egg have burst into a thousand piece , and it sharp shell strike him in the face and scratch him horribly .
Smarting with pain he run to the bucket and stoop down to throw some water over his head .
As he stretch out his hand up start the wasp and sting him on the nose .
The monkey shriek and run to the door , but a he pass through down fell the mortar and strike him dead .
` After that the crab live happily for many year , and at length die in peace under her own kaki tree .

The Horse Gullfaxi And The Sword Gunnfoder Many many year ago there live a king and queen who have one only son , call Sigurd .
When the little boy be only ten year old the queen , his mother , fell ill and die , and the king , who love her dearly , build a splendid monument to his wife 's memory , and day after day he sit by it and bewail his sad loss .
One morning , a he sit by the grave , he notice a richly dress lady close to him .
He ask her name and she answer that it be Ingiborg , and seem surprised to see the king there all alone .
Then he tell her how he have lose his queen , and how he come daily to weep at her grave .
In return , the lady inform him that she have lately lose her husband , and suggest that they might both find it a comfort if they make friend .

The Story Of The Sham Prince , Or The Ambitious Tailor Once upon a time there live a respectable young tailor call Labakan , who work for a clever master in Alexandria .
No one could call Labakan either stupid or lazy , for he could work extremely well and quickly -- when he choose ; but there be something not altogether right about him .
Sometimes he would stitch away as fast a if he have a red-hot needle and a burning thread , and at other time he would sit lose in thought , and with such a queer look about him that his fellow-workmen use to say , ` Labakan have get on his aristocratic face today . '
On Fridays he would put on his fine robe which he have buy with the money he have manage to save up , and go to the mosque .
As he come back , after prayer , if he meet any friend who say ` Good-day , ' or ` How be you , friend Labakan ? '
he would wave his hand graciously or nod in a condescending way ; and if his master happen to say to him , a he sometimes do , ` Really , Labakan , you look like a prince , ' he be delight , and would answer , ` Have you notice it too ? '
or ` Well , so I have long think . '
Things go on like this for some time , and the master put up with Labakan 's absurdity because he be , on the whole , a good fellow and a clever workman .
One day , the sultan 's brother happen to be pass through Alexandria , and want to have one of his state robe alter , so he send for the master tailor , who hand the robe over to Labakan a his best workman .
In the evening , when every one have leave the workshop and go home , a great longing drive Labakan back to the place where the royal robe hung .
He stand a long time gaze at it , admire the rich material and the splendid embroidery in it .
At last he could hold out no longer .
He felt he must try it on , and lo !
and behold , it fit a though it have be make for him .
` Am not I as good a prince a any other ? '
he ask himself , a he proudly pace up and down the room .
` Has not the master often say that I seem bear to be a prince ? '
It seem to him that he must be the son of some unknown monarch , and at last he determine to set out at once and travel in search of his proper rank .
He felt a if the splendid robe have be send him by some kind fairy , and he take care not to neglect such a precious gift .
He collect all his saving , and , conceal by the darkness of the night , he pass through the gate of Alexandria .
The new prince excite a good deal of curiosity where ever he go , for his splendid robe and majestic manner do not seem quite suitable to a person travel on foot .
If anyone ask question , he only reply with an important air of mystery that he have his own reason for not rid .
However , he soon find out that walk make him ridiculous , so at last he buy a quiet , steady old horse , which he manage to get cheap .
One day , a he be amble along upon Murva -LRB- that be the horse 's name -RRB- , a horseman overtook him and ask leave to join him , so that they might both beguile the journey with pleasant talk .
The newcomer be a bright , cheerful , good-looking young man , who soon plunge into conversation and ask many question .
He tell Labakan that his own name be Omar , that he be a nephew of Elfi Bey , and be travel in order to carry out a command give him by his uncle on his death bed .
Labakan be not quite so open in his confidence , but hint that he too be of noble birth and be travel for pleasure .
The two young men take a fancy to each other and ride on together .
On the second day of their journey Labakan question Omar a to the order he have to carry out , and to his surprise heard this tale .
Elfi Bey , Pacha of Cairo , have bring up Omar from his early childhood , and the boy have never know his parent .
On his deathbed Elfi Bey call Omar to him , and then tell him that he be not his nephew , but the son of a great king , who , have be warn of come danger by his astrologer , have send the young prince away and make a vow not to see him till his twenty-second birthday .
Elfi Bey do not tell Omar his father 's name , but expressly desire him to be at a great pillar four day ' journey east of Alexandria on the fourth day of the come month , on which day he would be twenty-two year old .
Here he would meet some men , to whom he be to hand a dagger which Elfi Bey give him , and to say ` Here be I for whom you seek . '
If they answer : ` Praised be the Prophet who have preserve you , ' he be to follow them , and they would take him to his father .
Labakan be greatly surprised and interested by this story , but after hear it he could not help look on Prince Omar with envious eye , angry that his friend should have the position he himself long so much for .
He begin to make comparison between the prince and himself , and be oblige to confess that he be a fine-looking young man with very good manner and a pleasant expression .
At the same time , he felt sure that have he be in the prince 's place any royal father might have be glad to own him .
These thought haunt him all day , and he dream them all night .
He wake very early , and a he saw Omar sleep quietly , with a happy smile on his face , a wish arose in his mind to take by force or by cunning the thing which an unkind fate have deny him .
The dagger which be to act a a passport be stick in Omar 's girdle .
Labakan draw it gently out , and hesitate for a moment whether or not to plunge it into the heart of the sleep prince .
However , he shrink from the idea of murder , so he content himself with place the dagger in his own belt , and , saddle Omar 's swift horse for himself , be many mile away before the prince wake up to realise his loss .
For two day Labakan rode on steadily , fear l , after all , Omar might reach the meeting place before him .
At the end of the second day he saw the great pillar at a distance .
It stand on a little hill in the middle of a plain , and could be see a very long way off .
Labakan 's heart beat fast at the sight .
Though he have have some time in which to think over the part he mean to play his conscience make him rather uneasy .
However , the thought that he must certainly have be bear to be a king support him , and he bravely ride on .
The neighbourhood be quite bare and desert , and it be a good thing that the new prince have bring food for some time with him , a two day be still want till the appointed time .
Towards the middle of the next day he saw a long procession of horse and camel come towards him .
It halt at the bottom of the hill , and some splendid tent be pitch .
Everything look like the escort of some great man .
Labakan make a shrewd guess that all these people have come here on his account ; but he check his impatience , know that only on the fourth day could his wish be fulfil .
The first ray of the rise sun wake the happy tailor .
As he begin to saddle his horse and prepare to ride to the pillar , he could not help have some remorseful thought of the trick he have play and the blighted hope of the real prince .
But the die be cast , and his vanity whisper that he be a fine look a young man a the proud king might wish his son to be , and that , moreover , what have happen have happen .
With these thought he summon up all his courage sprang on his horse , and in less than a quarter of an hour be at the foot of the hill .
Here he dismount , tie the horse to a bush , and , draw out Prince Omar 's dagger climb up the hill .
At the foot of the pillar stand six men round a tall and stately person .
His superb robe of cloth of gold be gird round him by a white cashmere shawl , and his white , richly jewelled turban show that he be a man of wealth and high rank .

` Praised be the Prophet who have preserve you !
reply the old man with tear of joy .
'Em brace me , my dear son Omar ! '
The proud tailor be deeply move by these solemn word , and with mingled shame and joy sank into the old king 's arm .
But his happiness be not long unclouded .

` Stop ! '

` Oh !
heaven forbid ! '

` He be talk nonsense again .

All this fill Labakan 's proud heart with rapture , whilst the unfortunate Omar follow in silent rage and despair .
At length they arrive in the capital , where the public rejoicing be grand and more brilliant than anywhere else .
The queen await them in the great hall of the palace , surround by her entire court .

she cry .
