Oh , dear , no , that wo n't do at all . '
But the queen claim his promise , and a he be a man of his word the king give in at last .
He go to his son and beg that he would humour his mother , who have set her heart on his make a kaftan .
The worthy Labakan laugh to himself .
` If that be all she want , ' think he , ` her majesty will soon be please to own me . '
Two room be prepare , with piece of material , scissors , needle and thread , and each young man be shut up in one of them .
The king felt rather curious a to what sort of garment his son would make , and the queen , too , be very anxious a to the result of her experiment .
On the third day they send for the two young men and their work .
Labakan come first and spread out his kaftan before the eye of the astonished king .
` See , father , ' he say ; ` see , my honoured mother , if this be not a masterpiece of work .
I 'll bet the court tailor himself can not do good .
The queen smile and turn to Omar : ` And what have you do , my son ? '
Impatiently he throw the stuff and scissors down on the floor . '
I have be taught how to manage a horse , to draw a sword , and to throw a lance some sixty pace , but I never learn to sew , and such a thing would have be think beneath the notice of the pupil of Elfi Bey , the ruler of Cairo . '
` Ah , true son of your father , ' cry the queen ; ` if only I might embrace you and call you son !
Forgive me , my lord and husband , ' she add , turn to the king , ` for try to find out the truth in this way .
Do you not see yourself now which be the prince and which the tailor ?
Certainly this kaftan be a very fine one , but I should like to know what master teach this young man how to make clothes . '
The king sit deep in thought , look now at his wife and now at Labakan , who be do his best to hide his vexation at his own stupidity .
At last the king say : ` Even this trial do not satisfy me ; but happily I know of a sure way to discover whether or not I have be deceive . '
He order his swift horse to be saddle , mount , and ride off alone into a forest at some little distance .
Here live a kindly fairy call Adolzaide , who have often help the king of his race with her good advice , and to her he betook himself .
In the middle of the forest be a wide open space surround by great cedar tree , and this be suppose to be the fairy 's favourite spot .
When the king reach this place he dismount , tie his horse to the tree , and stand in the middle of the open place say : ` If it be true that you have help my ancestor in their time of need , do not despise their descendant , but give me counsel , for that of men have fail me . '
He have hardly finish speaking when one of the cedar tree open , and a veiled figure all dress in white step from it . '
I know your errand , King Sached , ' she say ; ` it be an honest one , and I will give you my help .
Take these two little box and let the two men who claim to be your son choose between them .
I know that the real prince will make no mistake . '
She then hand him two little box make of ivory set with gold and pearl .
On the lid of each -LRB- which the king vainly try to open -RRB- be an inscription in diamond .
On one stand the word ` Honour and Glory , ' and on the other ` Wealth and Happiness . '
` It would be a hard choice , ' think the king a he ride home .
He lose no time in send for the queen and for all his court , and when all be assemble he make a sign , and Labakan be lead in .
With a proud air he walk up to the throne , and kneel down , ask : ` What do my lord and father command ? '
The king reply : ` My son , doubt have be throw on your claim to that name .
One of these box contain the proof of your birth .
Choose for yourself .
No doubt you will choose right . '
He then point to the ivory box , which be place on two little table near the throne .
Labakan rise and look at the box .
He think for some minute , and then say : ` My honoured father , what can be good than the happiness of be your son , and what noble than the rich of your love .
I choose the box with the word `` Wealth and Happiness . '' '
` We shall see presently if you have choose the right one .
For the present take a seat there beside the Pacha of Medina , ' reply the king .
Omar be next lead in , look sad and sorrowful .
He throw himself down before the throne and ask what be the king 's pleasure .
The king point out the two box to him , and he rise and go to the table .
He carefully read the two motto and say : ` The last few day have show me how uncertain be happiness and how easily riches vanish away .
Should I lose a crown by it I make my choice of `` Honour and Glory . '' '
He lay his hand on the box a he speak , but the king sign to him to wait , and order Labakan to come to the other table and lay his hand on the box he have choose .
Then the king rise from his throne , and in solemn silence all present rise too , whilst he say : ` Open the box , and may Allah show u the truth . '
The box be open with the great ease .
In the one Omar have choose lay a little gold crown and sceptre on a velvet cushion .
In Labakan 's box be find -- a large needle with some thread !
The king tell the two young men to bring him their box .
They do so .
He take the crown in his hand , and a he hold it , it grow big and big , till it be as large a a real crown .
He place it on the head of his son Omar , kiss him on the forehead , and place him on his right hand .
Then , turn to Labakan , he say : ` There be an old proverb , `` The cobbler stick to his last . ''
It seem a though you be to stick to your needle .
You have not deserve any mercy , but I can not be harsh on this day .
I give you your life , but I advise you to leave this country as fast a you can . '
Full of shame , the unlucky tailor could not answer .
He fling himself down before Omar , and with tear in his eye ask : ` Can you forgive me , prince ? '
` Go in peace , ' say Omar a he raise him .
` Oh , my true son ! '
cry the king a he clasp the prince in his arm , whilst all the pacha and emir shout , ` Long live Prince Omar ! '
In the midst of all the noise and rejoice Labakan slip off with his little box under his arm .
He go to the stable , saddle his old horse , Murva , and ride out of the gate towards Alexandria .
Nothing but the ivory box with it diamond motto be leave to show him that the last few week have not be a dream .
When he reach Alexandria he ride up to his old master 's door .
When he enter the shop , his master come forward to ask what be his pleasure , but as soon a he saw who it be he call his workman , and they all fell on Labakan with blow and angry word , till at last he fell , half fainting , on a heap of old clothes .
The master then scold him soundly about the stolen robe , but in vain Labakan tell him he have come to pay for it and offer three time it price .
They only fell to beat him again , and at last push him out of the house more dead than alive .
He could do nothing but remount his horse and ride to an inn .
Here he find a quiet place in which to rest his bruise and batter limb and to think over his many misfortune .
He fell asleep fully determine to give up try to be great , but to lead the life of an honest workman .
Next morning he set to work to fulfil his good resolution .
He sell his little box to a jeweller for a good price , buy a house and open a workshop .
Then he hang up a sign with , ` Labakan , Tailor , ' over his door , and sit down to mend his own torn clothes with the very needle which have be in the ivory box .
After a while he be call away , and when he go back to his work he find a wonderful thing have happen !
The needle be sew away all by itself and make the neat little stitch , such a Labakan have never be able to make even at his best .
Certainly even the small gift of a kind fairy be of great value , and this one have yet another advantage , for the thread never come to an end , however much the needle sewed .
Labakan soon get plenty of customer .
He use to cut out the clothes , make the first stitch with the magic needle , and then leave it to do the rest .
Before long the whole town go to him , for his work be both so good and so cheap .
The only puzzle be how he could do so much , work all alone , and also why he work with closed door .
And so the promise on the ivory box of ` Wealth and Happiness ' come true for him , and when he hear of all the brave doings of Prince Omar , who be the pride and darling of his people and the terror of his enemy , the ex-prince thought to himself , ` After all , I be well off a a tailor , for `` Honour and Glory '' be apt to be very dangerous thing . '
The Colony Of Cats Long , long ago , a far back a the time when animal speak , there live a community of cat in a desert house they have take possession of not far from a large town .
They have everything they could possibly desire for their comfort , they be well feed and well lodge , and if by any chance an unlucky mouse be stupid enough to venture in their way , they catch it , not to eat it , but for the pure pleasure of catch it .
The old people of the town relate how they have hear their parent speak of a time when the whole country be so overrun with rat and mouse that there be not so much a a grain of corn nor an ear of maize to be gather in the field ; and it might be out of gratitude to the cat who have rid the country of these plague that their descendant be allow to live in peace .
No one know where they get the money to pay for everything , nor who pay it , for all this happen so very long ago .
But one thing be certain , they be rich enough to keep a servant ; for though they live very happily together , and do not scratch nor fight more than human being would have do , they be not clever enough to do the housework themselves , and prefer at all event to have some one to cook their meat , which they would have scorn to eat raw .
Not only be they very difficult to please about the housework , but most woman quickly tire of live alone with only cat for companion , consequently they never keep a servant long ; and it have become a say in the town , when anyone find herself reduce to her last penny : ' I will go and live with the cat , ' and so many a poor woman actually do .
Now Lizina be not happy at home , for her mother , who be a widow , be much fonder of her elder daughter ; so that often the young one fare very badly , and have not enough to eat , while the elder could have everything she desire , and if Lizina dare to complain she be certain to have a good beating .
At last the day come when she be at the end of her courage and patience , and exclaim to her mother and sister : ` As you hate me so much you will be glad to be rid of me , so I be go to live with the cat ! '
` Be off with you ! '
cry her mother , seize an old broom-handle from behind the door .
Poor Lizina do not wait to be tell twice , but run off at once and never stop till she reach the door of the cat ' house .
Their cook have leave them that very morning , with her face all scratch , the result of such a quarrel with the head of the house that he have very nearly scratch out her eye .
Lizina therefore be warmly welcome , and she set to work at once to prepare the dinner , not without many misgiving a to the taste of the cat , and whether she would be able to satisfy them .
Going to and fro about her work , she find herself frequently hinder by a constant succession of cat who appear one after another in the kitchen to inspect the new servant ; she have one in front of her foot , another perch on the back of her chair while she peel the vegetable , a third sat on the table beside her , and five or six others prowl about among the pot and pan on the shelf against the wall .
The air resound with their purring , which mean that they be please with their new maid , but Lizina have not yet learn to understand their language , and often she do not know what they want her to do .
However , a she be a good , kindhearted girl , she set to work to pick up the little kitten which tumble about on the floor , she patch up quarrel , and nurse on her lap a big tabby -- the old of the community -- which have a lame paw .
All these kindness could hardly fail to make a favourable impression on the cat , and it be even good after a while , when she have have time to grow accustom to their strange way .
Never have the house be keep so clean , the meat so well serve , nor the sick cat so well care for .
After a time they have a visit from an old cat , whom they call their father , who live by himself in a barn at the top of the hill , and come down from time to time to inspect the little colony .
He too be much take with Lizina , and inquire , on first see her : ` Are you well serve by this nice , black-eyed little person ? '
and the cat answer with one voice : ` Oh , yes , Father Gatto , we have never have so good a servant ! '
At each of his visit the answer be always the same ; but after a time the old cat , who be very observant , notice that the little maid have grow to look sadder and sadder .
` What be the matter , my child have any one be unkind to you ? '
he ask one day , when he find her cry in her kitchen .
She burst into tear and answer between her sob : ` Oh , no !
they be all very good to me ; but I long for news from home , and I pine to see my mother and my sister . '
Old Gatto , be a sensible old cat , understand the little servant 's feeling .
` You shall go home , ' he say , ` and you shall not come back here unless you please .
But first you must be reward for all your kind service to my child .
Follow me down into the inner cellar , where you have never yet be , for I always keep it locked and carry the key away with me . '
Lizina look round her in astonishment a they go down into the great vaulted cellar underneath the kitchen .
Before her stand the big earthenware water jar , one of which contain oil , the other a liquid shining like gold .
` In which of these jar shall I dip you ? '
ask Father Gatto , with a grin that show all his sharp white teeth , while his moustache stand out straight on either side of his face .
The little maid look at the two jar from under her long dark lash : ` In the oil jar , ' she answer timidly , think to herself : ' I could not ask to be bath in gold . '
But Father Gatto reply : ` No , no ; you have deserve something well than that . '
And seize her in his strong paw he plunge her into the liquid gold .
Wonder of wonder !
when Lizina come out of the jar she shine from head to foot like the sun in the heaven on a fine summer 's day .
Her pretty pink cheek and long black hair alone keep their natural colour , otherwise she have become like a statue of pure gold .
Father Gatto purr loudly with satisfaction .
` Go home , ' he say , ` and see your mother and sister ; but take care if you hear the cock crow to turn towards it ; if on the contrary the as bray , you must look the other way . '
The little maid , have gratefully kiss the white paw of the old cat , set off for home ; but just a she get near her mother 's house the cock crow , and quickly she turn towards it .
Immediately a beautiful golden star appear on her forehead , crown her glossy black hair .
At the same time the as begin to bray , but Lizina take care not to look over the fence into the field where the donkey be feed .
Her mother and sister , who be in front of their house , uttered cry of admiration and astonishment when they saw her , and their cry become still louder when Lizina , take her handkerchief from her pocket , draw out also a handful of gold .
For some day the mother and her two daughter live very happily together , for Lizina have give them everything she have bring away except her golden clothing , for that would not come off , in spite of all the effort of her sister , who be madly jealous of her good fortune .
The golden star , too , could not be remove from her forehead .
But all the gold piece she draw from her pocket have find their way to her mother and sister . '
I will go now and see what I can get out of the pussy , ' say Peppina , the elder girl , one morning , a she take Lizina 's basket and fasten her pocket into her own skirt . '
I should like some of the cat ' gold for myself , ' she think , a she leave her mother 's house before the sun rise .
The cat colony have not yet take another servant , for they know they could never get one to replace Lizina , whose loss they have not yet cease to mourn .
When they hear that Peppina be her sister , they all run to meet her .
` She be not the least like her , ' the kitten whisper among themselves .
` Hush , be quiet ! '
the old cat say ; ` all servant can not be pretty . '
No , decidedly she be not at all like Lizina .
Even the most reasonable and large-minded of the cat soon acknowledge that .
The very first day she shut the kitchen door in the face of the tom-cats who use to enjoy watch Lizina at her work , and a young and mischievous cat who jump in by the open kitchen window and alight on the table get such a blow with the rolling-pin that he squall for an hour .
With every day that pass the household become more and more aware of it misfortune .
The work be a badly do a the servant be surly and disagreeable ; in the corner of the room there be collect heap of dust ; spider ' web hang from the ceiling and in front of the window-panes ; the bed be hardly ever make , and the feather bed , so beloved by the old and feeble cat , have never once be shake since Lizina leave the house .
At Father Gatto 's next visit he find the whole colony in a state of uproar .
` Caesar have one paw so badly swell that it look a if it be break , ' say one .
` Peppina kick him with her great wooden shoe on .
Hector have an abscess in his back where a wooden chair be fling at him ; and Agrippina 's three little kitten have die of hunger beside their mother , because Peppina forget them in their basket up in the attic .
There be no put up with the creature -- do send her away , Father Gatto !
Lizina herself would not be angry with u ; she must know very well what her sister be like . '
` Come here , ' say Father Gatto , in his most severe tone to Peppina .
And he take her down into the cellar and show her the same two great jar that he have show Lizina .
` In which of these shall I dip you ? '
he ask ; and she make haste to answer : ` In the liquid gold , ' for she be no more modest than she be good and kind .
Father Gatto 's yellow eye dart fire .
` You have not deserve it , ' he utter , in a voice like thunder , and seize her he fling her into the jar of oil , where she be nearly suffocate .
When she come to the surface screaming and struggling , the vengeful cat seize her again and roll her in the ash-heap on the floor ; then when she rise , dirty , blind , and disgust to behold , he thrust her from the door , say : ` Begone , and when you meet a braying as be careful to turn your head towards it . '
Stumbling and rag , Peppina set off for home , think herself fortunate to find a stick by the wayside with which to support herself .
She be within sight of her mother 's house when she hear in the meadow on the right , the voice of a donkey loudly bray .
Quickly she turn her head towards it , and at the same time put her hand up to her forehead , where , wave like a plume , be a donkey 's tail .
She run home to her mother at the top of her speed , yell with rage and despair ; and it take Lizina two hour with a big basin of hot water and two cake of soap to get rid of the layer of ash with which Father Gatto have adorn her .
As for the donkey 's tail , it be impossible to get rid of that ; it be a firmly fix on her forehead a be the golden star on Lizina 's .
Their mother be furious .
She first beat Lizina unmercifully with the broom , then she take her to the mouth of the well and lower her into it , leave her at the bottom weeping and cry for help .
Before this happen , however , the king 's son in pass the mother 's house have see Lizina sit sew in the parlour , and have be dazzle by her beauty .
After come back two or three time , he at last ventured to approach the window and to whisper in the soft voice : ` Lovely maiden , will you be my bride ? '
and she have answer : ' I will . '
Next morning , when the prince arrive to claim his bride , he find her wrap in a large white veil .
` It be so that maiden be receive from their parent ' hand , ' say the mother , who hop to make the king 's son marry Peppina in place of her sister , and have fasten the donkey 's tail round her head like a lock of hair under the veil .
The prince be young and a little timid , so he make no objection , and seat Peppina in the carriage beside him .
Their way lead past the old house inhabit by the cat , who be all at the window , for the report have get about that the prince be go to marry the most beautiful maiden in the world , on whose forehead shone a golden star , and they know that this could only be their adored Lizina .
As the carriage slowly pass in front of the old house , where cat from all part of world seem to be gather a song burst from every throat : Mew , mew , mew !
Prince , look quick behind you !
In the well be fair Lizina , And you 've get nothing but Peppina .
When he hear this the coachman , who understand the cat 's language well than the prince , his master , stop his horse and ask : ` Does your highness know what the grimalkins be say ? '
and the song break forth again louder than ever .
With a turn of his hand the prince throw back the veil , and discover the puffed-up , swollen face of Peppina , with the donkey 's tail twist round her head .
` Ah , traitress ! '
he exclaim , and order the horse to be turn round , he drive the elder daughter , quiver with rage , to the old woman who have seek to deceive him .
With his hand on the hilt of his sword he demand Lizina in so terrific a voice that the mother hasten to the well to draw her prisoner out .
Lizina 's clothing and her star shone so brilliantly that when the prince lead her home to the king , his father , the whole palace be light up .
Next day they be marry , and live happy ever after ; and all the cat , head by old Father Gatto , be present at the wedding .
How To Find Out A True Friend Once upon a time there live a king and queen who long to have a son .
As none come , one day they make a vow at the shrine of St. James that if their prayer be grant the boy should set out on a pilgrimage as soon a he have pass his eighteenth birthday .
And fancy their delight when one even the king return home from hunt and saw a baby lie in the cradle .
All the people come crowd round to peep at it , and declare it be the most beautiful baby that ever be see .
Of course that be what they always say , but this time it happen to be true .
And every day the boy grow big and strong till he be twelve year old , when the king die , and he be leave alone to take care of his mother .
In this way six year pass by , and his eighteenth birthday draw near .
When she think of this the queen 's heart sank within her , for he be the light of her eye ' and how be she to send him forth to the unknown danger that beset a pilgrim ?
So day by day she grow more and more sorrowful , and when she be alone wept bitterly .
Now the queen imagine that no one but herself know how sad she be , but one morning her son say to her , ` Mother , why do you cry the whole day long ? '
` Nothing , nothing , my son ; there be only one thing in the world that trouble me . '
` What be that one thing ? '
ask he .
` Are you afraid your property be badly manage ?
Let me go and look into the matter . '
This please the queen , and he ride off to the plain country , where his mother own great estate ; but everything be in beautiful order , and he return with a joyful heart , and say , ` Now , mother , you can be happy again , for your land be well manage than anyone else 's I have see .
The cattle be thrive ; the field be thick with corn , and soon they will be ripe for harvest . '
` That be good news indeed , ' answer she ; but it do not seem to make any difference to her , and the next morning she be weep and wail as loudly a ever .
` Dear mother , ' say her son in despair , ` if you will not tell me what be the cause of all this misery I shall leave home and wander far through the world . '
` Ah , my son , my son , ' cry the queen , ` it be the thought that I must part from you which cause me such grief ; for before you be bear we vow a vow to St. James that when your eighteenth birthday be pass you should make a pilgrimage to his shrine , and very soon you will be eighteen , and I shall lose you .
And for a whole year my eye will never be gladden by the sight of you , for the shrine be far away . '
` Will it take no long than that to reach it ? '
say he .
` Oh , do n't be so wretched ; it be only dead people who never return .
As long a I be alive you may be sure I will come back to you . '
After this manner he comfort his mother , and on his eighteenth birthday his best horse be lead to the door of the palace , and he take leave of the queen in these word , ` Dear mother , farewell , and by the help of fate I shall return to you as soon a I can . '
The queen burst into tear and weep sore ; then amidst her sobs she draw three apple from her pocket and hold them out , say , ` My son , take these apple and give heed unto my word .
You will need a companion in the long journey on which you be go .
If you come across a young man who please you beg him to accompany you , and when you get to an inn invite him to have dinner with you .
After you have eat cut one of these apple in two unequal part , and ask him to take one .
If he take the large bit , then part from him , for he be no true friend to you .
But if he take the small bit treat him a your brother , and share with him all you have . '
Then she kiss her son once more , and bless him , and let him go .
The young man ride a long way without meet a single creature , but at last he saw a youth in the distance about the same age a himself , and he spur his horse till he come up with the stranger , who stop and ask : ` Where be you go , my fine fellow ? ' '
I be make a pilgrimage to the shrine of St. James , for before I be bear my mother vow that I should go forth with a thank offering on my eighteenth birthday . '
` That be my case too , ' say the stranger , ` and , a we must both travel in the same direction , let u bear each other company . '
The young man agree to this proposal , but he take care not to get on term of familiarity with the new comer until he have try him with the apple .
By-and-by they reach an inn , and at sight of it the king 's son say , ' I be very hungry .
Let u enter and order something to eat . '
The other consent , and they be soon sit before a good dinner .
When they have finish the king 's son draw an apple from his pocket , and cut it into a big half and a little half , and offer both to the stranger , who take the big bit .
` You be no friend of mine , ' think the king 's son , and in order to part company with him he pretend to be ill and declare himself unable to proceed on his journey .
` Well , I ca n't wait for you , ' reply the other ; ' I be in haste to push on , so farewell . '
` Farewell , ' say the king 's son , glad in his heart to get rid of him so easily .
The king 's son remain in the inn for some time , so a to let the young man have a good start ; them he order his horse and rode after him .
But he be very sociable and the way seem long and dull by himself .
` Oh , if I could only meet with a true friend , ' he think , ` so that I should have some one to speak to .
I hate be alone . '
Soon after he come up with a young man , who stop and ask him , ` Where be you go , my fine fellow ? '
The king 's son explain the object of his journey , and the young man answer , a the other have do , that he also be fulfil the vow of his mother make at his birth .
` Well , we can ride on together , ' say the king 's son , and the road seem much short now that he have some one to talk to .
At length they reach an inn , and the king 's son exclaim , ' I be very hungry ; let u go in and get something to eat . '
When they have finish the king 's son draw an apple out of his pocket and cut it in two ; he hold the big bit and the little bit out to his companion , who take the big bit at once and soon eat it up .
` You be no friend of mine , ' think the king 's son , and begin to declare he felt so ill he could not continue his journey .
When he have give the young man a good start he set off himself , but the way seem even longer and duller than before .
` Oh , if I could only meet with a true friend he should be a a brother to me , ' he sigh sadly ; and a the thought pass through his mind , he notice a youth go the same road a himself .
The youth come up to him and say , ` Which way be you go , my fine fellow ? '
And for the third time the king 's son explain all about his mother 's vow .
Why , that be just like me , ' cry the youth .
` Then let u ride on together , ' answer the king 's son .
Now the mile seem to slip by , for the new comer be so lively and entertain that the king 's son could not help hop that he indeed might prove to be the true friend .
More quickly than he could have think possible they reach an inn by the road-side , and turn to his companion the king 's son say , ' I be hungry ; let u go in and have something to eat . '
So they go in and order dinner , and when they have finish the king 's son draw out of his pocket the last apple , and cut it into two unequal part , and hold both out to the stranger .
And the stranger take the little piece , and the heart of the king 's son be glad within him , for at last he have find the friend he have be look for .
` Good youth , ' he cry , ` we will be brother , and what be mine shall be thine , and what be thine shall be mine .
And together we will push on to the shrine , and if one of u die on the road the other shall carry his body there . '
And the stranger agree to all he say , and they ride forward together .
It take them a whole year to reach the shrine , and they pass through many different land on their way .
One day they arrive tired and half-starved in a big city , and say to one another , ` Let u stay here for a little and rest before we set forth again . '
So they hire a small house close to the royal castle , and take up their abode there .
The following morning the king of the country happen to step on to his balcony , and saw the young men in the garden , and say to himself , ` Dear me , those be wonderfully handsome youth ; but one be handsome than the other , and to him will I give my daughter to wife ; ' and indeed the king 's son excel his friend in beauty .
In order to set about his plan the king ask both the young men to dinner , and when they arrive at the castle he receive them with the utmost kindness , and send for his daughter , who be more lovely than both the sun and moon put together .
But at bed-time the king cause the other young man to be give a poisoned drink , which kill him in a few minute , for he think to himself , ` If his friend die the other will forget his pilgrimage , and will stay here and marry my daughter . '
When the king 's son awake the next morning he inquire of the servant where his friend have go , a he do not see him .
` He die suddenly last night , ' say they , ` and be to be bury immediately . '
But the king 's son spring up , and cry , ` If my friend be dead I can stay here no long , and can not linger an hour in this house . '
` Oh , give up your journey and remain here , ' exclaim the king , ` and you shall have my daughter for your wife . '
` No , ' answer the king 's son , ' I can not stay ; but , I pray you , grant my request , and give me a good horse , and let me go in peace , and when I have fulfil my vow then I will return and marry your daughter . '
So the king , see no word would move him , order a horse to be bring round , and the king 's son mount it , and take his dead friend before him on the saddle , and ride away .
Now the young man be not really dead , but only in a deep sleep .
When the king 's son reach the shrine of St. James he get down from his horse , take his friend in his arm a if he have be a child , and lay him before the altar .
` St. James , ' he say , ' I have fulfil the vow my parent make for me .
I have come myself to your shrine , and have bring my friend .
I place him in your hand .
Restore him to life , I pray , for though he be dead yet have he fulfil his vow also . '
And , behold !
while he yet pray his friend get up and stand before him as well a ever .
And both the young men give thanks , and set their face towards home .
When they arrive at the town where the king dwelt they enter the small house over against the castle .
The news of their coming spread very soon , and the king rejoice greatly that the handsome young prince have come back again , and command great feast to be prepare , for in a few day his daughter should marry the king 's son .
The young man himself could imagine no great happiness , and when the marriage be over they spend some month at the court making merry .
At length the king 's son say , ` My mother await me at home , full of care and anxiety .
Here I must remain no long , and to-morrow I will take my wife and my friend and start for home . '
And the king be content that he should do so , and give order to prepare for their journey .
Now in his heart the king cherish a deadly hate towards the poor young man whom he have try to kill , but who have return to him living , and in order to do him hurt send him on a message to some distant spot .
` See that you be quick , ' say he , ` for your friend will await your return before he start . '
The youth put spur to his horse and depart , bid the prince farewell , so that the king 's message might be deliver the sooner .
As soon a he have start the king go to the chamber of the prince , and say to him , ` If you do not start immediately , you will never reach the place where you must camp for the night . ' '
I can not start without my friend , ' reply the king 's son .
` Oh , he will be back in an hour , ' reply the king , ` and I will give him my best horse , so that he will be sure to catch you up . '
The king 's son allow himself to be persuade and take leave of his father-in-law , and set out with his wife on his journey home .
Meanwhile the poor friend have be unable to get through his task in the short time appoint by the king , and when at last he return the king say to him , ` Your comrade be a long way off by now ; you have good see if you can overtake him . '
So the young man bow and leave the king 's presence , and follow after his friend on foot , for he have no horse .
Night and day he run , till at length he reach the place where the king 's son have pitch his tent , and sink down before him , a miserable object , wear out and cover with mud and dust .
But the king 's son welcome him with joy , and tend him a he would his brother .
And at last they come home again , and the queen be wait and watch in the palace , a she have never cease to do since her son have ride away .
She almost die of joy at see him again , but after a little she remember his sick friend , and order a bed to be make ready and the best doctor in all the country to be send for .
When they hear of the queen 's summons they flock from all part , but none could cure him .
After everyone have try and fail a servant enter and inform the queen that a strange old man have just knock at the palace gate and declare that he be able to heal the die youth .
Now this be a holy man , who have heard of the trouble the king 's son be in , and have come to help .
It happen that at this very time a little daughter be bear to the king 's son , but in his distress for his friend he have hardly a thought to spare for the baby .
He could not be prevail on to leave the sick bed , and he be bend over it when the holy man enter the room .
` Do you wish your friend to be cure ? '
ask the new comer of the king 's son .
` And what price would you pay ? '
` What price ? '
answer the king 's son ; ` only tell me what I can do to heal him . '
` Listen to me , then , ' say the old man .
` This evening you must take your child , and open her vein , and smear the wound of your friend with her blood .
And you will see , he will get well in an instant . '
At these word the king 's son shriek with horror , for he love the baby dearly , but he answer , ' I have swear that I would treat my friend a if he be my brother , and if there be no other way my child must be sacrifice . '
As by this time even have already fall he take the child and open it vein , and smear the blood over the wound of the sick man , and the look of death depart from him , and he grow strong and rosy once more .
But the little child lay a white and still a if she have be dead .
They lay her in the cradle and weep bitterly , for they think that by the next morning she would be lose to them .
At sunrise the old man return and ask after the sick man .
` He be as well a ever , ' answer the king 's son .
` And where be your baby ? '
` In the cradle yonder , and I think she be dead , ' reply the father sadly .
` Look at her once more , ' say the holy man , and a they draw near the cradle there lay the baby smile up at them . '
I be St. James of Lizia , ' say the old man , ` and I have come to help you , for I have see that you be a true friend .
From henceforward live happily , all of you , together , and if trouble should draw near you send for me , and I will aid you to get through them . '
With these word he lift his hand in blessing and vanish .
And they obey him , and be happy and content , and try to make the people of the land happy and content too .

Clever Maria There be once a merchant who live close to the royal palace , and have three daughter .
They be all pretty , but Maria , the young , be the pretty of the three .
One day the king sent for the merchant , who be a widower , to give him direction about a journey he wish the good man to take .
The merchant would rather not have go , a he do not like leave his daughter at home , but he could not refuse to obey the king 's command , and with a heavy heart he return home to say farewell to them .
Before he leave , he take three pot of basil , and give one to each girl , say , ' I be go a journey , but I leave these pot .
You must let nobody into the house .
When I come back , they will tell me what have happen . '
` Nothing will have happen , ' say the girl .
The father go away , and the following day the king , accompany by two friend , pay a visit to the three girl , who be sit at supper .
When they saw who be there , Maria say , ` Let u go and get a bottle of wine from the cellar .
I will carry the key , my eldest sister can take the light , while the other bring the bottle . '
But the king reply , ` Oh , do not trouble ; we be not thirsty . '
` Very well , we will not go , ' answer the two elder girl ; but Maria merely say , ' I shall go , anyhow . '
She leave the room , and go to the hall where she put out the light , and put down the key and the bottle , run to the house of a neighbour , and knock at the door .
` Who be there so late ? '
ask the old woman , thrust her head out of the window .
` Oh , let me in , ' answer Maria . '
I have quarrel with my eldest sister , and a I do not want to fight any more , I have come to beg you to allow me to sleep with you . '
So the old woman open the door and Maria slept in her house .
The king be very angry at her for play truant , but when she return home the next day , she find the plant of her sister wither away , because they have disobey their father .
Now the window in the room of the eldest overlook the garden of the king , and when she saw how fine and ripe the medlar be on the tree , she long to eat some , and beg Maria to scramble down by a rope and pick her a few , and she would draw her up again .
Maria , who be good-natured , swing herself into the garden by the rope , and get the medlar , and be just make the rope fast under her arm so a to be haul up , when her sister cry : ` Oh , there be such delicious lemon a little farther on .
You might bring me one or two . '
Maria turn round to pluck them , and find herself face to face with the gardener , who catch hold of her , exclaim , ` What be you do here , you little thief ? '
` Do n't call me names , ' she say , ` or you will get the bad of it , ' give him a she speak such a violent push that he fell pant into the lemon bush .
Then she seize the cord and clamber up to the window .
The next day the second sister have a fancy for banana and beg so hard , that , though Maria have declare she would never do such a thing again , at last she consent , and go down the rope into the king 's garden .
This time she meet the king , who say to her , ` Ah , here you be again , cunning one !
Now you shall pay for your misdeed . '
And he begin to cross-question her about what she have do .
Maria deny nothing , and when she have finish , the king say again , ` Follow me to the house , and there you shall pay the penalty . '
As he speak , he start for the house , look back from time to time to make sure that Maria have not run away .
All of a sudden , when he glance round , he find she have vanish completely , without leave a trace of where she have go .
Search be make all through the town , and there be not a hole or corner which be not ransack , but there be no sign of her anywhere .
This so enraged the king that he become quite ill , and for many month his life be despair of .
Meanwhile the two elder sister have marry the two friend of the king , and be the mother of little daughter .
Now one day Maria stole secretly to the house where her elder sister live , and snatch up the child put them into a beautiful basket she have with her , cover with flower inside and out , so that no one would ever guess it hold two baby .
Then she dress herself a a boy , and place the basket on her head , she walk slowly past the palace , cry a she go : ` Who will carry these flower to the king , who lie sick of love ? '
And the king in his bed hear what she say , and order one of his attendant to go out and buy the basket .
It be bring to his bedside , and a he raise the lid cry be hear , and peep in he saw two little child .
He be furious at this new trick which he felt have be play on him by Maria , and be still look at them , wonder how he should pay her out , when he be tell that the merchant , Maria 's father , have finish the business on which he have be send and return home .
Then the king remember how Maria have refuse to receive his visit , and how she have steal his fruit , and he determine to be revenge on her .
So he send a message by one of his page that the merchant be to come to see him the next day , and bring with him a coat make of stone , or else he would be punish .
Now the poor man have be very sad since he get home the evening before , for though his daughter have promise that nothing should happen while he be away , he have find the two elder one marry without ask his leave .
And now there be this fresh misfortune , for how be he to make a coat of stone ?
He wring his hand and declare that the king would be the ruin of him , when Maria suddenly enter .
` Do not grieve about the coat of stone , dear father ; but take this bit of chalk , and go to the palace and say you have come to measure the king . '
The old man do not see the use of this , but Maria have so often help him before that he have confidence in her , so he put the chalk in his pocket and go to the palace .
` That be no good , ' say the king , when the merchant have tell him what he have come for .
` Well , I ca n't make the coat you want , ' reply he .
` Then if you would save your head , hand over to me your daughter Maria . '
The merchant do not reply , but go sorrowfully back to his house , where Maria sit wait for him .
` Oh , my dear child , why be I born ?
The king say that , instead of the coat , I must deliver you up to him . '
` Do not be unhappy , dear father , but get a doll make , exactly like me , with a string attach to it head , which I can pull for `` Yes '' and `` No . '' '
So the old man go out at once to see about it .
The king remain patiently in his palace , feel sure that this time Maria could not escape him ; and he say to his page , ` If a gentleman should come here with his daughter and ask to be allow to speak with me , put the young lady in my room and see she do not leave it . '
When the door be shut on Maria , who have conceal the doll under her cloak , she hide herself under the couch , keep fast hold of the string which be fasten to it head .
` Senhora Maria , I hope you be well , ' say the king when he enter the room .
The doll nod .
` Now we will reckon up account , ' continue he , and he begin at the beginning , and end up with the flower-basket , and at each fresh misdeed Maria pull the string , so that the doll 's head nod assent .
` Who-so mock at me merit death , ' declare the king when he have end , and draw his sword , cut off the doll 's head .
It fell towards him , and a he felt the touch of a kiss , he exclaim , ` Ah , Maria , Maria , so sweet in death , so hard to me in life !
The man who could kill you deserves to die ! '
And he be about to turn his sword on himself , when the true Maria sprung out from under the bed , and fling herself into his arm .
And the next day they be marry and live happily for many year .

The Magic Kettle Right in the middle of Japan , high up among the mountain , an old man live in his little house .
He be very proud of it , and never tire of admire the whiteness of his straw mat , and the pretty papered wall , which in warm weather always slide back , so that the smell of the tree and flower might come in .
One day he be stand look at the mountain opposite , when he hear a kind of rumble noise in the room behind him .
He turn round , and in the corner he behold a rusty old iron kettle , which could not have see the light of day for many year .
How the kettle get there the old man do not know , but he take it up and look it over carefully , and when he find that it be quite whole he clean the dust off it and carry it into his kitchen .
` That be a piece of luck , ' he say , smile to himself ; ' a good kettle cost money , and it be as well to have a second one at hand in case of need ; mine be get wear out , and the water be already begin to come through it bottom . '
Then he take the other kettle off the fire , fill the new one with water , and put it in it place .
No sooner be the water in the kettle get warm than a strange thing happen , and the man , who be stand by , think he must be dream .
First the handle of the kettle gradually change it shape and become a head , and the spout grow into a tail , while out of the body spring four paw , and in a few minute the man find himself watch , not a kettle , but a tanuki !
The creature jump off the fire , and bound about the room like a kitten , run up the wall and over the ceiling , till the old man be in an agony l his pretty room should be spoil .
He cry to a neighbour for help , and between them they manage to catch the tanuki , and shut him up safely in a wooden chest .
Then , quite exhaust , they sit down on the mat , and consult together what they should do with this troublesome beast .
At length they decide to sell him , and bid a child who be pass send them a certain tradesman call Jimmu .
When Jimmu arrive , the old man tell him that he have something which he wish to get rid of , and lift the lid of the wooden chest , where he have shut up the tanuki .
But , to his surprise , no tanuki be there , nothing but the kettle he have find in the corner .
It be certainly very odd , but the man remember what have take place on the fire , and do not want to keep the kettle any more , so after a little bargaining about the price , Jimmu go away carry the kettle with him .
Now Jimmu have not go very far before he felt that the kettle be get heavy and heavy , and by the time he reach home he be so tired that he be thankful to put it down in the corner of his room , and then forget all about it .
In the middle of the night , however , he be awaken by a loud noise in the corner where the kettle stand , and raise himself up in bed to see what it be .
But nothing be there except the kettle , which seem quiet enough .
He think that he must have be dream , and fell asleep again , only to be rouse a second time by the same disturbance .
He jump up and go to the corner , and by the light of the lamp that he always keep burn he saw that the kettle have become a tanuki , which be run round after his tail .
After he grow weary of that , he run on the balcony , where he turn several somersault , from pure gladness of heart .
The tradesman be much troubled a to what to do with the animal , and it be only towards morning that he manage to get any sleep ; but when he open his eye again there be no tanuki , only the old kettle he have leave there the night before .
As soon a he have tidy his house , Jimmu set off to tell his story to a friend next door .
The man listen quietly , and do not appear so surprised a Jimmu expect , for he recollect have heard , in his youth , something about a wonder-working kettle .
` Go and travel with it , and show it off , ' say he , ` and you will become a rich man ; but be careful first to ask the tanuki 's leave , and also to perform some magic ceremony to prevent him from run away at the sight of the people . '
Jimmu thank his friend for his counsel , which he follow exactly .
The tanuki 's consent be obtain , a booth be build , and a notice be hang up outside it invite the people to come and witness the most wonderful transformation that ever be see .
They come in crowd , and the kettle be pass from hand to hand , and they be allow to examine it all over , and even to look inside .
Then Jimmu take it back , and set it on the platform , command it to become a tanuki .
In an instant the handle begin to change into a head , and the spout into a tail , while the four paw appear at the side .
` Dance , ' say Jimmu , and the tanuki do his step , and move first on one side and then on the other , till the people could not stand still any long , and begin to dance too .
Gracefully he lead the fan dance , and glide without a pause into the shadow dance and the umbrella dance , and it seem a if he might go on dance for ever .
And so very likely he would , if Jimmu have not declare he have dance enough , and that the booth must now be close .
Day after day the booth be so full it be hardly possible to enter it , and what the neighbour foretold have come to pass , and Jimmu be a rich man .
Yet he do not feel happy .
He be an honest man , and he think that he owe some of his wealth to the man from whom he have buy the kettle .
So , one morning , he put a hundred gold piece into it , and hang the kettle once more on his arm , he return to the seller of it . '
I have no right to keep it any longer , ' he add when he have end his tale , ` so I have bring it back to you , and inside you will find a hundred gold piece a the price of it hire . '
The man thank Jimmu , and say that few people would have be as honest a he .
And the kettle bring them both luck , and everything go well with them till they die , which they do when they be very old , respect by everyone .

The Shifty Lad In the land of Erin there dwelt long ago a widow who have an only son .
He be a clever boy , so she save up enough money to send him to school , and , as soon a he be old enough , to apprentice him to any trade that he would choose .
But when the time come , he say he would not be bind to any trade , and that he mean to be a thief .
Now his mother be very sorrowful when she hear of this , but she know quite well that if she try to stop his have his own way he would only grow more determined to get it .
So all the answer she make be that the end of thief be hang at the bridge of Dublin , and then she leave him alone , hop that when he be old he might become more sensible .
One day she be go to church to hear a sermon from a great preacher , and she beg the Shifty Lad , a the neighbour call him from the trick he play , to come with her .
But he only laugh and declare that he do not like sermon , add : ` However , I will promise you this , that the first trade you hear name after you come out from church shall be my trade for the rest of my life . '
These word give a little comfort to the poor woman , and her heart be light than before a she bid him farewell .
When the Shifty Lad think that the hour have nearly come for the sermon to be over , he hide himself in some bush in a little path that lead straight to his mother 's house , and , a she pass along , think of all the good thing she have hear , a voice shout close to her ear ` Robbery !
Robbery !
Robbery ! '
The suddenness of it make her jump .
The naughty boy have manage to change his voice , so that she do not know it for his , and he have conceal himself so well that , though she peer about all round her , she could see no one .
As soon a she have turn the corner the Shifty Lad come out , and by run very fast through the wood he contrive to reach home before his mother , who find him stretch out comfortably before the fire .
` Well , have you get any news to tell me ? '
ask he .
` No , nothing ; for I leave the church at once , and do not stop to speak to anyone . '
` Oh , then no one have mention a trade to you ? '
he say in tone of disappointment .
` Ye -- e , ' she reply slowly .
` At least , a I walk down the path a voice cry out `` Robbery !
Robbery !
Robbery ! ''
but that be all . '
` And quite enough too , ' answer the boy .
` What do I tell you ?
That be go to be my trade . '
` Then your end will be hang at the bridge of Dublin , ' say she .
But there be no sleep for her that night , for she lay in the dark think about her son .
` If he be to be a thief at all , he have well be a good one .
And who be there that can teach him ? '
the mother ask herself .
But an idea come to her , and she arise early , before the sun be up , and set off for the home of the Black Rogue , or Gallows Bird , who be such a wonderful thief that , though all have be rob by him , no one could catch him .
` Good-morning to you , ' say the woman a she reach the place where the Black Gallows Bird live when he be not away on his business .
` My son have a fancy to learn your trade .
Will you be kind enough to teach him ? '
` If he be clever , I do n't mind try , ' answer the Black Gallows Bird ; ` and , of course , if ANY one can turn him into a first-rate thief , it be I .
But if he be stupid , it be of no use at all ; I ca n't bear stupid people . '
` No , he be n't stupid , ' say the woman with a sigh .
` So to-night , after dark , I will send him to you . '
The Shifty Lad jump for joy when his mother tell him where she have be . '
I will become the best thief in all Erin ! '
he cry , and pay no heed when his mother shake her head and murmur something about ` the bridge of Dublin . '
Every evening after dark the Shifty Lad go to the home of the Black Gallows Bird , and many be the new trick he learn .
By-and-by he be allow to go out with the Bird and watch him at work , and at last there come a day when his master though that he have grow clever enough to help in a big robbery .
` There be a rich farmer up there on the hill , who have just sell all his fat cattle for much money and have buy some lean one which will cost him little .
Now it happen that , while he have receive the money for the fat cattle , he have not yet pay the price of the thin one , which he have in the cowhouse .
To-morrow he will go to the market with the money in his hand , so to-night we must get at the chest .
When all be quiet we will hide in the loft . '
There be no moon , and it be the night of Hallowe'en , and everyone be burn nut and catch apple in a tub of water with their hand tie , and play all sort of other game , till the Shifty Lad grow quite tired of wait for them to get to bed .
The Black Gallows Bird , who be more accustomed to the business , tuck himself up on the hay and go to sleep , tell the boy to wake him when the merry-makers have depart .
But the Shifty Lad , who could keep still no longer , creep down to the cowshed and loosen the head of the cattle which be tie , and they begin to kick each other and bellow , and make such a noise that the company in the farmhouse run out to tie them up again .
Then the Shifty Lad enter the room and pick up a big handful of nut , and return to the loft , where the Black Rogue be still sleep .
At first the Shifty Lad shut his eye too , but very soon he sit up , and take a big needle and thread from his pocket , he sew the hem of the Black Gallows Bird 's coat to a heavy piece of bullock 's hide that be hang at his back .
By this time the cattle be all tie up again , but a the people could not find their nut they sit round the fire and begin to tell story . '
I will crack a nut , ' say the Shifty Lad .
` You shall not , ' cry the Black Gallows Bird ; ` they will hear you . ' '
I do n't care , ' answer the Shifty Lad . '
I never spend Hallowe'en yet without crack a nut ' ; and he crack one .
` Some one be crack nut up there , ' say one of the merry-makers in the farmhouse .
` Come quickly , and we will see who it be . '
He speak loudly , and the Black Gallows Bird heard , and run out of the loft , drag the big leather hide after him which the Shifty Lad have sew to his coat .
` He be steal my hide ! '
shout the farmer , and they all dart after him ; but he be too swift for them , and at last he manage to tear the hide from his coat , and then he fly like a hare till he reach his old hiding-place .
But all this take a long time , and meanwhile the Shifty Lad get down from the loft , and search the house till he find the chest with the gold and silver in it , conceal behind a load of straw and cover with loaf of bread and a great cheese .
The Shifty Lad sling the money bag round his shoulder and take the bread and the cheese under his arm , then set out quietly for the Black Rogue 's house .

cry his master in great wrath .

I have bring what you want ' ; and he lay the thing he be carry down on the ground .

you be the good thief , ' say the Black Rogue 's wife ; and the Black Rogue add : ` Yes , it be you who be the clever boy ' ; and they divide the spoil and the Black Gallows Bird have one half and the Shifty Lad the other half .
A few week after that the Black Gallows Bird have news of a wedding that be to be hold near the town ; and the bridegroom have many friend and everybody send him a present .
Now a rich farmer who live up near the moor think that nothing be so useful to a young couple when they first begin to keep house a a fine fat sheep , so he bid his shepherd go off to the mountain where the flock be feed , and bring him back the best he could find .
And the shepherd choose out the large and fat of the sheep and the one with the white fleece ; then he tie it foot together and put it across his shoulder , for he have a long way to go .
That day , the Shifty Lad happen to be wander over the moor , when he saw the man with the sheep on his shoulder walking along the road which lead past the Black Rogue 's house .
The sheep be heavy and the man be in no hurry , so he come slowly and the boy know that he himself could easily get back to his master before the shepherd be even in sight . '
I will wager , ' he cry , a he push quickly through the bush which hide the cabin -- ' I will wager that I will steal the sheep from the man that be come before he pass here . '
` Will you indeed ? '
say the Gallows Bird . '
I will wager you a hundred silver piece that you can do nothing of the sort . '
` Well , I will try it , anyway , ' reply the boy , and disappear in the bush .
He run fast till he enter a wood through which the shepherd must go , and then he stop , and take off one of his shoe smear it with mud and set it in the path .
When this be do he slip behind a rock and wait .
Very soon the man come up , and see the shoe lie there , he stoop and look at it .
` It be a good shoe , ' he say to himself , ` but very dirty .
Still , if I have the fellow , I would be at the trouble of clean it ' ; so he throw the shoe down again and go on .
The Shifty Lad smile a he hear him , and , pick up the shoe , he creep round by a short way and lay the other shoe on the path .
A few minute after the shepherd arrive , and behold the second shoe lie on the path .

he exclaim when he saw it . '
I will go back and pick up the other one , and then I shall have a pair of good shoe , ' and he put the sheep on the grass and return to fetch the shoe .
Then the Shifty Lad put on his shoe , and , pick up the sheep , carry it home .
And the Black Rogue pay him the hundred mark of his wager .
When the shepherd reach the farmhouse that night he tell his tale to his master , who scold him for be stupid and careless , and bid him go the next day to the mountain and fetch him a kid , and he would send that a a wedding gift .
But the Shifty Lad be on the look-out , and hid himself in the wood , and the moment the man draw near with the kid on his shoulder begin to bleat like a sheep , and no one , not even the sheep 's own mother , could have tell the difference .
` Why , it must have get it foot loose , and have stray after all , ' think the man ; and he put the kid on the grass and hurry off in the direction of the bleating .
Then the boy run back and pick up the kid , and take it to the Black Gallows Bird .
The shepherd could hardly believe his eye when he return from seek the sheep and find that the kid have vanish .
He be afraid to go home and tell the same tale that he have tell yesterday ; so he search the wood through and through till night be nearly come .
Then he felt that there be no help for it , and he must go home and confess to his master .

Again the Shifty Lad , who be on the watch , perceive him pas by , and when he saw the man return with the great bull he cry to the Black Rogue : ` Be quick and come into the wood , and we will try to get the bull also . '

ask the Black Rogue .
` Oh , quite easily !
You hide yourself out there and baa like a sheep , and I will go in the other direction and bleat like a kid .
It will be all right , I assure you . '
The shepherd be walk slowly , drive the bull before him , when he suddenly hear a loud baa amongst the bush far away on one side of the path , and a feeble bleat answer it from the other side .
` Why , it must be the sheep and the kid that I lose , ' say he .
` Yes , surely it must ' ; and tie the bull hastily to a tree , he go off after the sheep and the kid , and search the wood till he be tire .
Of course by the time he come back the two thief have drive the bull home and kill him for meat , so the man be oblige to go to his master and confess that he have be trick again .
After this the Black Rogue and the Shifty Lad grow bolder and bolder , and stole great quantity of cattle and sell them and grow quite rich .
One day they be return from the market with a large sum of money in their pocket when they pass a gallows erect on the top of a hill .
` Let u stop and look at that gallows , ' exclaim the Shifty Lad . '
I have never see one so close before .
Yet some say that it be the end of all thief . '
There be no one in sight , and they carefully examine every part of it . '
I wonder how it feel to be hang , ' say the Shifty Lad . '
I should like to know , in case they ever catch me .
I 'll try first , and then you can do so . '
As he speak he fasten the loose cord about his neck , and when it be quite secure he tell the Black Rogue to take the other end of the rope and draw him up from the ground .
` When I be tire of it I will shake my leg , and then you must let me down , ' say he .
The Black Rogue draw up the rope , but in half a minute the Shifty Lad 's leg begin to shake , and he quickly let it down again .
` You ca n't imagine what a funny feeling hang give you , ' murmur the Shifty Lad , who look rather purple in the face and speak in an odd voice . '
I do n't think you have every try it , or you would n't have let me go up first .
Why , it be the pleasant thing I have ever do .
I be shake my leg from sheer delight , and if you have be there you would have shake your leg too . '
` Well , let me try , if it be so nice , ' answer the Black Rogue .
` But be sure you tie the knot securely , for I do n't want to fall down and break my neck . '
` Oh , I will see to that ! '
reply the Shifty Lad .
` When you be tire , just whistle , and I 'll let you down . '
So the Black Rogue be draw up , and as soon a he be as high a the rope would allow him to go the Shifty Lad call to him : ` Do n't forest to whistle when you want to come down ; but if you be enjoy yourself a I do , shake your leg . '
And in a moment the Black Rogue 's leg begin to shake and to kick , and the Shifty Lad stand below , watch him and laugh heartily .
` Oh , how funny you be !
If you could only see yourself !
Oh , you ARE funny !
But when you have have enough , whistle and you shall be let down ' ; and he rock again with laughter .
But no whistle come , and soon the leg cease to shake and to kick , for the Black Gallows Bird be dead , a the Shifty Lad intend he should be .
Then he go home to the Black Rogue 's wife , and tell her that her husband be dead , and that he be ready to marry her if she like .
But the woman have be fond of the Black Rogue , thief though he be , and she shrink from the Shifty Lad in horror , and set the people after him , and he have to fly to another part of the country where none knew of his doings .
Perhaps if the Shifty Lad 's mother know anything of this , she may have think that by this time her son might be tire of steal , and ready to try some honest trade .
But in reality he love the trick and danger , and life would have seem very dull without them .
So he go on just a before , and make friend whom he teach to be as wicked a himself , till they take to rob the king 's storehouse , and by the advice of the Wise Man the king send out soldier to catch the band of thief .
For a long while they try in vain to lay hand on them .
The Shifty Lad be too clever for them all , and if they lay trap he lay good one .
At last one night he steal upon some soldier while they be asleep in a barn and kill them , and persuade the villager that if THEY do not kill the other soldier before morning they would certainly be kill themselves .
Thus it happen that when the sun rise not a single soldier be alive in the village .
Of course this news soon reach the king 's ear , and he be very angry , and summon the Wise Man to take counsel with him .
And this be the counsel of the Wise Man -- that he should invite all the people in the countryside to a ball , and among them the bold and impudent thief would be sure to come , and would be sure to ask the king 's daughter to dance with him .
` Your counsel be good , ' say the king , who make his feast and prepare for his ball ; and all the people of the countryside be present , and the Shifty Lad come with them .
When everyone have eat and drink as much a they want they go into the ballroom .
There be a great throng , and while they be press through the doorway the Wise Man , who have a bottle of black ointment hidden in his robe , place a tiny dot on the cheek of the Shifty Lad near his ear .
The Shifty Lad felt nothing , but a he approach the king 's daughter to ask her to be his partner he catch sight of the black dot in a silver mirror .
Instantly he guess who have put it there and why , but he say nothing , and dance so beautifully that the princess be quite delight with him .
At the end of the dance he bow low to his partner and leave her , to mingle with the crowd that be fill the doorway .
As he pass the Wise Man he contrive not only to steal the bottle but to place two black dot on his face , and one on the face of twenty other men .
Then he slip the bottle back in the Wise Man 's robe .
By-and-by he go up to the king 's daughter again , and beg for the honour of another dance .
She consent , and while he be stoop to tie the ribbon on his shoe she take out from her pocket another bottle , which the Wizard have give her , and put a black dot on his cheek .
But she be not as skilful a the Wise Man , and the Shifty Lad felt the touch of her finger ; so as soon a the dance be over he contrive to place a second black dot on the face of the twenty men and two more on the Wizard , after which he slip the bottle into her pocket .
At length the ball come to an end , and then the king order all the door to be shut , and search make for a man with two black dot on his cheek .
The chamberlain go among the guest , and soon find such a man , but just a he be go to arrest him and bring him before the king his eye fell on another with the same mark , and another , and another , till he have count twenty -- besides the Wise Man -- on whose face be find spot .
Not know what to do , the chamberlain hurry back with his tale to the king , who immediately send for the Wise Man , and then for his daughter .
` The thief must have steal your bottle , ' say the king to the Wizard .
` No , my lord , it be here , ' answer the Wise Man , hold it out .
` Then he must have get yours , ' he cry , turn to his daughter .
` Indeed , father , it be safe in my pocket , ' reply she , take it out a she speak ; and they all three look at each other and remain silent .
` Well , ' say the king at last , ` the man who have do this be clever than most men , and if he will make himself know to me he shall marry the princess and govern half my kingdom while I be alive , and the whole of it when I be dead .
Go and announce this in the ballroom , ' he add to an attendant , ` and bring the fellow hither . '
So the attendant go into the ballroom and do a the king have bid him , when , to his surprise , not one man , but twenty , step forward , all with black dot on their face . '
I be the person you want , ' they all exclaim at once , and the attendant , a much bewilder a the chamberlain have be , desire them to follow him into the king 's presence .
But the question be too difficult for the king to decide , so he call together his council .
For hour they talk , but to no purpose , and in the end they hit upon a plan which they might just as well have think of at the beginning .
And this be the plan .
A child be to be bring to the palace , and next the king 's daughter would give her an apple .
Then the child be to take the apple and be lead into a room where the twenty men with the black dot be sit in a ring .
And to whomsoever the child give the apple , that man should marry the king 's daughter .
` Of course , ' say the king , ` it may not be the right man , after all , but then again it MAY be .
Anyhow , it be the best we can do . '
The princess herself lead the child into the room where the twenty men be now seat .
She stand in the centre of the ring for a moment , look at one man after another , and then hold out the apple to the Shifty Lad , who be twist a shaving of wood round his finger , and have the mouthpiece of a bagpipe hang from his neck .
` You ought not to have anything which the others have not get , ' say the chamberlain , who have accompany the princess ; and he bid the child stand outside for a minute , while he take away the shaving and the mouthpiece , and make the Shifty Lad change his place .
Then he call the child in , but the little girl know him again , and go straight up to him with the apple .
` This be the man whom the child have twice choose , ' say the chamberlain , sign to the Shifty Lad to kneel before the king .
` It be all quite fair ; we try it twice over . '
In this way the Shifty Lad win the king 's daughter , and they be marry the next day .
A few day later the bride and bridegroom be take a walk together , and the path lead down to the river , and over the river be a bridge .
` And what bridge may this be ? '
ask the Shifty Lad ; and the princess tell him that this be the bridge of Dublin .
` Is it indeed ? '
cry he .
` Well , now , many be the time that my mother have say , when I play her a trick , that my end would be that I should hang on the bridge of Dublin . '
` Oh , if you want to fulfil her prophecy , ' laugh the princess , ` you have only to let me tie my handkerchief round your ankle , and I will hold you a you hang over the wall of the bridge . '
` That would be fine fun , ' say he ; ` but you be not strong enough to hold me up . '
` Oh , yes , I be , ' say the princess ; ` just try . '
So at last he let her bind the handkerchief round his ankle and hang him over the wall , and they both laugh and jest at the strength of the princess .
` Now pull me up again , ' call he ; but a he speak a great cry arise that the palace be burn .
The princess turn round with a start , and let go her handkerchief , and the Shifty Lad fell , and strike his head on a stone , and die in an instant .
So his mother 's prophecy have come true , after all .
West Highland Tales .
The False Prince and the True The king have just awaken from his midday sleep , for it be summer , and everyone rise early and rest from twelve to three , a they do in hot country .
He have dress himself in cool white clothes , and be pass through the hall on his way to the council chamber , when a number of young noble suddenly appear before him , and one amongst them step forward and speak .
` Sire , this morning we be all play tennis in the court , the prince and this gentleman with the rest , when there break out some dispute about the game .
The prince lose his temper , and say many insulting thing to the other , who be play against him , till at length the gentleman whom you see there strike him violently in the face , so that the blood ran from his mouth and nose .
We be all so horrify at the sight , that we should most likely have kill the man then and there , for dare to lay hand on the prince , have not his grandfather the duke step between and command u to lay the affair before you . '
The king have listen attentively to the story , and when it be end he say : ' I suppose the prince have no arm with him , or else he would have use them ? '
` Yes , sire , he have arm ; he always carry a dagger in his belt .
But when he saw the blood pour from his face , he go to a corner of the court and begin to cry , which be the strange thing of all . '
On hear this the king walk to the window and stood for a few minute with his back to the room , where the company of young men remain silent .
Then he come back , his face white and stern . '
I tell you , ' he say , ` and it be the solemn truth , that I would rather you have tell me that the prince be dead , though he be my only son , than know that he would suffer such an injury without attempt to avenge it .
As for the gentleman who strike him , he will be bring before my judge , and will plead his own cause , but I hardly think he can escape death , after have assault the heir to the crown . '
The young man raise his head a if to reply , but the king would not listen , and command his guard to put him under arrest , add , however , that if the prisoner wish to visit any part of the city , he be at liberty to do so properly guard , and in fifteen day he would be bring to trial before the high judge in the land .
The young man leave the king 's presence , surround by soldier , and accompany by many of his friend , for he be a great favourite .
By their advice he spend the fourteen day that remain to him go about to seek counsel from wise men of all sort , a to how he might escape death , but no one could help him , for none could find any excuse for the blow he have give to the prince .
The fourteenth night have come , and in despair the prisoner go out to take his last walk through the city .
He wander on hardly know where he go , and his face be so white and desperate that none of his companion dare speak to him .
The sad little procession have pass some hour in this manner , when , near the gate of a monastery , an old woman appear round a corner , and suddenly stand before the young man .
She be bent almost double , and be so wizened and wrinkle that she look at least ninety ; only her eye be bright and quick a those of a girl .
` Sir , ' she say , ' I know all that have happen to you , and how you be seek if in any wise you can save your life .
But there be none that can answer that question save only I myself , if you will promise to do all I ask . '
At her word the prisoner felt a if a load have all at once be roll off him .
` Oh , save me , and I will do anything ! '
he cry .
` It be so hard to leave the world and go out into the darkness . '
` You will not need to do that , ' answer the old woman , ` you have only get to marry me , and you will soon be free . '
` Marry you ? '
exclaim he , ` but -- but -- I be not yet twenty , and you -- why , you must be a hundred at least !
Oh , no , it be quite impossible . '
He speak without thinking , but the flash of anger which dart from her eye make him feel uncomfortable .
However , all she say be : ` As you like ; since you reject me , let the crow have you , ' and hurry away down the street .
Left to himself , the full horror of his come death rush upon the young man , and he understand that he have throw away his sole chance of life .
Well , if he must , he must , he say to himself , and begin to run as fast a he could after the old crone , who by this time could scarcely be see , even in the moonlight .
Who would have believe a woman past ninety could walk with such speed ?
It seem more like fly !
But at length , breathless and exhaust , he reach her side , and gasp out : ` Madam , pardon me for my hasty word just now ; I be wrong , and will thankfully accept the offer you make me . '
` Ah , I think you would come to your sens , ' answer she , in rather an odd voice .
` We have no time to lose -- follow me at once , ' and they go on silently and swiftly till they stop at the door of a small house in which the priest live .
Before him the old woman bid the prisoner swear that she should be his wife , and this he do in the presence of witness .
Then , beg the priest and the guard to leave them alone for a little , she tell the young man what he be to do , when the next morning he be bring before the king and the judge .
The hall be full to overflow when the prisoner enter it , and all marvel at the brightness of his face .
The king inquired if he have any excuse to plead for the high treason he have commit by strike the heir to the throne , and , if so , to be quick in set it forth .
With a low bow the youth make answer in a clear voice : ' O my lord and gracious king , and you , noble and wise men of the land , I leave my cause without fear in your hand , know that you will listen and judge rightly , and that you will suffer me to speak to the end , before you give judgment .
` For four year , you , O king , have be marry to the queen and yet have no child , which grieve you greatly .
The queen saw this , and likewise that your love be go from her , and think night and day of some plan that might put an end to this evil .
At length , when you be away fight in distant country , she decide what she would do , and adopt in secret the baby of a poor quarryman , send a messenger to tell you that you have a son .
No one suspect the truth except a priest to whom the queen confess the truth , and in a few week she fell ill and die , leave the baby to be bring up a become a prince .
