And now , if your highness will permit me , I will speak of myself . '
` What you have already tell me , ' answer the king , ` be so strange that I can not imagine what more there be to tell , but go on with your story . '
` One day , shortly after the death of the queen , ' continue the young man , ` your highness be hunt , and outstrip all your attendant while chase the deer .
You be in a part of the country which you do not know , so see an orchard all pink and white with apple-blossoms , and a girl toss a ball in one corner , you go up to her to ask your way .
But when she turn to answer you , you be so struck with her beauty that all else flee from your mind .
Again and again you ride back to see her , and at length persuade her to marry you .
She only think you a poor knight , and agree that a you wish it , the marriage should be keep secret .
` After the ceremony you give her three ring and a charm with a cross on it , and then put her in a cottage in the forest , think to hide the matter securely .
` For some month you visit the cottage every week ; but a rebellion break out in a distant part of the kingdom , and call for your presence .
When next you ride up to the cottage , it be empty , and none could inform you whither your bride have go .
That , sire , I can now tell you , ' and the young man pause and look at the king , who colour deeply .
` She go back to her father the old duke , once your chamberlain , and the cross on her breast reveal at once who you be .
Fierce be his anger when he hear his daughter 's tale , and he vow that he would hide her safely from you , till the day when you would claim her publicly a your queen .
` By and bye I be bear , and be bring up by my grandfather in one of his great house .
Here be the ring you give to my mother , and here be the cross , and these will prove if I be your son or not . '
As he speak the young man lay the jewel at the foot of the king , and the noble and the judge press round to examine them .
The king alone do not move from his seat , for he have forget the hall of justice and all about him , and saw only the apple-orchard , a it be twenty year ago , and the beautiful girl playing at ball .
A sudden silence round him make him look up , and he find the eye of the assembly fix on him .
` It be true ; it be he who be my son , and not the other , ' he say with an effort , ` and let every man present swear to acknowledge him a king , after my death . '
Therefore one by one they all kneel before him and take the oath , and a message be send to the false prince , forbid him ever again to appear at court , though a handsome pension be grant him .
At last the ceremony be over , and the king , sign to his newly find son to follow him , rise and go into another room .
` Tell me how you know all that , ' he say , throw himself into a carved chair fill with crimson cushion , and the prince tell of his meeting with the old woman who have bring him the jewel from his mother , and how he have swear before a priest to marry her , though he do not want to do it , on account of the difference in their age , and besides , he would rather receive a bride choose by the king himself .
But the king frown , and answer sharply : ` You swear to marry her if she save your life , and , come what may , you must fulfil your promise . '
Then , strike a silver shield that hang close by , he say to the equerry who appear immediately : ` Go and seek the priest who live near the door of the prison , and ask him where you can find the old woman who visit him last night ; and when you have find her , bring her to the palace . '
It take some time to discover the whereabouts of the old woman , but at length it be accomplish , and when she arrive at the palace with the equerry , she be receive with royal honour , a become the bride of the prince .
The guard look at each other with astonished eye , a the wizened creature , bow with age , pass between their line ; but they be more amazed still at the lightness of her step a she skip up the step to the great door before which the king be stand , with the prince at his side .
If they both felt a shock at the appearance of the age lady they do not show it , and the king , with a grave bow , take her band , and lead her to the chapel , where a bishop be wait to perform the marriage ceremony .
For the next few week little be see of the prince , who spend all his day in hunting , and try to forget the old wife at home .
As for the princess , no one trouble himself about her , and she pass the day alone in her apartment , for she have absolutely decline the service of the ladies-in-waiting whom the king have appoint for her .
One night the prince return after a longer chase than usual , and he be so tired that he go up straight to bed .
Suddenly he be awaken by a strange noise in the room , and suspect that a robber might have steal in , he jump out of bed , and seize his sword , which lay ready to his hand .
Then he perceive that the noise proceed from the next room , which belong to the princess , and be light by a burning torch .
Creeping softly to the door , he peep through it , and behold her lie quietly , with a crown of gold and pearl upon her head , her wrinkle all go , and her face , which be white than the snow , as fresh a that of a girl of fourteen .
Could that really be his wife -- that beautiful , beautiful creature ?
The prince be still gaze in surprise when the lady open her eye and smile at him .
` Yes , I really be your wife , ' she say , a if she have guess his thought , ` and the enchantment be end .
Now I must tell you who I be , and what befell to cause me to take the shape of an old woman .
` The king of Granada be my father , and I be bear in the palace which overlook the plain of the Vega .
I be only a few month old when a wicked fairy , who have a spite against my parent , cast a spell over me , bend my back and wrinkling my skin till I look a if I be a hundred year old , and make me such an object of disgust to everyone , that at length the king order my nurse to take my away from the palace .
She be the only person who care about me , and we live together in this city on a small pension allow me by the king .
` When I be about three an old man arrive at our house , and beg my nurse to let him come in and rest , a he could walk no longer .
She saw that he be very ill , so put him to bed and take such care of him that by and bye he be as strong a ever .
In gratitude for her goodness to him , he tell her that he be a wizard and could give her anything she choose to ask for , except life or death , so she answer that what she long for most in the world be that my wrinkled skin should disappear , and that I should regain the beauty with which I be bear .
To this he reply that a my misfortune result from a spell , this be rather difficult , but he would do his best , and at any rate he could promise that before my fifteenth birthday I should be free from the enchantment if I could get a man who would swear to marry me a I be .
` As you may suppose , this be not easy , a my ugliness be such that no one would look at me a second time .
My nurse and I be almost in despair , a my fifteenth birthday be draw near , and I have never so much a speak to a man .
At last we receive a visit from the wizard , who tell u what have happen at court , and your story , bid me to put myself in your way when you have lose all hope , and offer to save you if you would consent to marry me .
` That be my history , and now you must beg the king to send messenger at once to Granada , to inform my father of our marriage , and I think , ' she add with a smile , ` that he will not refuse u his blessing . '
Adapted from the Portuguese .
The Jogi 's Punishment Once upon a time there come to the ancient city of Rahmatabad a jogi -LSB- FN # 1 : A Hindu holy man . -RSB-
of holy appearance , who take up his abode under a tree outside the city , where he would sit for day at a time fast from food and drink , motionless except for the finger that turn restlessly his string of bead .
The fame of such holiness a this soon spread , and daily the citizen would flock to see him , eager to get his blessing , to watch his devotion , or to hear his teaching , if he be in the mood to speak .
Very soon the rajah himself heard of the jogi , and begin regularly to visit him to seek his counsel and to ask his prayer that a son might be vouchsafe to him .
Days pass by , and at last the rajah become so possess with the thought of the holy man that he determine if possible to get him all to himself .
So he build in the neighbourhood a little shrine , with a room or two add to it , and a small courtyard closely wall up ; and , when all be ready , beseech the jogi to occupy it , and to receive no other visitor except himself and his queen and such pupil a the jogi might choose , who would hand down his teaching .
To this the jogi consent ; and thus he live for some time upon the king 's bounty , whilst the fame of his godliness grow day by day .
Now , although the rajah of Rahmatabad have no son , he possess a daughter , who a she grow up become the most beautiful creature that eye ever rest upon .
Her father have long before betroth her to the son of the neighbouring rajah of Dilaram , but a yet she have not be marry to him , and live the quiet life proper to a maiden of her beauty and position .
The princess have of course heard of the holy man and of his miracle and his fasting , and she be fill with curiosity to see and to speak to him ; but this be difficult , since she be not allow to go out except into the palace ground , and then be always closely guard .
However , at length she find an opportunity , and make her way one even alone to the hermit 's shrine .
Unhappily , the hermit be not really as holy a he seem ; for no sooner do he see the princess than he fell in love with her wonderful beauty , and begin to plot in his heart how he could win her for his wife .
But the maiden be not only beautiful , she be also shrewd ; and as soon a she read in the glance of the jogi the love that fill his soul , she spring to her foot , and , gather her veil about her , run from the place as fast a she could .
The jogi try to follow , but he be no match for her ; so , beside himself with rage at find that he could not overtake her , he fling at her a lance , which wound her in the leg .
The brave princess stoop for a second to pluck the lance out of the wound , and then run on until she find herself safe at home again .
There she bath and bind up the wound secretly , and tell no one how naughty she have be , for she know that her father would punish her severely .
Next day , when the king go to visit the jogi , the holy man would neither speak to nor look at him .
` What be the matter ? '
ask the king .
` Wo n't you speak to me to-day ? ' '
I have nothing to say that you would care to hear , ' answer the jogi .
` Why ? '
say the king .
` Surely you know that I value all that you say , whatever it may be . '
But still the jogi sit with his face turn away , and the more the king press him the more silent and mysterious he become .
At last , after much persuasion , he say : ` Let me tell you , then , that there be in this city a creature which , if you do not put an end to it , will kill every single person in the place . '
The king , who be easily frighten , grow pale .
` What ? '
he gasp -- ` what be this dreadful thing ?
How be I to know it and to catch it ?
Only counsel me and help me , and I will do all that you advise . '
` Ah ! '
reply the jogi , ` it be indeed dreadful .
It be in the shape of a beautiful girl , but it be really an evil spirit .
Last evening it come to visit me , and when I look upon it it beauty fade into hideousness , it teeth become horrible fang , it eye glare like coal of fire , great claw spring from it slender finger , and be I not what I be it might have consume me . '
The king could hardly speak from alarm , but at last he say : ` How be I to distinguish this awful thing when I see it ? '
` Search , ' say the jogi , ` for a lovely girl with a lance wound in her leg , and when she be found secure her safely and come and tell me , and I will advise you what to do next . '
Away hurry the king , and soon set all his soldier scour the country for a girl with a lance wound in her left .
For two day the search go on , and then it be somehow discover that the only person with a lance wound in the leg be the princess herself .
The king , greatly agitate , go off to tell the jogi , and to assure him that there must be some mistake .
But of course the jogi be prepare for this , and have his answer ready .
` She be not really your daughter , who be steal away at her birth , but an evil spirit that have take her form , ' say he solemnly .
` You can do what you like , but if you do n't take my advice she will kill you all . '
And so solemn he appear , and so unshaken in his confidence , that the king 's wisdom be blind , and he declare that he would do whatever the jogi advise , and believe whatever he say .
So the jogi direct him to send him secretly two carpenter ; and when they arrive he set them to make a great chest , so cunningly jointed and put together that neither air nor water could penetrate it .
There and then the chest be make , and , when it be ready , the jogi bid the king to bring the princess by night ; and they two thrust the poor little maiden into the chest and fasten it down with long nail , and between them carry it to the river and push it out into the stream .
As soon a the jogi get back from this deed he call two of his pupil , and pretend that it have be reveal to him that there should be find float on the river a chest with something of great price within it ; and he bid them go and watch for it at such a place far down the stream , and when the chest come slowly along , bob and turn in the tide , they be to seize it and secretly and swiftly bring it to him , for he be now determine to put the princess to death himself .
The pupil set off at once , wonder at the strangeness of their errand , and still more at the holiness of the jogi to whom such secret be reveal .
It happen that , a the next morning be dawn , the gallant young prince of Dilaram be hunt by the bank of the river , with a great following of wazirs , attendant , and huntsman , and a he ride he saw float on the river a large chest , which come slowly along , bob and turn in the tide .
Raising himself in his saddle , he give an order , and half a dozen men plunge into the water and draw the chest out on to the river bank , where every one crowd around to see what it could contain .
The prince be certainly not the least curious among them ; but he be a cautious young man , and , a he prepare to open the chest himself , he bid all but a few stand back , and these few to draw their sword , so a to be prepare in case the chest should hold some evil beast , or djinn , or giant .
When all be ready and expectant , the prince with his dagger force open the lid and flung it back , and there lay , live and breathing , the most lovely maiden he have ever see in his life .
Although she be half stifle from her confinement in the chest , the princess speedily revive , and , when she be able to sit up , the prince begin to question her a to who she be and how she come to be shut up in the chest and set afloat upon the water ; and she , blush and tremble to find herself in the presence of so many stranger , tell him that she be the princess of Rahmatabad , and that she have be put into the chest by her own father .
When he on his part tell her that he be the prince of Dilaram , the astonishment of the young people be unbounded to find that they , who have be betroth without ever have see one another , should have actually meet for the first time in such strange circumstance .
In fact , the prince be so move by her beauty and modest way that he call up his wazirs and demand to be marry at once to this lovely lady who have so completely win his heart .
And marry they be then and there upon the river bank , and go home to the prince 's palace , where , when the story be tell , they be welcome by the old rajah , the prince 's father , and the remainder of the day be give over to feast and rejoice .
But when the banquet be over , the bride tell her husband that now , on the threshold of their married life , she have more to relate of her adventure than he have give her the opportunity to tell a yet ; and then , without hide anything , she inform him of all that happen to her from the time she have steal out to visit the wicked jogi .
In the morning the prince call his chief wazir and order him to shut up in the chest in which the princess have be find a great monkey that live chain up in the palace , and to take the chest back to the river and set it afloat once more and watch what become of it .
So the monkey be catch and put into the chest , and some of the prince 's servant take it down to the river and push it off into the water .
Then they follow secretly a long way off to see what become of it .
Meanwhile the jogi 's two pupil watch and watch for the chest until they be nearly tire of watching , and be begin to wonder whether the jogi be right after all , when on the second day they spy the great chest come float on the river , slowly bobbing and turning in the tide ; and instantly a great joy and exultation seize them , for they think that here indeed be further proof of the wonderful wisdom of their master .
With some difficulty they secure the chest , and carry it back a swiftly and secretly a possible to the jogi 's house .
As soon a they bring in the chest , the jogi , who have be get very cross and impatient , tell them to put it down , and to go outside whilst he open the magic chest .
` And even if you hear cry and sound , however alarm , you must on no account enter , ' say the jogi , walk over to a closet where lay the silken cord that be to strangle the princess .
And the two pupil do a they be tell , and go outside and shut close all the door .
Presently they hear a great outcry within and the jogi 's voice cry aloud for help ; but they dare not enter , for have they not be tell that whatever the noise , they must not come in ?
So they sit outside , wait and wondering ; and at last all grow still and quiet , and remain so for such a long time that they determine to enter and see if all be well .
No sooner have they open the door lead into the courtyard than they be nearly upset by a huge monkey that come leap straight to the doorway and escape past them into the open field .
Then they step into the room , and there they saw the jogi 's body lie torn to piece on the threshold of his dwelling !
Very soon the story spread , a story will , and reach the ear of the princess and her husband , and when she know that her enemy be dead she make her peace with her father .
From Major Campbell , Feroshepore .
The Heart of a Monkey A long time ago a little town make up of a collection of low hut stand in a tiny green valley at the foot of a cliff .
Of course the people have take great care to build their house out of reach of the high tide which might be drive on shore by a west wind , but on the very edge of the town there have spring up a tree so large that half it bough hung over the hut and the other half over the deep sea right under the cliff , where shark love to come and splash in the clear water .
The branch of the tree itself be laden with fruit , and every day at sunrise a big grey monkey might have be see sit in the topmost branch have his breakfast , and chatter to himself with delight .
After he have eat all the fruit on the town side of the tree the monkey swung himself along the branch to the part which hung over the water .
While he be look out for a nice shady place where he might perch comfortably he notice a shark watch him from below with greedy eye .
` Can I do anything for you , my friend ? '
ask the monkey politely .
` Oh !
if you only would throw me down some of those delicious thing , I should be so grateful , ' answer the shark .
` After you have live on fish for fifty year you begin to feel you would like a change .
And I be so very , very tired of the taste of salt . '
` Well , I do n't like salt myself , ' say the monkey ; ` so if you will open your mouth I will throw this beautiful juicy kuyu into it , ' and , a he speak , he pull one off the branch just over his head .
But it be not so easy to hit the shark 's mouth a he suppose , even when the creature have turn on his back , and the first kuyu only struck one of his teeth and roll into the water .
However , the second time the monkey have good luck , and the fruit fell right in .
` Ah , how good ! '
cry the shark .
` Send me another , please . '
And the monkey grow tire of pick the kuyu long before the shark be tire of eat them .
` It be get late , and I must be go home to my child , ' he say , at length , ` but if you be here at the same time to-morrow I will give you another treat . '
` Thank you , thank you , ' say the shark , show all his great ugly teeth a he grin with delight ; ` you ca n't guess how happy you have make me , ' and he swim away into the shadow , hop to sleep away the time till the monkey come again .
For week the monkey and the shark breakfast together , and it be a wonder that the tree have any fruit left for them .
They become fast friend , and tell each other about their home and their child , and how to teach them all they ought to know .
By and bye the monkey become rather discontent with his green house in a grove of palm beyond the town , and long to see the strange thing under the sea which he have hear of from the shark .
The shark perceive this very clearly , and describe great marvel , and the monkey a he listen grow more and more gloomy .
Matters be in this state when one day the shark say : ' I really hardly know how to thank you for all your kindness to me during these week .
Here I have nothing of my own to offer you , but if you would only consent to come home with me , how gladly would I give you anything that might happen to take your fancy . ' '
I should like nothing well , ' cry the monkey , his teeth chatter , a they always do when he be pleased .
` But how could I get there ?
Not by water .
Ugh !
It make me ill to think of it ! '
` Oh !
do n't let that trouble you , ' reply the shark , ` you have only to sit on my back and I will undertake that not a drop of water shall touch you . '
So it be arrange , and directly after breakfast next morning the shark swam close up under the tree and the monkey drop neatly on his back , without even a splash .
After a few minute -- for at first he felt a little frighten at his strange position -- the monkey begin to enjoy himself vastly , and ask the shark a thousand question about the fish and the sea-weeds and the oddly-shaped thing that float past them , and a the shark always give him some sort of answer , the monkey never guess that many of the object they saw be a new to his guide a to himself .
The sun have rise and set six time when the shark suddenly say , ` My friend , we have now perform half our journey , and it be time that I should tell you something . '
` What be it ? '
ask the monkey .
` Nothing unpleasant , I hope , for you sound rather grave ? '
` Oh , no !
Nothing at all .
It be only that shortly before we leave I hear that the sultan of my country be very ill , and that the only thing to cure him be a monkey 's heart . '
` Poor man , I be very sorry for him , ' reply the monkey ; ` but you be unwise not to tell me till we have start . '
` What do you mean ? '
ask the shark ; but the monkey , who now understand the whole plot , do not answer at once , for he be consider what he should say .
` Why be you so silent ? '
inquire the shark again . '
I be think what a pity it be you do not tell me while I be still on land , and then I would have bring my heart with me . '
` Your heart !
Why be n't your heart here ? '
say the shark , with a puzzled expression .
` Oh , no !
Of course not .
Is it possible you do n't know that when we leave home we always hang up our heart on tree , to prevent their be troublesome ?
However , perhaps you wo n't believe that , and will just think I have invent it because I be afraid , so let u go on to your country as fast a we can , and when we arrive you can look for my heart , and if you find it you can kill me . '
The monkey spoke in such a calm , indifferent way that the shark be quite deceive , and begin to wish he have not be in such a hurry .
` But there be no use go on if your heart be not with you , ' he say at last .
` We have well turn back to the town , and then you can fetch it . '
Of course , this be just what the monkey want , but he be careful not to seem too pleased .
` Well , I do n't know , ' he remark carelessly , ` it be such a long way ; but you may be right . ' '
I be sure I be , ' answer the shark , ` and I will swim as quickly a I can , ' and so he do , and in three day they catch sight of the kuyu tree hanging over the water .
With a sigh of relief the monkey catch hold of the near branch and swung himself up .
` Wait for me here , ' he call out to the shark . '
I be so hungry I must have a little breakfast , and then I will go and look for my heart , ' and he go far and far into the branch so that the shark could not see him .
Then he curl himself up and go to sleep .
` Are you there ? '
cry the shark , who be soon tire of swim about under the cliff , and be in haste to be go .
The monkey awoke with a start , but do not answer .
` Are you there ? '
call the shark again , loud than before , and in a very cross voice .
` Oh , yes .
I be here , ' reply the monkey ; ` but I wish you have not waken me up .
I be have such a nice nap . '
` Have you get it ? '
ask the shark .
` It be time we be go . '
` Going where ? '
inquire the monkey .
` Why , to my country , of course , with your heart .
You CA N'T have forget ! '
` My dear friend , ' answer the monkey , with a chuckle , ' I think you must be go a little mad .
Do you take me for a washerman 's donkey ? '
` Do n't talk nonsense , ' exclaim the shark , who do not like be laugh at .
` What do you mean about a washerman 's donkey ?
And I wish you would be quick , or we may be too late to save the sultan . '
` Did you really never hear of the washerman 's donkey ? '
ask the monkey , who be enjoy himself immensely .
` Why , he be the beast who have no heart .
And a I be not feeling very well , and be afraid to start while the sun be so high l I should get a sunstroke , if you like , I will come a little nearer and tell you his story . '
` Very well , ' say the shark sulkily , ` if you wo n't come , I suppose I may as well listen to that a do nothing . '
So the monkey begin . '
A washerman once live in the great forest on the other side of the town , and he have a donkey to keep him company and to carry him wherever he want to go .
For a time they get on very well , but by and bye the donkey grow lazy and ungrateful for her master 's kindness , and run away several mile into the heart of the forest , where she do nothing but eat and eat and eat , till she grow so fat she could hardly move .
` One day a she be taste quite a new kind of grass and wonder if it be as good a what she have have for dinner the day before , a hare happen to pass by . '
`` Well , that be a fat creature , '' think she , and turn out of her path to tell the news to a lion who be a friend of hers .
Now the lion have be very ill , and be not strong enough to go hunt for himself , and when the hare come and tell him that a very fat donkey be to be find only a few hundred yard off , tear of disappointment and weakness fill his eye . '
`` What be the good of tell me that ? ''
he ask , in a weepy voice ; `` you know I can not even walk as far a that palm . '' '
`` Never mind , '' answer the hare briskly .
`` If you ca n't go to your dinner your dinner shall come to you , '' and nod a farewell to the lion she go back to the donkey . '
`` Good morning , '' say she , bow politely to the donkey , who lift her head in surprise .
`` Excuse my interrupting you , but I have come on very important business . '' '
`` Indeed , '' answer the donkey , `` it be most kind of you to take the trouble .
May I inquire what the business be ? '' '
`` Certainly , '' reply the hare .
`` It be my friend the lion who have hear so much of your charm and good quality that he have send me to beg that you will give him your paw in marriage .
He regret deeply that he be unable to make the request in person , but he have be ill and be too weak to move . '' '
`` Poor fellow !
How sad ! ''
say the donkey .
`` But you must tell him that I feel honour by his proposal , and will gladly consent to be Queen of the Beasts . '' '
`` Will you not come and tell him so yourself ? ''
ask the hare .
` Side by side they go down the road which lead to the lion 's house .
It take a long while , for the donkey be so fat with eat she could only walk very slowly , and the hare , who could have run the distance in about five minute , be oblige to creep along till she almost drop with fatigue at not be able to go at her own pace .
When at last they arrive the lion be sit up at the entrance , look very pale and thin .
The donkey suddenly grow shy and hang her head , but the lion put on his best manner and invite both his visitor to come in and make themselves comfortable .
` Very soon the hare get up and say , `` Well , a I have another engagement I will leave you to make acquaintance with your future husband , '' and wink at the lion she bound away .
` The donkey expect that as soon a they be leave alone the lion would begin to speak of their marriage , and where they should live , but a he say nothing she look up .
To her surprise and terror she saw him crouch in the corner , his eye glare with a red light , and with a loud roar he spring towards her .
But in that moment the donkey have have time to prepare herself , and jump on one side deal the lion such a hard kick that he shriek with the pain .
Again and again he strike at her with his claw , but the donkey could bite too , as well a the lion , who be very weak after his illness , and at last a well-planted kick knock him right over , and he roll on the floor , groan with pain .
The donkey do not wait for him to get up , but run away as fast a she could and be lose in the forest .
` Now the hare , who know quite well what would happen , have not go to do her business , but hide herself in some bush behind the cave , where she could hear quite clearly the sound of the battle .
When all be quiet again she creep gently out , and stole round the corner . '
`` Well , lion , have you kill her ? ''
ask she , run swiftly up the path . '
`` Killed her , indeed ! ''
answer the lion sulkily , `` it be she who have nearly kill me .
I never know a donkey could kick like that , though I take care she should carry away the mark of my claw . '' '
`` Dear me !
Fancy such a great fat creature be able to fight ! ''
cry the hare .
`` But do n't vex yourself .
Just lie still , and your wound will soon heal , '' and she bid her friend , good bye , and return to her family .
` Two or three week pass , and only bare place on the donkey 's back show where the lion 's claw have be , while , on his side , the lion have recover from his illness and be now as strong a ever .
He be begin to think that it be almost time for him to begin hunt again , when one morning a rustle be hear in the creeper outside , and the hare 's head peep through . '
`` Ah !
there be no need to ask how you be , '' she say .
`` Still you must n't overtire yourself , you know .
Shall I go and bring you your dinner ? '' '
`` If you will bring me that donkey I will tear it in two , '' cry the lion savagely , and the hare laugh and nod and go on her errand .
` This time the donkey be much further than before , and it take longer to find her .
At last the hare catch sight of four hoof in the air , and run towards them .
The donkey be lie on a soft cool bed of moss near a stream , roll herself backwards and forward from pleasure . '
`` Good morning , '' say the hare politely , and the donkey get slowly on to her leg , and look to see who her visitor could be . '
`` Oh , it be you , be it ? ''
she exclaim .
`` Come and have a chat .
What news have you get ? '' '
`` I must n't stay , '' answer the hare ; `` but I promise the lion to beg you to pay him a visit , a he be not well enough to call on you . '' '
`` Well , I do n't know , '' reply the donkey gloomily , `` the last time we go he scratch me very badly , and really I be quite afraid . '' '
`` He be only try to kiss you , '' say the hare , `` and you bite him , and of course that make him cross . '' '
`` If I be sure of that , '' hesitate the donkey . '
`` Oh , you may be quite sure , '' laugh the hare .
`` I have a large acquaintance among lion .
But let u be quick , '' and rather unwillingly the donkey set out .
` The lion saw them come and hid himself behind a large tree .
As the donkey go past , follow by the hare , he spring out , and with one blow of his paw stretch the poor foolish creature dead before him . '
`` Take this meat and skin it and roast it , '' he say to the hare ; `` but my appetite be not so good a it be , and the only part I want for myself be the heart .
The rest you can either eat yourself or give away to your friend . '' '
`` Thank you , '' reply the hare , balance the donkey on her back as well a she be able , and though the leg trail along the ground she manage to drag it to an open space some distance off , where she make a fire and roast it .
As soon a it be cook the hare take out the heart and have just finish eat it when the lion , who be tire of wait , come up . '
`` I be hungry , '' say he .
`` Bring me the creature 's heart ; it be just what I want for supper . '' '
`` But there be no heart , '' answer the hare , look up at the lion with a puzzled face . '
`` What nonsense ! ''
say the lion .
`` As if every beast have not get a heart .
What do you mean ? '' '
`` This be a washerman 's donkey , '' reply the hare gravely . '
`` Well , and suppose it be ? '' '
`` Oh , fie ! ''
exclaim the hare .
`` You , a lion and a grown-up person , and ask question like that .
If the donkey have have a heart would she be here now ?
The first time she come she know you be try to kill her , and run away .
Yet she come back a second time .
Well , if she have have a heart would she have come back a second time ?
Now would she ? ''
` And the lion answer slowly , `` No , she would not . ''
` So you think I be a washerman 's donkey ? '
say the monkey to the shark , when the story be end .
` You be wrong ; I be not .
And a the sun be get low in the sky , it be time for you to begin your homeward journey .
You will have a nice cool voyage , and I hope you will find the sultan well .
Farewell ! '
And the monkey disappear among the green branch , and be go .
From ` Swahili Tales , ' by Edward Steere , LL.D .
The Fairy Nurse There be once a little farmer and his wife living near Coolgarrow .
They have three child , and my story happen while the young be a baby .
The wife be a good wife enough , but her mind be all on her family and her farm , and she hardly ever go to her knee without fall asleep , and she think the time spend in the chapel be twice as long a it need be .
So , friend , she let her man and her two child go before her one day to Mass , while she call to consult a fairy man about a disorder one of her cow have .
She be late at the chapel , and be sorry all the day after , for her husband be in grief about it , and she be very fond of him .
Late that night he be waken up by the cry of his child call out ` Mother !
Mother ! '
When he sit up and rub his eye , there be no wife by his side , and when he ask the little one what be become of their mother , they say they saw the room full of nice little men and woman , dress in white and red and green , and their mother in the middle of them , go out by the door a if she be walk in her sleep .
Out he run , and search everywhere round the house but , neither tale nor tidings do he get of her for many a day .
Well , the poor man be miserable enough , for he be a fond of his woman a she be of him .
It use to bring the salt tear down his cheek to see his poor child neglect and dirty , a they often be , and they 'd be bad enough only for a kind neighbour that use to look in whenever she could spare time .
The infant be away with a nurse .
About six week after -- just a he be go out to his work one morning -- a neighbour , that use to mind woman when they be ill , come up to him , and keep step by step with him to the field , and this be what she tell him .
` Just a I be fall asleep last night , I hear a horse 's tramp on the grass and a knock at the door , and there , when I come out , be a fine-looking dark man , mount on a black horse , and he tell me to get ready in all haste , for a lady be in great want of me .
As soon a I put on my cloak and thing , he take me by the hand , and I be sit behind him before I felt myself stir .
`` Where be we go , sir ? ''
say I . `` You 'll soon know , '' say he ; and he draw his finger across my eye , and not a ray could I see .
I keep a tight grip of him , and I little knew whether he be go backwards or forward , or how long we be about it , till my hand be take again , and I felt the ground under me .
The finger go the other way across my eye , and there we be before a castle door , and in we go through a big hall and great room all paint in fine green colour , with red and gold band and ornament , and the fine carpet and chair and table and window curtain , and grand lady and gentleman walk about .
At last we come to a bedroom , with a beautiful lady in bed , with a fine bouncing boy beside her .
The lady clap her hand , and in come the Dark Man and kiss her and the baby , and praise me , and give me a bottle of green ointment to rub the child all over .
` Well , the child I rub , sure enough ; but my right eye begin to smart , and I put up my finger and give it a rub , and then star , for never in all my life be I so frighten .
The beautiful room be a big , rough cave , with water ooze over the edge of the stone and through the clay ; and the lady , and the lord , and the child weazened , poverty-bitten creature -- nothing but skin and bone -- and the rich dress be old rag .
I do n't let on that I find any difference , and after a bit say the Dark Man , `` Go before me to the hall door , and I will be with you in a few moment , and see you safe home . ''
Well , just a I turn into the outside cave , who should I see watch near the door but poor Molly .
She look round all terrify , and say she to me in a whisper , `` I 'm bring here to nurse the child of the king and queen of the fairy ; but there be one chance of save me .
All the court will pass the cross near Templeshambo next Friday night , on a visit to the fairy of Old Ross .
If John can catch me by the hand or cloak when I ride by , and have courage not to let go his grip , I 'll be safe .
Here 's the king .
Do n't open your mouth to answer .
I saw what happen with the ointment . ''
` The Dark Man do n't once cast his eye towards Molly , and he seem to have no suspicion of me .
When we come out I look about me , and where do you think we be but in the dyke of the Rath of Cromogue .
I be on the horse again , which be nothing but a big rag-weed , and I be in dread every minute I 'd fall off ; but nothing happen till I find myself in my own cabin .
The king slip five guinea into my hand as soon a I be on the ground , and thank me , and bid me good night .
I hope I 'll never see his face again .
I get into bed , and could n't sleep for a long time ; and when I examine my five guinea this morning , that I leave in the table drawer the last thing , I find five withered leaf of oak -- bad luck to the giver ! '
Well , you may all think the fright , and the joy , and the grief the poor man be in when the woman finish her story .
They talk and they talk , but we need n't mind what they say till Friday night come , when both be stand where the mountain road cross the one go to Ross .
There they stand , look towards the bridge of Thuar , in the dead of the night , with a little moonlight shin from over Kilachdiarmid .
At last she give a start , and `` By this and by that , '' say she , `` here they come , bridle jingle and feather toss ! ''
He look , but could see nothing ; and she stand tremble and her eye wide open , look down the way to the ford of Ballinacoola .
`` I see your wife , '' say she , `` rid on the outside just so a to rub against u .
We 'll walk on quietly , a if we suspect nothing , and when we be pass I 'll give you a shove .
If you do n't do YOUR duty then , woe be with you ! ''
Well , they walk on easy , and the poor heart beat in both their breast ; and though he could see nothing , he hear a faint jingle and trampling and rustling , and at last he get the push that she promise .
He spread out his arm , and there be his wife 's waist within them , and he could see her plain ; but such a hullabulloo rise a if there be an earthquake , and he find himself surround by horrible-looking thing , roar at him and strive to pull his wife away .
But he make the sign of the cross and bid them begone in God 's name , and hold his wife a if it be iron his arm be make of .
Bedad , in one moment everything be as silent a the grave , and the poor woman lie in a faint in the arm of her husband and her good neighbour .
Well , all in good time she be mind her family and her business again ; and I 'll go bail , after the fright she get , she spend more time on her knee , and avoid fairy men all the day of the week , and particularly on Sunday .
It be hard to have anything to do with the good people without get a mark from them .
My brave nurse do n't escape no more than another .
She be one Thursday at the market of Enniscorthy , when what do she see walk among the tub of butter but the Dark Man , very hungry-looking , and take a scoop out of one tub and out of another .
` Oh , sir , ' say she , very foolish , ' I hope your lady be well , and the baby . '
` Pretty well , thank you , ' say he , rather frighten like .
` How do I look in this new suit ? '
say he , get to one side of her . '
I ca n't see you plain at all , sir , ' say she .
` Well , now ? '
say he , get round her back to the other side .
` Musha , indeed , sir , your coat look no good than a withered dock-leaf . '
` Maybe , then , ' say he , ` it will be different now , ' and he strike the eye next him with a switch .
Friends , she never saw a glimmer after with that one till the day of her death .
` Legendary Fictions of the Irish Celts , ' by Patrick Kennedy .
A Lost Paradise In the middle of a great forest there live a long time ago a charcoal-burner and his wife .
They be both young and handsome and strong , and when they get marry , they think work would never fail them .
But bad time come , and they grow poor and poor , and the night in which they go hungry to bed become more and more frequent .
Now one even the king of that country be hunt near the charcoal-burner 's hut .
As he pass the door , he hear a sound of sobbing , and be a good-natured man he stop to listen , think that perhaps he might be able to give some help .
` Were there ever two people so unhappy ! '
say a woman 's voice .
` Here we be , ready to work like slave the whole day long , and no work can we get .
And it be all because of the curiosity of old mother Eve !
If she have only be like me , who never want to know anything , we should all have be as happy a king to-day , with plenty to eat , and warm clothes to wear .
Why -- ' but at this point a loud knock interrupt her lamentation .
` Who be there ? '
ask she .
` I ! '
reply somebody .
` And who be `` I '' ? '
` The king .
Let me in . '
Full of surprise the woman jump up and pull the bar away from the door .
As the king enter , he notice that there be no furniture in the room at all , not even a chair , so he pretend to be in too great a hurry to see anything around him , and only say ` You must not let me disturb you .
I have no time to stay , but you seem to be in trouble .
Tell me ; be you very unhappy ? '
` Oh , my lord , we can find no work and have eat nothing for two day ! '
answer she .
` Nothing remain for u but to die of hunger . '
` No , no , you sha n't do that , ' cry the king , ` or if you do , it will be your own fault .
You shall come with me into my palace , and you will feel a if you be in Paradise , I promise you .
In return , I only ask one thing of you , that you shall obey my order exactly . '
The charcoal-burner and his wife both star at him for a moment , a if they could hardly believe their ear ; and , indeed , it be not to be wonder at !
Then they find their tongue , and exclaim together : ` Oh , yes , yes , my lord !
we will do everything you tell u .
How could we be so ungrateful a to disobey you , when you be so kind ? '
The king smile , and his eye twinkle .
` Well , let u start at once , ' say he .
` Lock your door , and put the key in your pocket . '
The woman look a if she think this be needless , see it be quite , quite certain they would never come back .
But she dare not say so , and do a the king tell her .
After walk through the forest for a couple of mile , they all three reach the palace , and by the king 's order servant lead the charcoal-burner and his wife into room fill with beautiful thing such a they have never even dream of .
First they bath in green marble bath where the water look like the sea , and then they put on silken clothes that felt soft and pleasant .
When they be ready , one of the king 's special servant enter , and take them into a small hall , where dinner be lay , and this please them good than anything else .
They be just about to sit down to the table when the king walk in . '
I hope you have be attend to properly , ' say he , ` and that you will enjoy your dinner .
My steward will take care you have all you want , and I wish you to do exactly a you please .
Oh , by the bye , there be one thing !
You notice that soup-tureen in the middle of the table ?
Well , be careful on no account to lift the lid .
If once you take off the cover , there be an end of your good fortune . '
Then , bow to his guest , he leave the room .
` Did you hear what he say ? '
inquire the charcoal-burner in an awe-stricken voice .
` We be to have what we want , and do what we please .
Only we must not touch the soup-tureen . '
` No , of course we wo n't , ' answer the wife .
` Why should we wish to ?
But all the same it be rather odd , and one ca n't help wonder what be inside . '
For many day life go on like a beautiful dream to the charcoal-burner and his wife .
Their bed be so comfortable , they could hardly make up their mind to get up , their clothes be so lovely they could scarcely bring themselves to take them off ; their dinner be so good that they find it very difficult to leave off eat .
Then outside the palace be garden fill with rare flower and fruit and singing bird , or if they desire to go far , a golden coach , paint with wreath of forget-me-not and line with blue satin , await their order .
Sometimes it happen that the king come to see them , and he smile a he glance at the man , who be get rosy and plump each day .
But when his eye rest on the woman , they take on a look which seem to say ' I know it , ' though this neither the charcoal-burner nor his wife ever notice .
` Why be you so silent ? '
ask the man one morning when dinner have pass before his wife have uttered one word . '
A little while ago you use to be chatter all the day long , and now I have almost forget the sound of your voice . '
` Oh , nothing ; I do not feel inclined to talk , that be all ! '
She stop , and add carelessly after a pause , ` Do n't you ever wonder what be in that soup-tureen ? '
` No , never , ' reply the man .
` It be no affair of ours , ' and the conversation drop once more , but a time go on , the woman speak less and less , and seem so wretched that her husband grow quite frightened about her .
As to her food , she refuse one thing after another .
` My dear wife , ' say the man at last , ` you really must eat something .
What in the world be the matter with you ?
If you go on like this you will die . ' '
I would rather die than not know what be in that tureen , ' she burst forth so violently that the husband be quite startle .
` Is that it ? '
cry he ; ` be you make yourself miserable because of that ?
Why , you know we should be turn out of the palace , and send away to starve . '
` Oh no , we should n't .
The king be too good-natured .
Of course he do n't mean a little thing like this !
Besides , there be no need to lift the lid off altogether .
Just raise one corner so that I may peep .
We be quite alone : nobody will ever know . '
The man hesitate : it do seem a ` little thing , ' and if it be to make his wife content and happy it be well worth the risk .
So he take hold of the handle of the cover and raise it very slowly and carefully , while the woman stoop down to peep .
Suddenly she startle back with a scream , for a small mouse have spring from the inside of the tureen , and have nearly hit her in the eye .
Round and round the room it run , round and round they both run after it , knock down chair and vas in their effort to catch the mouse and put it back in the tureen .
In the middle of all the noise the door open , and the mouse run out between the foot of the king .
In one instant both the man and his wife be hide under the table , and to all appearance the room be empty .
` You may as well come out , ' say the king , ` and hear what I have to say . ' '
I know what it be , ' answer the charcoal-burner , hang his head .
The mouse have escape . ' '
A guard of soldier will take you back to your hut , ' say the king .
` Your wife have the key . '
` Were n't they silly ? '
cry the grandchild of the charcoal-burners when they hear the story .
` How we wish that we have have the chance !
WE should never have want to know what be in the soup-tureen ! '
From ` Litterature Orale de l'Auvergne , ' par Paul Sebillot .
How Brave Walter Hunted Wolves A little back from the high road there stand a house which be call ` Hemgard . '
Perhaps you remember the two beautiful mountain ash tree by the reddish-brown paling , and the high gate , and the garden with the beautiful barberry bush which be always the first to become grown in spring , and which in summer be weigh down with their beautiful berry .
Behind the garden there be a hedge with tall aspen which rustle in the morning wind , behind the hedge be a road , behind the road be a wood , and behind the wood the wide world .
But on the other side of the garden there be a lake , and beyond the lake be a village , and all around stretch meadow and field , now yellow , now green .
In the pretty house , which have white window-frames , a neat porch and clean step , which be always strew with finely-cut juniper leave , Walter 's parent live .
His brother Frederick , his sister Lotta , old Lena , Jonah , Caro and Bravo , Putte and Murre , and Kuckeliku .
Caro live in the dog house , Bravo in the stable , Putte with the stableman , Murre a little here and a little there , and Kuckeliku live in the hen house , that be his kingdom .
Walter be six year old , and he must soon begin to go to school .
He can not read yet , but he can do many other thing .
He can turn cartwheel , stand on his head , ride see-saw , throw snowball , play ball , crow like a cock , eat bread and butter and drink sour milk , tear his trouser , wear hole in his elbow , break the crockery in piece , throw ball through the windowpane , draw old men on important paper , walk over the flower-beds , eat himself sick with gooseberry , and be well after a whipping .
For the rest he have a good heart but a bad memory , and forget his father 's and his mother 's admonition , and so often get into trouble and meet with adventure , a you shall hear , but first of all I must tell you how brave he be and how he hunt wolf .
Once in the spring , a little before Midsummer , Walter hear that there be a great many wolf in the wood , and that please him .
He be wonderfully brave when he be in the midst of his companion or at home with his brother and sister , then he use often to say ` One wolf be nothing , there ought to be at least four . '
When he wrestle with Klas Bogenstrom or Frithiof Waderfelt and strike them in the back , he would say ` That be what I shall do to a wolf ! '
and when he shoot arrow at Jonas and they rattle against his sheepskin coat he would say : ` That be how I should shoot you if you be a wolf ! '
Indeed , some think that the brave boy boast a little ; but one must indeed believe him since he say so himself .
So Jonas and Lena use to say of him ` Look , there go Walter , who shoot the wolf . '
And other boy and girl would say ` Look , there go brave Walter , who be brave enough to fight with four . '
There be no one so fully convince of this a Walter himself , and one day he prepare himself for a real wolf hunt .
He take with him his drum , which have hole in one end since the time he have climb up on it to reach a cluster of rowan berry , and his tin sabre , which be a little broken , because he have with incredible courage fight his way through a whole unfriendly army of gooseberry bush .
He do not forget to arm himself quite to the teeth with his pop-gun , his bow , and his air-pistol .
He have a burnt cork in his pocket to blacken his moustache , and a red cock 's feather to put in his cap to make himself look fierce .
He have besides in his trouser pocket a clasp knife with a bone handle , to cut off the ear of the wolf as soon a he have kill them , for he think it would be cruel to do that while they be still live .
It be such a good thing that Jonas be go with corn to the mill , for Walter get a seat on the load , while Caro run bark beside them .
As soon a they come to the wood Walter look cautiously around him to see perchance there be a wolf in the bush , and he do not omit to ask Jonas if wolf be afraid of a drum .
` Of course they be ' -LRB- that be understood -RRB- say Jonas .
Thereupon Walter begin to beat his drum with all his might while they be go through the wood .
When they come to the mill Walter immediately ask if there have be any wolf in the neighbourhood lately .
` Alas !
yes , ' say the miller , ` last night the wolf have eat our fat ram there by the kiln not far from here . '
` Ah ! '
say Walter , ` do you think that there be many ? '
` We do n't know , ' answer the miller .
` Oh , it be all the same , ' say Walter . '
I only ask so that I should know if I should take Jonas with me . '
I could manage very well alone with three , but if there be more , I might not have time to kill them all before they run away . '
` In Walter 's place I should go quite alone , it be more manly , ' say Jonas .
` No , it be well for you to come too , ' say Walter .
` Perhaps there be many . '
` No , I have not time , ' say Jonas , ` and besides , there be sure not to be more than three .
Walter can manage them very well alone . '
` Yes , ' say Walter , ` certainly I could ; but , you see , Jonas , it might happen that one of them might bite me in the back , and I should have more trouble in kill them .
If I only know that there be not more than two I should not mind , for them I should take one in each hand and give them a good shaking , like Susanna once shake me . ' '
I certainly think that there will not be more than two , ' say Jonas , ` there be never more than two when they slay child and ram ; Walter can very well shake them without me . '
` But , you see , Jonas , ' say Walter , ` if there be two , it might still happen that one of them escape and bite me in the leg , for you see I be not so strong in the left hand a in the right .
You can very well come with me , and take a good stick in case there be really two .
Look , if there be only one , I shall take him so with both my hand and throw him live on to his back , and he can kick as much a he like , I shall hold him fast . '
` Now , when I really think over the thing , ' say Jonas , ' I be almost sure there will not be more than one .
What would two do with one ram ?
There will certainly not be more than one . '
` But you should come with me all the same , Jonas , ' say Walter .
` You see I can very well manage one , but I be not quite accustomed to wolf yet , and he might tear hole in my new trouser . '
` Well , just listen , ' say Jonas , ' I be begin to think that Walter be not so brave a people say .
First of all Walter would fight against four , and then against three , then two , and then one , and now Walter want help with one .
Such a thing must never be ; what would people say ?
Perhaps they would think that Walter be a coward ? '
` That 's a lie , ' say Walter , ' I be not at all frighten , but it be more amusing when there be two .
I only want someone who will see how I strike the wolf and how the dust fly out of his skin . '
` Well , then , Walter can take the miller 's little Lisa with him .
She can sit on a stone and look on , ' say Jonas .
` No , she would certainly be frighten , ' say Walter , ` and how would it do for a girl to go wolf-hunting ?
Come with me , Jonas , and you shall have the skin , and I will be content with the ear and the tail . '
` No , thank you , ' say Jonas , ` Walter can keep the skin for himself .
Now I see quite well that he be frighten .
Fie , shame on him ! '
This touch Walter 's pride very near . '
I shall show that I be not frighten , ' he say ; and so he take his drum , sabre , cock 's feather , clasp-knife , pop-gun and air-pistol , and go off quite alone to the wood to hunt wolf .
It be a beautiful evening , and the bird be sing in all the branch .
Walter go very slowly and cautiously .
At every step he look all round him to see if perchance there be anything lurk behind the stone .
He quite think something move away there in the ditch .
Perhaps it be a wolf .
` It be well for me to beat the drum a little before I go there , ' thought Walter .
Br-r-r , so he begin to beat his drum .
Then something move again .
Caw !
caw !
a crow fly up from the ditch .
Walter immediately regain courage .
` It be well I take my drum with me , ' he think , and go straight on with courageous step .
Very soon he come quite close to the kiln , where the wolf have kill the ram .
But the nearer he come the more dreadful he think the kiln look .
It be so gray and old .
Who know how many wolf there might be hide there ?
Perhaps the very one which kill the ram be still sit there in a corner .
Yes , it be not at all safe here , and there be no other people to be see in the neighbourhood .
It would be horrible to be eat up here in the daylight , think Walter to himself ; and the more he think about it the ugly and grayer the old kiln look , and the more horrible and dreadful it seem to become the food of wolf .
` Shall I go back and say that I strike one wolf and it escape ? '
thought Walter .
` Fie ! '
say his conscience , ` Do you not remember that a lie be one of the bad sin , both in the sight of God and man ?
If you tell a lie to-day and say you strike a wolf , to-morrow surely it will eat you up . '
` No , I will go to the kiln , ' thought Walter , and so he go .
But he do not go quite near .
He go only so near that he could see the ram 's blood which colour the grass red , and some tuft of wool which the wolf have tear from the back of the poor animal .
It look so dreadful . '
I wonder what the ram think when they eat him up , ' think Walter to himself ; and just then a cold shiver run through him from his collar right down to his boot .
` It be well for me to beat the drum , ' he think to himself again , and so he begin to beat it .
But it sound horrid , and an echo come out from the kiln that seem almost like the howl of a wolf .
The drumstick stiffen in Walter 's hand , and he think now they be come ... !
Yes , sure enough , just then a shaggy , reddish-brown wolf 's head look out from under the kiln !
What do Walter do now ?
Yes , the brave Walter who alone could manage four , throw his drum far away , take to his heel and ran , and run as fast a he could back to the mill .
But , ala !
the wolf run after him .
Walter look back ; the wolf be quick than he and only a few step behind him .
Then Walter run faster .
But fear get the good of him , he neither hear nor saw anything more .
He run over stick , stone and ditch ; he lose drum-sticks , sabre , bow , and air-pistol , and in his terrible hurry he trip over a tuft of grass .
There he lay , and the wolf jump on to him ... It be a gruesome tale !
Now you may well believe that it be all over with Walter and all his adventure .
That would have be a pity .
But do not be surprise if it be not quite so bad a that , for the wolf be quite a friendly one .
He certainly jump on to Walter , but he only shake his coat and rub his nose against his face ; and Walter shriek .
Yes , he shriek terribly !
Happily Jonas hear his cry of distress , for Walter be quite near the mill now , and he run and help him up .
` What have happen ? '
he ask .
` Why do Walter scream so terribly ? ' '
A wolf !
A wolf ! '
cry Walter , and that be all he could say .
` Where be the wolf ? '
say Jonas . '
I do n't see any wolf . '
` Take care , he be here , he have bite me to death , ' groan Walter .
Then Jonas begin to laugh ; yes , he laugh so that he nearly burst his skin belt .
Well , well , be that the wolf ?
Was that the wolf which Walter be to take by the neck and shake and throw down on it back , no matter how much it struggle ?
Just look a little close at him : he be your old friend , your own good old Caro .
I quite expect he find a leg of the ram in the kiln .
When Walter beat his drum , Caro creep out , and when Walter run away , Caro run after him , a he so often do when Walter want to romp and play .
` Down , Caro !
you ought to be rather ashamed to have put such a great hero to flight ! '
Walter get up feel very foolish .
` Down , Caro ! '
he say , both relieve and annoy .
` It be only a dog , then if it have be a wolf I certainly should have kill him ... ' ` If Walter would listen to my advice , and boast a little less , and do a little more , ' say Jonas , consolingly .
` Walter be not a coward , be he ? '
` I !
You shall see , Jonas , when we next meet a bear .
You see I like so much good to fight with bear . '
` Indeed ! '
laugh Jonas .
` Are you at it again ?
` Dear Walter , remember that it be only coward who boast ; a really brave man never talk of his bravery . '
From Z. Topelius .
The King of the Waterfalls When the young king of Easaidh Ruadh come into his kingdom , the first thing he think of be how he could amuse himself best .
The sport that all his life have pleased him best suddenly seem to have grow dull , and he want to do something he have never do before .
At last his face brighten . '
I know ! '
he say . '
I will go and play a game with the Gruagach . '
Now the Gruagach be a kind of wicked fairy , with long curly brown hair , and his house be not very far from the king 's house .
But though the king be young and eager , he be also prudent , and his father have tell him on his deathbed to be very careful in his dealing with the ` good people , ' a the fairy be call .
Therefore before go to the Gruagach the king seek out a wise man of the countryside . '
I be want to play a game with the curly-haired Gruagach , ' say he .
` Are you , indeed ? '
reply the wizard .
` If you will take my counsel , you will play with someone else . '
` No ; I will play with the Gruagach , ' persist the king .
` Well , if you must , you must , I suppose , ' answer the wizard ; ` but if you win that game , ask a a prize the ugly crop-headed girl that stand behind the door . ' '
I will , ' say the king .
So before the sun rise he get up and go to the house of the Gruagach , who be sit outside . '
O king , what have bring you here to-day ? '
ask the Gruagach .
` But right welcome you be , and more welcome will you be still if you will play a game with me . '
` That be just what I want , ' say the king , and they play ; and sometimes it seem a if one would win , and sometimes the other , but in the end it be the king who be the winner .
` And what be the prize that you will choose ? '
inquire the Gruagach .
` The ugly crop-headed girl that stand behind the door , ' reply the king .
` Why , there be twenty others in the house , and each fairer than she ! '
exclaim the Gruagach .
` Fairer they may be , but it be she whom I wish for my wife , and none other , ' and the Gruagach saw that the king 's mind be set upon her , so he enter his house , and bid all the maiden in it come out one by one , and pas before the king .
One by one they come ; tall and short , dark and fair , plump and thin , and each say ' I be she whom you want .
You will be foolish indeed if you do not take me . '
But he take none of them , neither short nor tall , dark nor fair , plump nor thin , till at the last the crop-headed girl come out .
` This be mine , ' say the king , though she be so ugly that most men would have turn from her .
` We will be marry at once , and I will carry you home . '
And marry they be , and they set forth across a meadow to the king 's house .
As they go , the bride stoop and pick a sprig of shamrock , which grow amongst the grass , and when she stand upright again her ugliness have all go , and the most beautiful woman that ever be see stand by the king 's side .
The next day , before the sun rise , the king sprang from his bed , and tell his wife he must have another game with the Gruagach .
` If my father lose that game , and you win it , ' say she , ` accept nothing for your prize but the shaggy young horse with the stick saddle . ' '
I will do that , ' answer the king , and he go .
` Does your bride please you ? '
ask the Gruagach , who be stand at his own door .
` Ah !
do she not ! '
answer the king quickly .
` Otherwise I should be hard indeed to please .
But will you play a game to-day ? ' '
I will , ' reply the Gruagach , and they play , and sometimes it seem a if one would win , and sometimes the other , but in the end the king be the winner .
` What be the prize that you will choose ? '
ask the Gruagach .
` The shaggy young horse with the stick saddle , ' answer the king , but he notice that the Gruagach hold his peace , and his brow be dark a he lead out the horse from the stable .
Rough be it mane and dull be it skin , but the king care nothing for that , and throw his leg over the stick saddle , ride away like the wind .
On the third morning the king get up as usual before dawn , and as soon a he have eat food he prepare to go out , when his wife stop him . '
I would rather , ' she say , ` that you do not go to play with the Gruagach , for though twice you have win yet some day he will win , and then he will put trouble upon you . '
` Oh !
I must have one more game , ' cry the king ; ` just this one . '
And he go off to the house of the Gruagach .
Joy fill the heart of the Gruagach when he saw him come , and without wait to talk they play their game .
Somehow or other , the king 's strength and skill have depart from him , and soon the Gruagach be the victor .
` Choose your prize , ' say the king , when the game be end , ` but do not be too hard on me , or ask what I can not give . '
` The prize I choose , ' answer the Gruagach , ` be that the crop-headed creature should take thy head and thy neck , if thou dost not get for me the Sword of Light that hang in the house of the king of the oak windows . ' '
I will get it , ' reply the young man bravely ; but as soon a he be out of sight of the Gruagach he pretend no more , and his face grow dark and his step lag .
` You have bring nothing with you to-night , ' say the queen , who be stand on the step await him .
She be so beautiful that the king be fain to smile when he look at her , but then he remember what have happen , and his heart grow heavy again .
` What be it ?
What be the matter ?
Tell me thy sorrow that I may bear it with thee , or , it may be , help thee ! '
Then the king tell her everything that have befall him , and she stroke his hair the while .
` That be nothing to grieve about , ' she say when the tale be finish .
` You have the best wife in Erin , and the best horse in Erin .
Only do a I bid you , and all will go well . '
And the king suffer himself to be comfort .
He be still sleep when the queen rise and dress herself , to make everything ready for her husband 's journey ; and the first place she go to be the stable , where she feed and water the shaggy brown horse and put the saddle on it .
Most people think this saddle be of wood , and do not see the little sparkle of gold and silver that be hide in it .
She strap it lightly on the horse 's back , and then lead it down before the house , where the king wait .
` Good luck to you , and victory in all your battle , ' she say , a she kiss him before he mount . '
I need not be tell you anything .
Take the advice of the horse , and see you obey it . '
So he wave his hand and set out on his journey , and the wind be not swift than the brown horse -- no , not even the March wind which race it and could not catch it .
But the horse never stop nor look behind , till in the dark of the night he reach the castle of the king of the oak window .
` We be at the end of the journey , ' say the horse , ` and you will find the Sword of Light in the king 's own chamber .
If it come to you without scrape or sound , the token be a good one .
At this hour the king be eat his supper , and the room be empty , so none will see you .
The sword have a knob at the end , and take heed that when you grasp it , you draw it softly out of it sheath .
Now go !
I will be under the window . '
Stealthily the young man crept along the passage , pause now and then to make sure that no man be follow him , and enter the king 's chamber .
A strange white line of light tell him where the sword be , and cross the room on tiptoe , he seize the knob , and draw it slowly out of the sheath .
The king could hardly breathe with excitement lest it should make some noise , and bring all the people in the castle run to see what be the matter .
But the sword slide swiftly and silently along the case till only the point be leave touch it .
Then a low sound be heard , a of the edge of a knife touch a silver plate , and the king be so startled that he nearly drop the knob .
` Quick !
quick ! '
cry the horse , and the king scramble hastily through the small window , and leapt into the saddle .
` He have hear and he will follow , ' say the horse ; ` but we have a good start , ' And on they speed , on and on , leave the wind behind them .
At length the horse slacken it pace .
` Look and see who be behind you , ' it say ; and the young man look . '
I see a swarm of brown horse race madly after u , ' he answer .
` We be swift than those , ' say the horse , and fly on again .
` Look again , O king !
Is anyone come now ? ' '
A swarm of black horse , and one have a white face , and on that horse a man be seat .
He be the king of the oak windows . '
` That be my brother , and swifter still than I , ' say the horse , ` and he will fly past me with a rush .
Then you must have your sword ready , and take off the head of the man who sit on him , a he turn and look at you .
And there be no sword in the world that will cut off his head , save only that one . ' '
I will do it , ' reply the king ; and he listen with all his might , till he judge that the white-faced horse be close to him .
Then he sit up very straight and make ready .
The next moment there be a rushing noise a of a mighty tempest , and the young man catch a glimpse of a face turn towards him .
Almost blindly he strike , not know whether he have kill or only wound the rider .
But the head roll off , and be catch in the brown horse 's mouth .
` Jump on my brother , the black horse , and go home as fast a you can , and I will follow as quickly a I may , ' cry the brown horse ; and leap forward the king alight on the back of the black horse , but so near the tail that he almost fell off again .
But he stretch out his arm and clutch wildly at the mane and pull himself into the saddle .
Before the sky be streak with red he be at home again , and the queen be sit wait till he arrive , for sleep be far from her eye .
Glad be she to see him enter , but she say little , only take her harp and sang softly the song which he love , till he go to bed , soothe and happy .
It be broad day when he wake , and he spring up say : ` Now I must go to the Gruagach , to find out if the spell he lay on me be loose . '
` Have a care , ' answer the queen , ` for it be not with a smile a on the other day that he will greet you .
Furiously he will meet you , and will ask you in his wrath if you have get the sword , and you will reply that you have get it .
Next he will want to know how you get it , and to this you must say that but for the knob you have not get it at all .
Then he will raise his head to look at the knob , and you must stab him in the mole which be on the right side of his neck ; but take heed , for if you miss the mole with the point of the sword , then my death and your death be certain .
He be brother to the king of the oak window , and sure will he be that the king must be head , or the sword would not be in your hand . '
After that she kiss him , and bid him good speed .
` Didst thou get the sword ? '
ask the Gruagach , when they meet in the usual place . '
I get the sword . '
` And how didst thou get it ? '
` If it have not have a knob on the top , then I have not get it , ' answer the king .
` Give me the sword to look at , ' say the Gruagach , peer forward ; but like a flash the king have draw it from under his nose and pierce the mole , so that the Gruagach roll over on the ground .
` Now I shall be at peace , ' think the king .
But he be wrong , for when he reach home he find his servant tie together back to back with cloth bind round their mouth , so that they could not speak .
He hasten to set them free , and he ask who have treat them in so evil a manner .
` No sooner have you go than a great giant come , and dealt with u a you see , and carry off your wife and your two horse , ' say the men .
` Then my eye will not close nor will my head lay itself down till I fetch my wife and horse home again , ' answer he , and he stop and note the track of the horse on the grass , and follow after them till he arrive at the wood , when the darkness fell . '
I will sleep here , ' he say to himself , ` but first I will make a fire , ' And he gather together some twig that be lie about , and then take two dry stick and rub them together till the fire come , and he sat by it .
The twig crack and the flame blaze up , and a slim yellow dog push through the bush and lay his head on the king 's knee , and the king stroke his head .
` Wuf , wuf , ' say the dog .
` Sore be the plight of thy wife and thy horse when the giant drive them last night through the forest . '
` That be why I have come , ' answer the king ; and suddenly his heart seem to fail him and he felt that he could not go on . '
I can not fight that giant , ' he cry , look at the dog with a white face . '
I be afraid , let me turn homewards . '
` No , do n't do that , ' reply the dog .
` Eat and sleep , and I will watch over you . '
So the king ate and lay down , and sleep till the sun wake him .
` It be time for you to start on your way , ' say the dog , ` and if danger press , call on me , and I will help you . '
` Farewell , then , ' answer the king ; ' I will not forget that promise , ' and on he go , and on , and on , till he reach a tall cliff with many stick lie about .
` It be almost night , ' he think ; ' I will make a fire and rest , ' and thus he do , and when the flame blaze up , the hoary hawk of the grey rock fly on to a bough above him .
` Sore be the plight of thy wife and thy horse when they pass here with the giant , ' say the hawk .
` Never shall I find them , ' answer the king , ` and nothing shall I get for all my trouble . '
` Oh , take heart , ' reply the hawk ; ` thing be never so bad but what they might be bad .
Eat and sleep and I will watch thee , ' and the king do a he be bid by the hawk , and by the morning he felt brave again .
` Farewell , ' say the bird , ` and if danger press call to me , and I will help you . '
On he walk , and on and on , till a dusk be fall he come to a great river , and on the bank there be stick lie about . '
I will make myself a fire , ' he think , and thus he do , and by and bye a smooth brown head peer at him from the water , and a long body follow it .
` Sore be the plight of thy wife and thy horse when they pass the river last night , ' say the otter . '
I have seek them and not find them , ' answer the king , ` and nought shall I get for my trouble . '
` Be not so downcast , ' reply the otter ; ` before noon to-morrow thou shalt behold thy wife .
But eat and sleep and I will watch over thee . '
So the king do a the otter bid him , and when the sun rise he wake and saw the otter lie on the bank .
` Farewell , ' cry the otter a he jump into the water , ` and if danger press , call to me and I will help you . '
For many hour the king walk , and at length he reach a high rock , which be rent into two by a great earthquake .
Throwing himself on the ground he look over the side , and right at the very bottom he saw his wife and his horse .
His heart give a great bound , and all his fear leave him , but he be force to be patient , for the side of the rock be smooth , and not even a goat could find foothold .
So he get up again , and make his way round through the wood , push by tree , scramble over rock , wad through stream , till at last he be on flat ground again , close to the mouth of the cavern .
His wife give a shriek of joy when he come in , and then burst into tear , for she be tired and very frightened .
But her husband do not understand why she weep , and he be tire and bruise from his climb , and a little cross too .
` You give me but a sorry welcome , ' grumble he , ` when I have half-killed myself to get to you . '
` Do not heed him , ' say the horse to the weep woman ; ` put him in front of u , where he will be safe , and give him food , for he be weary . '
And she do a the horse tell her , and he ate and rest , till by and bye a long shadow fell over them , and their heart beat with fear , for they know that the giant be come . '
I smell a stranger , ' cry the giant , a he enter ; but it be dark inside the chasm , and he do not see the king , who be crouch down between the foot of the horse . '
A stranger , my lord !
no stranger ever come here , not even the sun ! '
and the king 's wife laugh gaily a she go up to the giant and stroke the huge hand which hang down by his side .
` Well , I perceive nothing , certainly , ' answer he , ` but it be very odd .
However , it be time that the horse be feed ; ' and he lift down an armful of hay from a shelf of rock and hold out a handful to each animal , who move forward to meet him , leave the king behind .
As soon a the giant 's hand be near their mouth they each make a snap , and begin to bite them , so that his groan and shriek might have be hear a mile off .
Then they wheel round and kick him till they could kick no more .
At length the giant crawl away , and lay quiver in a corner , and the queen go up to him .
` Poor thing !
poor thing ! '
