she say , ` they seem to have go mad ; it be awful to behold . '
` If I have have my soul in my body they would certainly have kill me , ' groan the giant .
` It be lucky indeed , ' answer the queen ; ` but tell me , where be thy soul , that I may take care of it ? '
` Up there , in the Bonnach stone , ' answer the giant , point to a stone which be balance loosely on an edge of rock .
` But now leave me , that I may sleep , for I have far to go to-morrow . '
Soon snore be hear from the corner where the giant lay , and then the queen lay down too , and the horse , and the king be hide between them , so that none could see him .
Before the dawn the giant rise and go out , and immediately the queen run up to the Bonnach stone , and tug and push at it till it be quite steady on it ledge , and could not fall over .
And so it be in the evening when the giant come home ; and when they saw his shadow , the king creep down in front of the horse .
` Why , what have you do to the Bonnach stone ? '
ask the giant . '
I fear l it should fall over , and be break , with your soul in it , ' say the queen , ` so I put it far back on the ledge . '
` It be not there that my soul be , ' answer he , ` it be on the threshold .
But it be time the horse be feed ; ' and he fetch the hay , and give it to them , and they bite and kick him a before , till he lay half dead on the ground .
Next morning he rise and go out , and the queen run to the threshold of the cave , and wash the stone , and pull up some moss and little flower that be hide in the cranny , and by and bye when dusk have fall the giant come home .
` You have be clean the threshold , ' say he .
` And be I not right to do it , see that your soul be in it ? '
ask the queen .
` It be not there that my soul be , ' answer the giant .
` Under the threshold be a stone , and under the stone be a sheep , and in the sheep 's body be a duck , and in the duck be an egg , and in the egg be my soul .
But it be late , and I must fee the horse ; ' and he bring them the hay , but they only bit and kick him a before , and if his soul have be within him , they would have kill him outright .
It be still dark when the giant get up and go his way , and then the king and the queen run forward to take up the threshold , while the horse look on .
But sure enough !
just a the giant have say , underneath the threshold be the flagstone , and they pull and tug till the stone give way .
Then something jump out so suddenly , that it nearly knock them down , and a it flee past , they saw it be a sheep .
` If the slim yellow dog of the greenwood be only here , he would soon have that sheep , ' cry the king ; and a he speak , the slim yellow dog appear from the forest , with the sheep in his mouth .
With a blow from the king , the sheep fell dead , and they open it body , only to be blind by a rush of wing a the duck fly past .
` If the hoary hawk of the rock be only here , he would soon have that duck , ' cry the king ; and a he speak the hoary hawk be see hover above them , with the duck in his mouth .
They cut off the duck 's head with a swing of the king 's sword , and take the egg out of it body , but in his triumph the king hold it carelessly , and it slip from his hand , and roll swiftly down the hill right into the river .
` If the brown otter of the stream be only here , he would soon have that egg , ' cry the king ; and the next minute there be the brown otter , drip with water , hold the egg in his mouth .
But beside the brown otter , a huge shadow come steal along -- the shadow of the giant .
The king stand star at it , a if he be turn into stone , but the queen snatch the egg from the otter and crush it between her two hand .
And after that the shadow suddenly shrink and be still , and they know that the giant be dead , because they have find his soul .
Next day they mount the two horse and rode home again , visit their friend the brown otter and the hoary hawk and the slim yellow dog by the way .
From ` West Highland Tales . '
A French Puck Among the mountain pasture and valley that lie in the centre of France there dwell a mischievous kind of spirit , whose delight it be to play trick on everybody , and particularly on the shepherd and the cowboy .
They never know when they be safe from him , a he could change himself into a man , woman or child , a stick , a goat , a ploughshare .
Indeed , there be only one thing whose shape he could not take , and that be a needle .
At least , he could transform himself into a needle , but try a he might he never be able to imitate the hole , so every woman would have find him out at once , and this he know .
Now the hour oftenest choose by this naughty sprite -LRB- whom we will call Puck -RRB- for perform his prank be about midnight , just when the shepherd and cowherd , tire out with their long day 's work , be sound asleep .
Then he would go into the cowshed and unfasten the chain that fix each beast in it own stall , and let them fall with a heavy clang to the ground .
The noise be so loud that it be certain to awaken the cowboy , however fatigue they might be , and they drag themselves wearily to the stable to put back the chain .
But no sooner have they return to their bed than the same thing happen again , and so on till the morning .
Or perhaps Puck would spend his night in plait together the mane and tail of two of the horse , so that it would take the groom hour of labour to get them right in the morning , while Puck , hidden among the hay in the loft , would peep out to watch them , enjoy himself amazingly all the time .
One even more than eighty year ago a man name William be pass along the bank of a stream when he notice a sheep who be bleat loudly .
William think it must have stray from the flock , and that he have well take it home with him till he could discover it owner .
So he go up to where it be stand , and a it seem so tired that it could hardly walk , he hoist it on his shoulder and continue on his way .
The sheep be pretty heavy , but the good man be merciful and stagger along as best he could under his load .
` It be not much far , ' he think to himself a he reach an avenue of walnut tree , when suddenly a voice speak out from over his head , and make him jump .
` Where be you ? '
say the voice , and the sheep answer : ` Here on the shoulder of a donkey . '
In another moment the sheep be stand on the ground and William be run towards home as fast a his leg would carry him .
But a he go , a laugh , which yet be something of a bleat , rang in his ear , and though he try not to hear , the word reach him , ` Oh , dear !
What fun I have have , to be sure ! '
Puck be careful not always to play his trick in the same place , but visit one village after another , so that everyone tremble l he should be the next victim .
After a bit he grow tire of cowboy and shepherd , and wonder if there be no one else to give him some sport .
At length he be tell of a young couple who be go to the near town to buy all that they need for set up house .
Quite certain that they would forget something which they could not do without , Puck wait patiently till they be jog along in their cart on their return journey , and change himself into a fly in order to overhear their conversation .
For a long time it be very dull -- all about their wedding day next month , and who be to be invite .
This lead the bride to her wedding dress , and she give a little scream .
` Just think !
Oh !
how could I be so stupid !
I have forget to buy the different coloured reel of cotton to match my clothes ! '
` Dear , dear ! '
exclaim the young man .
` That be unlucky ; and do n't you tell me that the dressmaker be come in to-morrow ? '
` Yes , I do , ' and then suddenly she give another little scream , which have quite a different sound from the first .
` Look !
Look ! '
The bridegroom look , and on one side of the road he saw a large ball of thread of all colour -- of all the colour , that be , of the dress that be tie on to the back of the cart .
` Well , that be a wonderful piece of good fortune , ' cry he , a he spring out to get it .
` One would think a fairy have put it there on purpose . '
` Perhaps she have , ' laugh the girl , and a she speak she seem to hear an echo of her laughter come from the horse , but of course that be nonsense .
The dressmaker be delight with the thread that be give her .
It match the stuff so perfectly , and never tie itself in knot , or break perpetually , a most thread do .
She finish her work much quick than she expect and the bride say she be to be sure to come to the church and see her in her wedding dress .
There be a great crowd assemble to witness the ceremony , for the young people be immense favourite in the neighbourhood , and their parent be very rich .
The door be open , and the bride could be see from afar , walk under the chestnut avenue .
` What a beautiful girl ! '
exclaim the men .
` What a lovely dress ! '
whisper the woman .
But just a she enter the church and take the hand of the bridegroom , who be wait for her , a loud noise be hear .
` Crick !
crack !
Crick !
crack ! '
and the wedding garment fell to the ground , to the great confusion of the wearer .
Not that the ceremony be put off for a little thing like that !
Cloaks in profusion be instantly offer to the young bride , but she be so upset that she could hardly keep from tear .
One of the guest , more curious than the rest , stay behind to examine the dress , determine , if she could , to find out the cause of the disaster .
` The thread must have be rotten , ' she say to herself . '
I will see if I can break it . '
But search a she would she could find none .
The thread have vanish !
From ` Litterature Orale de l'Auvergne , ' par Paul Sebillot .
The Three Crowns There be once a king who have three daughter .
The two eldest be very proud and quarrelsome , but the young be as good a they be bad .
Well , three prince come to court them , and two of them be exactly like the eldest lady , and one be just as lovable a the young .
One day they be all walk down to a lake that lay at the bottom of the lawn when they meet a poor beggar .
The king would n't give him anything , and the eldest princess would n't give him anything , nor their sweetheart ; but the young daughter and her true love do give him something , and kind word along with it , and that be good than all .
When they get to the edge of the lake what do they find but the beautifullest boat you ever saw in your life ; and say the eldest , ` I 'll take a sail in this fine boat ' ; and say the second eldest , ` I 'll take a sail in this fine boat ' ; and say the young , ' I wo n't take a sail in that fine boat , for I be afraid it 's an enchanted one . '
But the others persuade her to go in , and her father be just go in after her , when up sprung on the deck a little man only seven inch high , and order him to stand back .
Well , all the men put their hand to their sword ; and if the same sword be only plaything , they be n't able to draw them , for all strength that be leave their arm .
Seven Inches loosen the silver chain that fasten the boat , and push away , and after grin at the four men , say he to them .
` Bid your daughter and your bride farewell for awhile .
You , ' say he to the young , ` need n't fear , you 'll recover your princess all in good time , and you and she will be as happy a the day be long .
Bad people , if they be roll stark naked in gold , would not be rich .
Good-bye . '
Away they sail , and the lady stretch out their hand , but be n't able to say a word .
Well , they be n't cross the lake while a cat ` ud be lickin ' her ear , and the poor men could n't stir hand or foot to follow them .
They saw Seven Inches hand the three princess out of the boat , and let them down by a basket into a draw-well , but king nor prince ever saw an opening before in the same place .
When the last lady be out of sight , the men find the strength in their arm and leg again .
Round the lake they run , and never draw rein till they come to the well and windlass ; and there be the silk rope roll on the axle , and the nice white basket hang to it .
` Let me down , ' say the young prince .
` I 'll die or recover them again . '
` No , ' say the second daughter 's sweetheart , ` it be my turn first . '
And say the other , ' I be the eldest . '
So they give way to him , and in he get into the basket , and down they let him .
First they lose sight of him , and then , after wind off a hundred perch of the silk rope , it slacken , and they stop turn .
They wait two hour , and then they go to dinner , because there be no pull make at the rope .
Guards be set till next morning , and then down go the second prince , and sure enough , the young of all get himself let down on the third day .
He go down perch and perch , while it be a dark about him a if he be in a big pot with a cover on .
At last he saw a glimmer far down , and in a short time he felt the ground .
Out he come from the big lime-kiln , and , lo !
and behold you , there be a wood , and green field , and a castle in a lawn , and a bright sky over all .
` It 's in Tir-na-n-Oge I be , ' say he .
` Let 's see what sort of people be in the castle . '
On he walk , across field and lawn , and no one be there to keep him out or let him into the castle ; but the big hall-door be wide open .
He go from one fine room to another that be finer , and at last he reach the handsome of all , with a table in the middle .
And such a dinner a be lay upon it !
The prince be hungry enough , but he be too mannerly to eat without be invite .
So he sit by the fire , and he do not wait long till he hear step , and in come Seven Inches with the young sister by the hand .
Well , prince and princess fly into one another 's arm , and say the little man , say he , ` Why be n't you eat ? ' '
I think , sir , ' say the prince , ` it be only good manner to wait to be ask . '
` The other prince do n't think so , ' say he .
` Each o ' them fell to without leave , and only give me the rough word when I tell them they be make more free than welcome .
Well , I do n't think they feel much hunger now .
There they be , good marble instead of flesh and blood , ' say he , point to two statue , one in one corner , and the other in the other corner of the room .
The prince be frighten , but he be afraid to say anything , and Seven Inches make him sit down to dinner between himself and his bride ; and he 'd be as happy a the day be long , only for the sight of the stone men in the corner .
Well , that day go by , and when the next come , say Seven Inches to him , ` Now , you 'll have to set out that way , ' point to the sun , ` and you 'll find the second princess in a giant 's castle this evening , when you 'll be tire and hungry , and the eldest princess to-morrow evening ; and you may as well bring them here with you .
You need not ask leave of their master ; and perhaps if they ever get home , they 'll look on poor people a if they be flesh and blood like themselves . '
Away go the prince , and bedad !
it 's tired and hungry he be when he reach the first castle , at sunset .
Oh , be n't the second princess glad to see him !
And what a good supper she give him .
But she hear the giant at the gate , and she hide the prince in a closet .
Well , when he come in , he snuff , an ' he snuff , and say he , ` By the life , I smell fresh meat . '
` Oh , ' say the princess , ` it 's only the calf I get kill to-day . '
` Ay , ay , ' say he , ` be supper ready ? '
` It be , ' say she ; and before he rise from the table he eat three-quarters of a calf , and a flask of wine . '
I think , ' say he , when all be do , ' I smell fresh meat still . '
` It 's sleepy you be , ' say she ; ` go to bed . '
` When will you marry me ? '
say the giant .
` You 're put me off too long . '
` St. Tibb 's Eve , ' say she . '
I wish I know how far off that be , ' say he ; and he fell asleep , with his head in the dish .
Next day , he go out after breakfast , and she send the prince to the castle where the eldest sister be .
The same thing happen there ; but when the giant be snore , the princess waken up the prince , and they saddle two steed in the stable and rode into the field on them .
But the horse ' heel strike the stone outside the gate , and up get the giant and strode after them .
He roar and he shout , and the more he shout , the faster run the horse , and just a the day be break he be only twenty perch behind .
But the prince do n't leave the castle of Seven Inches without be provide with something good .
He rein in his steed , and fling a short , sharp knife over his shoulder , and up spring a thick wood between the giant and themselves .
They catch the wind that blow before them , and the wind that blow behind them do not catch them .
At last they be near the castle where the other sister live ; and there she be , wait for them under a high hedge , and a fine steed under her .
But the giant be now in sight , roar like a hundred lion , and the other giant be out in a moment , and the chase keep on .
For every two spring the horse give , the giant give three , and at last they be only seventy perch off .
Then the prince stop again , and fling the second knife behind him .
Down go all the flat field , till there be a quarry between them a quarter of a mile deep , and the bottom fill with black water ; and before the giant could get round it , the prince and princess be inside the kingdom of the great magician , where the high thorny hedge open of itself to everyone that he choose to let in .
There be joy enough between the three sister , till the two eldest saw their lover turn into stone .
But while they be shed tear for them , Seven Inches come in , and touch them with his rod .
So they be flesh , and blood , and life once more , and there be great hugging and kissing , and all sit down to breakfast , and Seven Inches sit at the head of the table .
When breakfast be over , he take them into another room , where there be nothing but heap of gold , and silver , and diamond , and silk , and satin ; and on a table there be lie three set of crown : a gold crown be in a silver crown , and that be lie in a copper crown .
He take up one set of crown , and give it to the eldest princess ; and another set , and give it to the second youngest princess ; and another , and give it to the young of all ; and say he , ` Now you may all go to the bottom of the pit , and you have nothing to do but stir the basket , and the people that be watch above will draw you up .
But remember , lady , you be to keep your crow safe , and be marry in them , all the same day .
If you be marry separately , or if you be marry without your crown , a curse will follow -- mind what I say . '
So they take leave of him with great respect , and walk arm-in-arm to the bottom of the draw-well .
There be a sky and a sun over them , and a great high wall , cover with ivy , rise before them , and be so high they could not see to the top of it ; and there be an arch in this wall , and the bottom of the draw-well be inside the arch .
The young pair go last ; and say the princess to the prince , ` I 'm sure the two prince do n't mean any good to you .
Keep these crown under your cloak , and if you be oblige to stay last , do n't get into the basket , but put a big stone , or any heavy thing inside , and see what will happen . '
As soon a they be inside the dark cave , they put in the eldest princess first , and stir the basket , and up she go .
Then the basket be let down again , and up go the second princess , and then up go the young ; but first she put her arm round her prince 's neck , and kiss him , and cry a little .
At last it come to the turn of the young prince , and instead of go into the basket he put in a big stone .
He draw on one side and listen , and after the basket be draw up about twenty perch , down come it and the stone like thunder , and the stone be break into little bit .
Well , the poor prince have nothing for it but to walk back to the castle ; and through it and round it he walk , and the fine of eating and drinking he get , and a bed of bog-down to sleep on , and long walk he take through garden and lawn , but not a sight could he get , high or low , of Seven Inches .
He , before a week , get tire of it , he be so lonesome for his true love ; and at the end of a month he do n't know what to do with himself .
One morning he go into the treasure room , and take notice of a beautiful snuff-box on the table that he do n't remember see there before .
He take it in his hand and open it , and out Seven Inches walk on the table . '

say the other , ` if I have my princess here , and could see you now and then , I 'd never know a dismal day . '
` Well , you 're long enough here now , and you 're want there above .
Keep your bride 's crown safe , and whenever you want my help , open this snuff-box .
Now take a walk down the garden , and come back when you 're tire . '
The prince be go down a gravel walk with a quickset hedge on each side , and his eye on the ground , and he be think of one thing and another .
At last he lift his eye , and there he be outside of a smith 's gate that he often pass before , about a mile away from the palace of his betrothed princess .
The clothes he have on him be as rag a you please , but he have his crown safe under his old cloak .

Are you any good with hammer and tongs ?
Come in and bear a hand , an I 'll give you diet and lodging , and a few penny when you earn them . '

I want nothing but to be busy . '
So he take the hammer , and pound away at the red-hot bar that the smith be turn on the anvil to make into a set of horse-shoes .

` You all hear how the two princess be loth to be marry till the young would be ready with her crown and her sweetheart .
But after the windlass loosen accidentally when they be pull up her bridegroom that be to be , there be no more sign of a well , or a rope , or a windlass , than there be on the palm of your hand .

Myself go down out o ' curiousity , and to be sure I be delight with the grand dress of the two bride , and the three crown on their head -- gold , silver , and copper , one inside the other .

and such running and racing and peep down a there be !
but the clerk soon open the door of the vault , and up come the two prince , their fine clothes cover an inch thick with cobweb and mould .

I 'll give my young daughter for a wife to whoever brings three crown to me like the others ; and if he do n't care to be marry , some other one will , and I 'll make his fortune . ' '
I wish , ' say the smith , ' I could do it ; but I be look at the crown after the princess get home , and I do n't think there 's a black or a white smith on the face of the earth that could imitate them . '
` Faint heart never win fair lady , ' say the prince .

` Are you in earnest ? '
say the smith .
` Faith , I be so , ' say he .
` Go !
you ca n't do bad than lose . '
To make a long story short , the smith get the quarter of a pound of gold , and the quarter of a pound of silver , and the quarter of a pound of copper , and give them and the pattern crown to the prince .
He shut the forge door at nightfall , and the neighbour all gather in the yard , and they hear him hammer , hammer , hammer , from that to daybreak ; and every now and then he 'd throw out through the window bit of gold , silver , and copper ; and the idler scramble for them , and curse one another , and pray for the good luck of the workman .
Well , just a the sun be think to rise , he open the door , and bring out the three crown he get from his true love , and such shouting and huzzaing a there be !

It be a big fellow that take service with me yesterday . '

` Are you the fellow , ' say he , ` that make these crown ? '
` Yes , ' say the other .
` Then , ' say he , ` maybe you 'd give yourself a brushing , and get into that coach ; the king want to see you .
I pity the princess . '
The young prince get into the carriage , and while they be on the way he open the snuff-box , and out walk Seven Inches , and stand on his thigh .
` Well , ' say he , ` what trouble be on you now ? '
` Master , ' say the other , ` please let me go back to my forge , and let this carriage be fill with paving stone . '
No sooner say than do .
The prince be sit in his forge , and the horse wonder what be after happen to the carriage .
When they come into the palace yard , the king himself open the carriage door , for respect to his new son-in-law .
As soon a he turn the handle , a shower of small stone fell on his powdered wig and his silk coat , and down he fell under them .
There be great fright and some laughter , and the king , after he wipe the blood from his forehead , look very cross at the eldest prince .
` My lord , ' say he , ` I 'm very sorry for this accident , but I 'm not to blame .
I saw the young smith get into the carriage , and we never stop a minute since . '
` It 's uncivil you be to him .
Go , ' say he to the other prince , ` and bring the young smith here , and be polite . '
` Never fear , ' say he .
But there 's some people that could n't be good-natured if they try , and not a bit civiller be the new messenger than the old , and when the king open the carriage door a second time , it 's shower of mud that come down on him .
` There 's no use , ' say he , ` go on this way .
The fox never get a good messenger than himself . '
So he change his clothes , and wash himself , and out he set to the prince 's forge and ask him to sit along with himself .
The prince beg to be allow to sit in the other carriage , and when they be half-way he open his snuff-box .
` Master , ' say he , ` I 'd wish to be dress now accord to my rank . '
` You shall be that , ' say Seven Inches .
` And now I 'll bid you farewell .
Continue a good and kind a you always be ; love your wife ; and that 's all the advice I 'll give you . '
So Seven Inches vanish ; and when the carriage door be open in the yard , out walk the prince as fine a hand could make him , and the first thing he do be to run over to his bride and embrace her .
Every one be full of joy but the two other prince .
There be not much delay about the marriage , and they be all celebrate on the one day .
Soon after , the two elder couple go to their own court , but the young pair stay with the old king , and they be as happy a the happy married couple you ever heard of in a story .
From ` West Highland Tales . '
The Story of a Very Bad Boy Once upon a time there live in a little village in the very middle of France a widow and her only son , a boy about fifteen , whose name be Antoine , though no one ever call him anything but Toueno-Boueno .
They be very poor indeed , and their hut shook about their ear on windy night , till they expect the wall to fall in and crush them , but instead of go to work a a boy of his age ought to do , Toueno-Boueno do nothing but lounge along the street , his eye fix on the ground , see nothing that go on round him .
` You be very , very stupid , my dear child , ' his mother would sometimes say to him , and then she would add with a laugh , ` Certainly you will never catch a wolf by the tail . '
One day the old woman bid Antoine go into the forest and collect enough dry leaf to make bed for herself and him .
Before he have finish it begin to rain heavily , so he hide himself in the hollow trunk of a tree , where he be so dry and comfortable that he soon fell fast asleep .
By and by he be awaken by a noise which sound like a dog scratching at the door , and he suddenly felt frighten , why he do not know .
Very cautiously he raise his head , and right above him he saw a big hairy animal , come down tail foremost .
` It be the wolf that they talk so much about , ' he say to himself , and he make himself as small a he could and shrink into a corner .
The wolf come down the inside of the tree , slowly , slowly ; Antoine felt turn to stone , so terrified be he , and hardly dare to breathe .
Suddenly an idea enter his mind , which he think might save him still .
He remember to have hear from his mother that a wolf could neither bend his back nor turn his head , so a to look behind him , and quick a lightning he stretch up his hand , and seize the wolf 's tail , pull it towards him .
Then he leave the tree and drag the animal to his mother 's house .
` Mother , you have often declare that I be too stupid to catch a wolf by the tail .
Now see , ' he cry triumphantly .
` Well , well , wonder will never cease , ' answer the good woman , who take care to keep at a safe distance .
` But a you really have get him , let u see if we ca n't put him to some use .
Fetch the skin of the ram which die last week out of the chest , and we will sew the wolf up in it .
He will make a splendid ram , and to-morrow we will drive him to the fair and sell him . '
Very likely the wolf , who be cunning and clever , may have understood what she say , but he think it best to give no sign , and suffer the skin to be sew upon him . '
I can always get away if I choose , ' think he , ` it be well not to be in a hurry ; ' so he remain quite still while the skin be draw over his head , which make him very hot and uncomfortable , and resist the temptation to snap off the finger or nose that be so close to his mouth .
The fair be at it height next day when Toueno-Boueno arrive with his wolf in ram 's clothing .
All the farmer crowd round him , each offer a high price than the last .
Never have they behold such a beautiful beast , say they , and at last , after much bargaining , he be hand over to three brother for a good sum of money .
It happen that these three brother own large flock of sheep , though none so large and fine a the one they have just buy .
` My flock be the near , ' observe the eldest brother ; ` we will leave him in the fold for the night , and to-morrow we will decide which pasture will be best for him . '
And the wolf grin a he listen , and hold up his head a little high than before .
Early next morning the young farmer begin to go his round , and the sheep-fold be the first place he visit .
To his horror , the sheep be all stretch out dead before him , except one , which the wolf have eat , bone and all .
Instantly the truth flash upon him .
It be no ram that lay curl up in the corner pretend to be asleep -LRB- for in reality he could bend back and turn his head as much a he like -RRB- , but a wolf who be watch him out of the corner of his eye , and might spring upon him at any moment .
So the farmer take no notice , and only think that here be a fine chance of revenge himself on his next brother for a trick which he have play , and merely tell him that the ram would not eat the grass in that field , and it might be well to drive him to the pasture by the river , where his own flock be feed .
The second brother eagerly swallow the bait , and that even the wolf be drive down to the field where the young man keep the sheep which have be leave him by his father .
By the next morning they also be all dead , but the second brother likewise hold his peace , and allow the sheep which belong to the young to share the fate of the other two .
Then they meet and confess to each other their disaster , and resolve to take the animal as fast a possible back to Toueno-Boueno , who should get a sound thrashing .
Antoine be sit on a plum tree belong to a neighbour , eat the ripe fruit , when he saw the three young farmer come towards him .
Swinging himself down , he fly home to the hut , cry breathlessly , ` Mother , mother , the farmer be close by with the wolf .
They have find out all about it , and will certainly kill me , and perhaps you too .
But if you do a I tell you , I may be able to save u both .
Lie down on the floor , and pretend to be dead , and be sure not to speak , whatever happen .
Thus when the three brother , each arm with a whip , enter the hut a few second later , they find a woman extend on the floor , and Toueno kneeling at her side , whistle loudly into her ear .
` What be you do now , you rascal ? '
ask the eldest .
` What be I do ?
Oh , my poor friend , I be the most miserable creature in the world !
I have lose the best of mother , and I do n't know what will become of me , ' and he hide his face in his hand and sob again .
` But what be you whistle like that for ? '
` Well , it be the only chance .
This whistle have be know to bring the dead back to life , and I hop -- ' here he bury his face in his hand again , but peep between his finger he saw that the brother have open their six eye as wide a saucer .
` Look ! '
he suddenly exclaim with a cry , ` Look !
I be sure I felt her body move !
And now her nostril be twitch .
Ah !
the whistle have not lose it power after all , ' and stoop down , Toueno whistle more loudly than before , so that the old woman 's foot and hand show sign of life , and she soon be able to life her head .
The farmer be so astonished at her restoration , that it be some time before they could speak .
At length the eldest turn to the boy and say : ` Now listen to me .
There be no manner of doubt that you be a young villain .
You sell u a ram knowing full well that it be a wolf , and we come here to-day to pay you out for it .
But if you will give u that whistle , we will pardon what you have do , and will leave you alone . '
` It be my only treasure , and I set great store by it , ' answer the boy , pretend to hesitate .
` But a you wish for it so much , well , I suppose I ca n't refuse , ' and he hold out the whistle , which the eldest brother put in his pocket .
Armed with the precious whistle , the three brother return home full of joy , and a they go the young say to the others , ' I have such a good idea !
Our wife be all lazy and grumbling , and make our life a burden .
Let u give them a lesson , and kill them as soon a we get in .
Of course we can restore them to life at once , but they will have have a rare fright . '
` Ah , how clever you be , ' answer the other two .
` Nobody else would have think of that . '
So gaily the three husband knock down their three wife , who fell dead to the ground .
Then one by one the men try the whistle , and blow so loudly that it seem a if their lung would burst , but the woman lay stark and stiff and never move an eyelid .
The husband grow pale and cold , for they have never dream of this , nor meant any harm , and after a while they understand that their effort be of no use , and that once more the boy have trick them .
With stern face they rise to their foot , and take a large sack they retrace their step to the hut .
This time there be no escape .
Toueno have be asleep , and only open his eye a they enter .
Without a word on either side they thrust him into the sack , and tie up the mouth , the eldest threw it over his shoulder .
After that they all set out to the river , where they intend to drown the boy .
But the river be a long way off , and the day be very hot , and Antoine be heavy , heavy than a whole sheaf of corn .
They carry him in turn , but even so they grow very tired and thirsty , and when a little tavern come in sight on the roadside , they thankfully fling the sack down on a bench and enter to refresh themselves .
They never notice that a beggar be sit in the shade at the end of the bench , but Toueno 's sharp ear catch the sound of someone eating , and as soon a the farmer have go into the inn he begin to groan softly .
` What be the matter ? '
ask the beggar , draw a little nearer .
` Why have they shut you up , poor boy ? '
` Because they want to make me a bishop , and I would not consent , ' answer Toueno .
` Dear me , ' exclaim the beggar , ` yet it be n't such a bad thing to be a bishop . ' '
I do n't say it be , ' reply the young rascal , ` but I should never like it .
However , if you have any fancy for wear a mitre , you need only untie the sack , and take my place . ' '
I should like nothing well , ' say the man , a he stoop to undo the big knot .
So it be the beggar and not Toueno-Boueno who be fling into the water .
The next morning the three wife be bury , and on return from the cemetery , their husband meet Toueno-Boueno drive a magnificent flock of sheep .
At the sight of him the three farmer stand still with astonishment .
` What !
you scoundrel ! '
they cry at last , ` we drown you yesterday , and to-day we find you again , as well a ever ! '
` It do seem odd , do n't it ? '
answer he .
` But perhaps you do n't know that beneath this world there lie another yet more beautiful and far , far rich .
Well , it be there that you send me when you fling me into the river , and though I felt a little strange at first , yet I soon begin to look about me , and to see what be happen .
There I notice that close to the place where I have fall , a sheep fair be be hold , and a bystander tell me that every day horse or cattle be sell somewhere in the town .
If I have only have the luck to be throw into the river on the side of the horse fair I might have make my fortune !
As it be , I have to content myself with buy these sheep , which you can get for nothing . '
` And do you know exactly the spot in the river which lie over the horse fair ? '
` As if I do not know it , when I have see it with my own eye . '
` Then if you do not want u to avenge our dead flock and our murdered wife , you will have to throw u into the river just over the place of the horse fair . '
` Very well ; only you must get three sack and come with me to that rock which jut into the river .
I will throw you in from there , and you will fall nearly on to the horse ' back . '
So he throw them in , and a they be never see again , no one ever know into which fair they have fall .
From ` Litterature Orale de L'Auvergne , ' par Paul Sebillot .
The Brown Bear of Norway There be once a king in Ireland , and he have three daughter , and very nice princess they be .
And one day , when they and their father be walk on the lawn , the king begin to joke with them , and to ask them whom they would like to be marry to .
` I 'll have the king of Ulster for a husband , ' say one ; ` and I 'll have the king of Munster , ' say another ; ` and , ' say the young , ` I 'll have no husband but the Brown Bear of Norway . '
For a nurse of hers use to be tell her of an enchanted prince that she call by that name , and she fell in love with him , and his name be the first name on her tongue , for the very night before she be dream of him .
Well , one laugh , and another laugh , and they joke with the princess all the rest of the evening .
But that very night she wake up out of her sleep in a great hall that be light up with a thousand lamp ; the rich carpet be on the floor , and the wall be cover with cloth of gold and silver , and the place be full of grand company , and the very beautiful prince she saw in her dream be there , and it be n't a moment till he be on one knee before her , and tell her how much he love her , and ask her would n't she be his queen .
Well , she have n't the heart to refuse him , and marry they be the same evening .
` Now , my darling , ' say he , when they be leave by themselves , ` you must know that I be under enchantment .
A sorceress , that have a beautiful daughter , wish me for her son-in-law ; but the mother get power over me , and when I refuse to wed her daughter she make me take the form of a bear by day , and I be to continue so till a lady would marry me of her own free will , and endure five year of great trial after . '
Well , when the princess wake in the morning , she miss her husband from her side , and spend the day very sadly .
But as soon a the lamp be light in the grand hall , where she be sit on a sofa cover with silk , the folding door fly open , and he be sit by her side the next minute .
So they spend another happy evening , but he warn her that whenever she begin to tire of him , or cease to have faith in him , they would be part for ever , and he 'd be oblige to marry the witch 's daughter .
She get use to find him absent by day , and they spend a happy twelvemonth together , and at last a beautiful little boy be bear ; and happy a she be before , she be twice a happy now , for she have her child to keep her company in the day when she could n't see her husband .
At last , one evening , when herself , and himself , and her child be sit with a window open because it be a sultry night , in flew an eagle , take the infant 's sash in his beak , and fly up in the air with him .
She scream , and be go to throw herself out the window after him , but the prince catch her , and look at her very seriously .
She bethink of what he say soon after their marriage , and she stop the cry and complaint that be on her tongue .
She spend her day very lonely for another twelvemonth , when a beautiful little girl be send to her .
Then she think to herself she 'd have a sharp eye about her this time ; so she never would allow a window to be more than a few inch open .
But all her care be in vain .
Another evening , when they be all so happy , and the prince dandle the baby , a beautiful greyhound stand before them , take the child out of the father 's hand , and be out of the door before you could wink .
This time she shout and run out of the room , but there be some of the servant in the next room , and all declare that neither child nor dog pass out .
She felt , somehow , a if it be her husband 's fault , but still she keep command over herself , and do n't once reproach him .
When the third child be bear she would hardly allow a window or a door to be leave open for a moment ; but she be n't the nearer to keep the child to herself .
They be sit one evening by the fire , when a lady appear standing by them .
The princess open her eye in a great fright and star at her , and while she be do so , the lady wrap a shawl round the baby that be sit in it father 's lap , and either sank through the ground with it or go up through the wide chimney .
This time the mother keep her bed for a month .
` My dear , ' say she to her husband , when she be begin to recover , ' I think I 'd feel well if I be to see my father and mother and sister once more .
If you give me leave to go home for a few day I 'd be glad . '
` Very well , ' say he , ' I will do that , and whenever you feel inclined to return , only mention your wish when you lie down at night . '
The next morning when she awake she find herself in her own old chamber in her father 's palace .
She ring the bell , and in a short time she have her mother and father and married sister about her , and they laugh till they cry for joy at find her safe back again .
In time she tell them all that have happen to her , and they do n't know what to advise her to do .
She be a fond of her husband a ever , and say she be sure that he could n't help let the child go ; but still she be afraid beyond the world to have another child torn from her .
Well , the mother and sister consult a wise woman that use to bring egg to the castle , for they have great faith in her wisdom .
She say the only plan be to secure the bear 's skin that the prince be oblige to put on every morning , and get it burn , and then he could n't help be a man night and day , and the enchantment would be at an end .
So they all persuade her to do that , and she promise she would ; and after eight day she felt so great a longing to see her husband again that she make the wish the same night , and when she wake three hour after , she be in her husband 's palace , and he himself be watch over her .
There be great joy on both side , and they be happy for many day .
Now she begin to think how she never mind her husband leave her in the morning , and how she never find him neglect to give her a sweet drink out of a gold cup just a she be go to bed .
One night she contrive not to drink any of it , though she pretend to do so ; and she be wakeful enough in the morning , and saw her husband pass out through a panel in the wainscot , though she keep her eyelid nearly close .
The next night she get a few drop of the sleepy posset that she save the evening before put into her husband 's night drink , and that make him sleep sound enough .
She get up after midnight , pass through the panel , and find a Beautiful brown bear 's hide hanging in the corner .
Then she steal back , and go down to the parlour fire , and put the hide into the middle of it till it be all fine ash .
She then lay down by her husband , give him a kiss on the cheek , and fell asleep .
If she be to live a hundred year she 'd never forget how she waken next morning , and find her husband look down on her with misery and anger in his face .
` Unhappy woman , ' say he , ` you have separate u for ever !
Why have n't you patience for five year ?
I be now oblige , whether I like or no , to go a three day ' journey to the witch 's castle , and marry her daughter .
The skin that be my guard you have burn it , and the egg-wife that give you the counsel be the witch herself .
I wo n't reproach you : your punishment will be severe without it .
Farewell for ever ! '
He kiss her for the last time , and be off the next minute , walk as fast a he could .
She shout after him , and then see there be no use , she dress herself and pursue him .
He never stop , nor stay , nor look back , and still she keep him in sight ; and when he be on the hill she be in the hollow , and when he be in the hollow she be on the hill .
Her life be almost leave her , when , just a the sun be set , he turn up a lane , and go into a little house .
She crawl up after him , and when she get inside there be a beautiful little boy on his knee , and he kiss and hug him .
` Here , my poor darling , ' say he , ` be your eldest child , and there , ' say he , point to a woman that be look on with a smile on her face , ` be the eagle that carry him away . '
She forget all her sorrow in a moment , hug her child , and laugh and cry over him .
The woman wash their foot , and rub them with an ointment that take all the soreness out of their bone , and make them as fresh a a daisy .
Next morning , just before sunrise , he be up , and prepare to be off , ` Here , ' say he to her , ` be a thing which may be of use to you .
It 's a scissors , and whatever stuff you cut with it will be turn into silk .
The moment the sun rise , I 'll lose all memory of yourself and the child , but I 'll get it at sunset again .
Farewell ! '
But he be n't far go till she be in sight of him again , leave her boy behind .
It be the same to-day a yesterday : their shadow go before them in the morning and follow them in the evening .
He never stop , and she never stop , and a the sun be set he turn up another lane , and there they find their little daughter .
It be all joy and comfort again till morning , and then the third day 's journey commence .
But before he start he give her a comb , and tell her that whenever she use it , pearl and diamond would fall from her hair .
Still he have his memory from sunset to sunrise ; but from sunrise to sunset he travel on under the charm , and never throw his eye behind .
This night they come to where the young baby be , and the next morning , just before sunrise , the prince speak to her for the last time .
` Here , my poor wife , ' say he , ` be a little hand-reel , with gold thread that have no end , and the half of our marriage ring .
If you ever get to my house , and put your half-ring to mine , I shall recollect you .
There be a wood yonder , and the moment I enter it I shall forget everything that ever happen between u , just a if I be bear yesterday .
Farewell , dear wife and child , for ever ! '
Just then the sun rise , and away he walk towards the wood .
She saw it open before him and close after him , and when she come up , she could no more get in than she could break through a stone wall .
She wring her hand and shed tear , but then she recollect herself , and cry out , ` Wood , I charge you by my three magic gift , the scissors , the comb , and the reel -- to let me through ' ; and it open , and she go along a walk till she come in sight of a palace , and a lawn , and a woodman 's cottage on the edge of the wood where it come nearest the palace .
She go into the lodge , and ask the woodman and his wife to take her into their service .
They be not willing at first ; but she tell them she would ask no wage , and would give them diamond , and pearl , and silk stuff , and gold thread whenever they wish for them , and then they agree to let her stay .
It be n't long till she hear how a young prince , that be just arrive , be live in the palace of the young mistress .
He seldom stir abroad , and every one that saw him remark how silent and sorrowful he go about , like a person that be search for some lost thing .
The servant and conceited folk at the big house begin to take notice of the beautiful young woman at the lodge , and to annoy her with their impudence .
The head footman be the most troublesome , and at last she invite him to come and take tea with her .
Oh , how rejoice he be , and how he brag of it in the servant ' hall !
Well , the evening come , and the footman walk into the lodge , and be show to her sitting-room ; for the lodge-keeper and his wife stand in great awe of her , and give her two nice room for herself .
Well , he sit down as stiff a a ramrod , and be talk in a grand style about the great doings at the castle , while she be get the tea and toast ready .
` Oh , ' say she to him , ` would you put your hand out at the window and cut me off a sprig or two of honeysuckle ? '
He get up in great glee , and put out his hand and head ; and say she , ` By the virtue of my magic gift , let a pair of horn spring out of your head , and sing to the lodge . '
Just a she wish , so it be .
They spring from the front of each ear , and meet at the back .
Oh , the poor wretch !
And how he bawl and roar !
and the servant that he use to be boast to be soon flock from the castle , and grinning , and huzzaing , and beat tune on tongs and shovel and pan ; and he curse and swearing , and the eye ready to start out of his head , and he so black in the face , and kick out his leg behind him like mad .
At last she pity him , and remove the charm , and the horn drop down on the ground , and he would have kill her on the spot , only he be as weak a water , and his fellow-servants come in and carry him up to the big house .
Well , some way or other the story come to the ear of the prince , and he stroll down that way .
She have only the dress of a countrywoman on her a she sit sew at the window , but that do not hide her beauty , and he be greatly puzzle after he have a good look , just a a body be puzzle to know whether something happen to him when he be young or if he only dream it .
Well , the witch 's daughter heard about it too , and she come to see the strange girl ; and what do she find her do but cut out the pattern of a gown from brown paper ; and a she cut away , the paper become the rich silk she ever saw .
The witch 's daughter look on with greedy eye , and , say she , ` What would you be satisfy to take for that scissors ? '
` I 'll take nothing , ' say she , ` but leave to spend one night outside the prince 's chamber . '
Well , the proud lady fire up , and be go to say something dreadful ; but the scissors keep on cut , and the silk grow rich and rich every inch .
So she promise what the girl have ask her .
When night come on she be let into the palace and lay down till the prince be in such a dead sleep that all she do could n't awake him .
She sing this verse to him , sigh and sobbing , and keep sing it the night long , and it be all in vain : Four long year I be marry to thee ; Three sweet babe I bore to thee ; Brown Bear of Norway , turn to me .
At the first dawn the proud lady be in the chamber , and lead her away , and the footman of the horn put out his tongue at her a she be quit the palace .
So there be no luck so far ; but the next day the prince pass by again and look at her , and salute her kindly , a a prince might a farmer 's daughter , and pass one ; and soon the witch 's daughter pass by , and find her comb her hair , and pearl and diamond drop from it .
Well , another bargain be make , and the princess spend another night of sorrow , and she leave the castle at daybreak , and the footman be at his post and enjoy his revenge .
The third day the prince go by , and stop to talk with the strange woman .
He ask her could he do anything to serve her , and she say he might .
She ask him do he ever wake at night .
He say that he often do , but that during the last two night he be listen to a sweet song in his dream , and could not wake , and that the voice be one that he must have know and love in some other world long ago .
Says she , ` Did you drink any sleepy posset either of these evening before you go to bed ? ' '
I do , ' say he .
` The two evening my wife give me something to drink , but I do n't know whether it be a sleepy posset or not . '
` Well , prince , ' say she , ` a you say you would wish to oblige me , you can do it by not taste any drink to-night . ' '
I will not , ' say he , and then he go on his walk .
Well , the great lady come soon after the prince , and find the stranger use her hand-reel and wind thread of gold off it , and the third bargain be make .
That even the prince be lie on his bed at twilight , and his mind much disturb ; and the door open , and in his princess walk , and down she sit by his bedside and sung : Four long year I be marry to thee ; Three sweet babe I bore to thee ; Brown Bear of Norway , turn to me .
` Brown Bear of Norway ! '
say he . '
I do n't understand you . '
` Do n't you remember , prince , that I be your wedded wife for four year ? ' '
I do not , ' say he , ` but I 'm sure I wish it be so . '
` Do n't you remember our three babe that be still alive ? '
` Show me them .
My mind be all a heap of confusion . '
` Look for the half of our marriage ring , that hang at your neck , and fit it to this . '
He do so , and the same moment the charm be break .
His full memory come back on him , and he fling his arm round his wife 's neck , and both burst into tear .
Well , there be a great cry outside , and the castle wall be hear splitting and cracking .
Everyone in the castle be alarm , and make their way out .
The prince and princess go with the rest , and by the time all be safe on the lawn , down come the building , and make the ground tremble for mile round .
No one ever saw the witch and her daughter afterwards .
It be not long till the prince and princess have their child with them , and then they set out for their own palace .
The king of Ireland and of Munster and Ulster , and their wife , soon come to visit them , and may every one that deserve it be as happy a the Brown Bear of Norway and his family .
From ` West Highland Tales . '
Little Lasse There be once a little boy whose name be Lars , and because he be so little he be call Little Lasse ; he be a brave little man , for he sail round the world in a pea-shell boat .
It be summer time , when the pea shell grow long and green in the garden .
Little Lasse crept into the pea bed where the pea stalk rise high above his cap , and he pick seventeen large shell , the long and straightest he could find .
Little Lasse think , perhaps , that no one saw him ; but that be foolish , for God see everywhere .
Then the gardener come with his gun over his shoulder , and he hear something rustling in the pea bed . '
I think that must be a sparrow , ' he say .
` Ras !
Ras ! '
but no sparrow fly out , for Little Lasse have no wing , only two small leg .
` Wait !
I will load my gun and shoot the sparrow , ' say the gardener .
Then Little Lasse be frighten , and creep out on to the path .
` Forgive me , dear gardener ! '
he say . '
I want to get some fine boat . '
` Well , I will this time , ' say the gardener .
` But another time Little Lasse must ask leave to go and look for boat in the pea bed . ' '
I will , ' answer Lasse ; and he go off to the shore .
Then he open the shell with a pin , split them carefully in two , and break small little bit of stick for the rower ' seat .
Then he take the pea which be in the shell and put them in the boat for cargo .
Some of the shell get break , some remain whole , and when all be ready Lasse have twelve boat .
But they should not be boat , they should be large warship .
He have three liner , three frigate , three brig and three schooner .
The large liner be call Hercules , and the small schooner The Flea .
Little Lasse put all the twelve into the water , and they float a splendidly and as proudly a any great ship over the wave of the ocean .
And now the ship must sail round the world .
The great island over there be Asia ; that large stone Africa ; the little island America ; the small stone be Polynesia ; and the shore from which the ship sail out be Europe .
The whole fleet set off and sail far away to other part of the world .
The ship of the line steer a straight course to Asia , the frigate sail to Africa , the brig to America , and the schooner to Polynesia .
But Little Lasse remain in Europe , and throw small stone out into the great sea .
Now , there be on the shore of Europe a real boat , father 's own , a beautiful white-painted boat , and Little Lasse get into it .
Father and mother have forbid this , but Little Lasse forget .
He think he should very much like to travel to some other part of the world . '
I shall row out a little way -- only a very little way , ' he think .
The pea-shell boat have travel so far that they only look like little speck on the ocean . '
I shall seize Hercules on the coast of Asia , ' say Lasse , ` and then row home again to Europe . '
He shake the rope that hold the boat , and , strange to say , the rope become loose .
Ditsch , ratsch , a man be a man , and so Little Lasse man the boat .
Now he would row -- and he could row , for he have row so often on the step sit home , when the step pretend to be a boat and father 's big stick an oar .
But when Little Lasse want to row there be no oar to be find in the boat .
The oar be lock up in the boat-house , and Little Lasse have not notice that the boat be empty .
It be not so easy a one think to row to Asia without oar .
What could Little Lasse do now ?
The boat be already some distance out on the sea , and the wind , which blow from land , be drive it still far out .
Lasse be frighten and begin to cry .
But there be no one on the shore to hear him .
Only a big crow perch alone in the birch tree ; and the gardener 's black cat sit under the birch tree , wait to catch the crow .
Neither of them trouble themselves in the least about Little Lasse , who be drift out to sea .
Ah !
how sorry Little Lasse be now that he have be disobedient and get into the boat , when father and mother have so often forbidden him to do so !
Now it be too late , he could not get back to land .
Perhaps he would be lose out on the great sea .
What should he do ?
When he have shout until he be tire and no one heard him , he put his two little hand together and say , ` Good God , do not be angry with Little Lasse . '
And then he go to sleep .
For although it be daylight , old Nukku Matti be sit on the shore of the ` Land of Nod , ' and be fish for little child with his long fishing rod .
He hear the low word which Little Lasse say to God , and he immediately draw the boat to himself and lay Little Lasse to sleep on a bed of rise leaf .
Then Nukku Matti say to one of the Dreams , ` Play with Little Lasse , so that he do not feel lonesome . '
It be a little dream-boy , so little , so little , that he be less than Lasse himself ; he have blue eye and fair hair , a red cap with a silver band , and white coat with pearl on the collar .
He come to Little Lasse and say , ` Would you like to sail round the world ? '
` Yes , ' say Lasse in his sleep , ' I should like to . '
` Come , then , ' say the dream-boy , ` and let u sail in your pea-shell boat .
You shall sail in Hercules and I shall sail in The Flea . '
So they sail away from the ` Land of Nod , ' and in a little while Hercules and The Flea be on the shore of Asia away at the other end of the world , where the Ice Sea flow through Behring Straits into the Pacific Ocean .
A long way off in the winter mist they could see the explorer Nordenskiold with his ship Vega try to find an opening between the ice .
It be so cold , so cold ; the great iceberg glitter strangely , and the huge whale now live under the ice , for they could not make a hole through with their awkward head .
All around on the dreary shore there be snow and snow as far a the eye could see ; little grey men in shaggy skin move about , and drive in small sledge through the snow drift , but the sledge be draw by dog .
` Shall we land here ? '
ask the dream-boy .
` No , ' say Little Lasse . '
I be so afraid that the whale would swallow u up , and the big dog bite u .
Let u sail instead to another part of the world . '
` Very well , ' say the dream-boy with the red cap and the silver band ; ` it be not far to America ' -- and at the same moment they be there .
The sun be shin and it be very warm .
Tall palm tree grow in long row on the shore and bore coconut in their top branch .
Men red a copper gallop over the immense green prairie and shoot their arrow at the buffalo , who turn against them with their sharp horn .
An enormous cobra which have creep up the stem of a tall palm tree throw itself on to a little llama that be graze at the foot .
Knaps !
it be all over the little llama .
` Shall we land here ? '
ask the dream-boy .
` No , ' say Little Lasse . '
I be so afraid that the buffalo will butt u , and the great serpent eat u up .
Let u travel to another part of the world . '
` Very well , ' say the dream-boy with the white coat , ` it be only a little way to Polynesia ' -- and then they be there .
It be very warm there , as warm a in a hot bath in Finland .
Costly spice grow on the shore : the pepper plant , the cinnamon tree , ginger , saffron ; the coffee plant and the tea plant .
Brown people with long ear and thick lip , and hideously painted face , hunt a yellow-spotted tiger among the high bamboo on the shore , and the tiger turn on them and stick it claw into one of the brown men .
Then all the others take to flight .
` Shall we land here ? '
ask the dream-boy .
` No , ' say Little Lasse .
` Do n't you see the tiger away there by the pepper plant ?
Let u travel to another part of the world . '
` We can do so , ' say the dream-boy with the blue eye .
` We be not far from Africa ' -- and a he say that they be there .
They anchor at the mouth of a great river where the shore be as green a the green velvet .
A little distance from the river an immense desert stretch away .
The air be yellow ; the sun shone so hot , so hot a if it would burn the earth to ash , and the people be as black a the black jet .
They ride across the desert on tall camel ; the lion roar with thirst , and the great crocodile with their grey lizard head and sharp white teeth gap up out of the river .
` Shall we land here ? '
ask the dream-boy .
` No , ' say Little Lasse .
` The sun would burn u , and the lion and the crocodile would eat u up .
Let u travel to another part of the world . '
` We can travel back to Europe , ' say the dream-boy with the fair hair .
And with that they be there .
They come to a shore where it be all so cool and familiar and friendly .
There stand the tall birch tree with it droop leaf ; at the top sit the old crow , and at it foot creep the gardener 's black cat .
Not far away be a house which Little Lasse have see before ; near the house there be a garden , and in the garden a pea bed with long pea shell .
An old gardener with a green coat walk about and wonder if the cucumber be ripe .
Fylax be bark on the step , and when he saw Little Lasse he wag his tail .
Old Stina be milk the cow in the farmyard , and there be a very familiar lady in a check woollen shawl on her way to the bleach green to see if the clothes be bleach .
There be , too , a well-known gentleman in a yellow summer coat , with a long pipe in his mouth ; he be go to see if the reaper have cut the rye .
A boy and a girl be run on the shore and call out , ` Little Lasse !
Come home for bread-and-butter ! '
` Shall we land here ? '
ask the dream-boy , and he blink his blue eye roguishly .
` Come with me , and I shall ask mother to give you some bread-and-butter and a glass of milk , ' say Little Lasse .
` Wait a little , ' say the dream-boy .
And now Little Lasse saw that the kitchen door be open , and from within there be hear a low , pleasant frizzling , like that which be hear when one whisk yellow batter with a wooden ladle into a hot frying-pan .
` Perhaps we should sail back to Polynesia now ? '
say the happy dream-boy .
` No ; they be fry pancake in Europe just now , ' say Little Lasse ; and he want to jump ashore , but he could not .
The dream-boy have tie him with a chain of flower , so that he could not move .
And now all the little dream come about him , thousand and thousand of little child , and they make a ring around him and sing a little song : The world be very , very wide , Little Lasse , Lasse , And though you 've sail beyond the tide , You can never tell how wide It be on the other side , Lasse , Little Lasse .
You have find it cold and hot , Little Lasse , Lasse ; But in no land be God not , Lasse , Little Lasse .
Many men live there a here , But they all to God be dear , Little Lasse , Lasse .
When His angel be your guide , Little Lasse , Lasse , Then no harm can e'er betide , Even on the other side Where the wild beast wander .
But tell u now , Whene'er you roam , Do you not find the best be home Of all the land you 've look upon , Lasse , Little Lasse ?
When the dream have sing their song they skip away , and Nukku Matti carry Lasse back to the boat .
He lay there for a long time quite still , and he still hear the frying-pan frizzling at home of the fire , the frizzling be very plain , Little Lasse hear it quite near him ; and so he wake up and rub his eye .
There he lay in the boat , where he have fall asleep .
The wind have turn , and the boat have drift out with one wind and drift in with another while Little Lasse slept , and what Lasse thought be frizzle in a frying-pan be the low murmur of the wave a they wash against the stone on the shore .
But he be not altogether wrong , for the clear blue sea be like a great pan in which God 's sun all day make cake for good child .
Little Lasse rub the sleep out of his eye and look around him .
Everything be the same a before ; the crow in the birch tree , the cat on the grass , and the pea-shell fleet on the shore .
Some of the ship have founder , and some have drift back to land .
Hercules have come back with it cargo from Asia , The Flea have arrive from Polynesia , and the other part of the world be just where they be before .
Little Lasse do not know what to think .
He have so often be in that grotto in the ` Land of Nod ' and do not know what trick dream can play .
But Little Lasse do not trouble his head with such thing ; he gather together his boat and walk up the shore back to the house .
His brother and sister run to meet him , and call out from the distance , ` Where have you be so long , Lasse ?
Come home and get some bread-and-butter . '
The kitchen door stand open , and inside be hear a strange frizzling .
The gardener be near the gate , water the dill and parsley , the carrot and parsnip .
` Well , ' he say , ` where have Little Lasse be so long ? '
Little Lasse straighten himself up stiff , and answer : ' I have sail round the world in a pea-shell boat . '
` Oh ! '
say the gardener .
He have forget Dreamland .
But you have not forget it ; you know that it exist .
You know the beautiful grotto and the bright silver wall whose lustre never fade , the sparkle diamond which never grow dim , the music which never cease it low , soft murmur through the sweet evening twilight .
The airy fairy fancy of happy Dreamland never grow old ; they , like the glorious star above u , be always young .
Perhaps you have catch a glimpse of their ethereal wing a they fly around your pillow .
Perhaps you have meet the same dream-boy with the blue eye and the fair hair , the one who wear the red cap with the silver band and the white coat with pearl on the collar .
Perhaps he have take you to see all the country of the world and the people , the cold waste land and the burning desert , the many colour men and the wild creature in the sea and in the wood , so that you may earn many thing , but come gladly home again .
Yes , who know ?
Perhaps you also have sail round the wide world once in a pea-shell boat .
From Z. Topelius .
` Moti ' Once upon a time there be a youth call Moti , who be very big and strong , but the clumsy creature you can imagine .
So clumsy be he that he be always put his great foot into the bowl of sweet milk or curd which his mother set out on the floor to cool , always smash , upset , break , until at last his father say to him : ` Here , Moti , be fifty silver piece which be the saving of year ; take them and go and make your living or your fortune if you can . '
Then Moti start off one early spring morning with his thick staff over his shoulder , sing gaily to himself a he walk along .
In one way and another he get along very well until a hot evening when he come to a certain city where he enter the traveller ' ` serai ' or inn to pass the night .
Now a serai , you must know , be generally just a large square enclose by a high wall with an open colonnade along the inside all round to accommodate both men and beast , and with perhaps a few room in tower at the corner for those who be too rich or too proud to care about sleep by their own camel and horse .
Moti , of course , be a country lad and have live with cattle all his life , and he be n't rich and he be n't proud , so he just borrow a bed from the innkeeper , set it down beside an old buffalo who remind him of home , and in five minute be fast asleep .
In the middle of the night he wake , feel that he have be disturb , and put his hand under his pillow find to his horror that his bag of money have be steal .
He jump up quietly and begin to prowl around to see whether anyone seem to be awake , but , though he manage to arouse a few men and beast by fall over them , he walk in the shadow of the archway round the whole serai without come across a likely thief .
He be just about to give it up when he overheard two men whisper , and one laugh softly , and peer behind a pillar , he saw two Afghan horsedealers count out his bag of money !
Then Moti go back to bed !
In the morning Moti follow the two Afghans outside the city to the horsemarket in which they horse be offer for sale .
Choosing the best-looking horse amongst them he go up to it and say : ` Is this horse for sale ?
may I try it ? '
and , the merchant assent , he scramble up on it back , dug in his heel , and off they fly .
Now Moti have never be on a horse in his life , and have so much ado to hold on with both hand as well a with both leg that the animal go just where it like , and very soon break into a break-neck gallop and make straight back to the serai where it have spend the last few night .
` This will do very well , ' thought Moti a they whirl in at the entrance .
As soon a the horse have arrive at it table it stop of it own accord and Moti immediately roll off ; but he jump up at once , tie the beast up , and call for some breakfast .
Presently the Afghans appear , out of breath and furious , and claim the horse .
` What do you mean ? '
cry Moti , with his mouth full of rice , ` it 's my horse ; I pay you fifty piece of silver for it -- quite a bargain , I 'm sure ! '
` Nonsense !
it be our horse , ' answer one of the Afghans begin to untie the bridle .
` Leave off , ' shout Moti , seize his staff ; ` if you do n't let my horse alone I 'll crack your skull !
you thieve !
I know you !
Last night you take my money , so to-day I take your horse ; that 's fair enough ! '
Now the Afghans begin to look a little uncomfortable , but Moti seem so determine to keep the horse that they resolve to appeal to the law , so they go off and lay a complaint before the king that Moti have steal one of their horse and would not give it up nor pay for it .
Presently a soldier come to summon Moti to the king ; and , when he arrive and make his obeisance , the king begin to question him a to why he have gallop off with the horse in this fashion .
But Moti declare that he have get the animal in exchange for fifty piece of silver , whilst the horse merchant vow that the money they have on them be what they have receive for the sale of other horse ; and in one way and another the dispute get so confuse that the king -LRB- who really think that Moti have steal the horse -RRB- say at last , ` Well , I tell you what I will do .
I will lock something into this box before me , and if he guess what it be , the horse be his , and if he do n't then it be yours . '
To this Moti agree , and the king arose and go out alone by a little door at the back of the Court , and presently come back clasp something closely wrap up in a cloth under his robe , slip it into the little box , lock the box , and set it up where all might see .
` Now , ' say the king to Moti , ` guess ! '
It happen that when the king have open the door behind him , Moti notice that there be a garden outside : without wait for the king 's return he begin to think what could be get out of the garden small enough to be shut in the box .
` Is it likely to be a fruit or a flower ?
No , not a flower this time , for he clasp it too tight .
Then it must be a fruit or a stone .
Yet not a stone , because he would n't wrap a dirty stone in his nice clean cloth .
Then it be a fruit !
And a fruit without much scent , or else he would be afraid that I might smell it .
Now what fruit without much scent be in season just now ?
When I know that I shall have guess the riddle ! '
As have be say before , Moti be a country lad , and be accustom to work in his father 's garden .
He know all the common fruit , so he think he ought to be able to guess right ; but so a not to let it seem too easy , he gaze up at the ceiling with a puzzled expression , and look down at the floor with an air or wisdom and his finger press against his forehead , and then he say , slowly , with his eye on the king , -- ` It be freshly pluck !
It be round and it be red !
It be a pomegranate ! '
Now the king know nothing about fruit except that they be good to eat ; and , a for season , he ask for whatever fruit he want whenever he want it , and saw that he get it ; so to him Moti 's guess be like a miracle , and clear proof not only of his wisdom but of his innocence , for it be a pomegranate that he have put into the box .
Of course when the king marvel and praise Moti 's wisdom , everybody else do so too ; and , whilst the Afghans go off crestfallen , Moti take the horse and enter the king 's service .
Very soon after this , Moti , who continue to live in the serai , come back one wet and stormy evening to find that his precious horse have stray .
Nothing remain of him but a broken halter cord , and no one know what have become of him .
After inquire of everyone who be likely to know , Moti seize the cord and his big staff and sallied out to look for him .
Away and away he tramp out of the city and into the neighbouring forest , track hoof-mark in the mud .
Presently it grow late , but still Moti wander on until suddenly in the gathering darkness he come right upon a tiger who be contentedly eat his horse .
` You thief ! '
shriek Moti , and run up and , just a the tiger , in astonishment , drop a bone -- whack !
come Moti 's staff on his head with such good will that the beast be half stun and could hardly breathe or see .
Then Moti continue to shower upon him blow and abuse until the poor tiger could hardly stand , whereupon his tormentor tie the end of the broken halter round his neck and drag him back to the serai .
` If you have my horse , ' he say , ' I will at least have you , that 's fair enough ! '
And he tie him up securely by the head and heel , much a he use to tie the horse ; then , the night be far go , he fling himself beside him and sleep soundly .
You can not imagine anything like the fright of the people in the serai , when they wake up and find a tiger -- very batter but still a tiger -- securely tethered amongst themselves and their beast !
Men gather in group talk and exclaiming , and find fault with the innkeeper for allow such a dangerous beast into the serai , and all the while the innkeeper be just as troubled a the rest , and none dare go near the place where the tiger stand blink miserably on everyone , and where Moti lay stretch out snore like thunder .
At last news reach the king that Moti have exchange his horse for a live tiger ; and the monarch himself come down , half disbelieve the tale , to see if it be really true .
Someone at last awaked Moti with the news that his royal master be come ; and he arise yawning , and be soon delightedly explain and show off his new possession .
The king , however , do not share his pleasure at all , but call up a soldier to shoot the tiger , much to the relief of all the inmate of the serai except Moti .
If the king , however , be before convinced that Moti be one of the wise of men , he be now still more convinced that he be the brave , and he increase his pay a hundredfold , so that our hero think that he be the lucky of men .
A week or two after this incident the king sent for Moti , who on arrival find his master in despair .
A neighbouring monarch , he explain , who have many more soldier than he , have declare war against him , and he be at his wit ' end , for he have neither money to buy him off nor soldier enough to fight him -- what be he to do ?
` If that be all , do n't you trouble , ' say Moti .
` Turn out your men , and I 'll go with them , and we 'll soon bring this robber to reason . '
The king begin to revive at these hopeful word , and take Moti off to his stable where he bid him choose for himself any horse he like .
There be plenty of fine horse in the stall , but to the king 's astonishment Moti choose a poor little rat of a pony that be use to carry grass and water for the rest of the stable .
` But why do you choose that beast ? '
say the king .
` Well , you see , your majesty , ' reply Moti , ` there be so many chance that I may fall off , and if I choose one of your fine big horse I shall have so far to fall that I shall probably break my leg or my arm , if not my neck , but if I fall off this little beast I ca n't hurt myself much . '
A very comical sight be Moti when he ride out to the war .
The only weapon he carry be his staff , and to help him to keep his balance on horseback he have tie to each of his ankle a big stone that nearly touch the ground a he sit astride the little pony .
The rest of the king 's cavalry be not very numerous , but they prance along in armour on fine horse .
Behind them come a great rabble of men on foot arm with all sort of weapon , and last of all be the king with his attendant , very nervous and ill at ease .
So the army start .
They have not very far to go , but Moti 's little pony , weight with a heavy man and two big rock , soon begin to lag behind the cavalry , and would have lag behind the infantry too , only they be not very anxious to be too early in the fight , and hang back so a to give Moti plenty of time .
The young man jog along more and more slowly for some time , until at last , get impatient at the slowness of the pony , he give him such a tremendous thwack with his staff that the pony completely lose his temper and bolt .
