First one stone become untied and roll away in a cloud of dust to one side of the road , whilst Moti nearly roll off too , but clasp his steed valiantly by it ragged mane , and , drop his staff , hold on for dear life .
Then , fortunately the other rock break away from his other leg and roll thunderously down a neighbouring ravine .
Meanwhile the advanced cavalry have barely time to draw to one side when Moti come dash by , yell bloodthirsty threat to his pony : ` You wait till I get hold of you !
I 'll skin you alive !
I 'll wring your neck !
I 'll break every bone in your body ! '
The cavalry think that this dreadful language be mean for the enemy , and be fill with admiration of his courage .
Many of their horse too be quite upset by this whirlwind that gallop howl through their midst , and in a few minute , after a little plunging and rearing and kicking , the whole troop be follow on Moti 's heel .
Far in advance , Moti continue his wild career .
Presently in his course he come to a great field of castor-oil plant , ten or twelve foot high , big and bushy , but quite green and soft .
Hoping to escape from the back of his fiery steed Moti grasp one in passing , but it root give way , and he dash on , with the whole plant look like a young tree flourish in his grip .
The enemy be in battle array , advance over the plain , their king with them confident and cheerful , when suddenly from the front come a desperate rider at a furious gallop .
` Sire ! '
he cry , ` save yourself !
the enemy be come ! '
` What do you mean ? '
say the king .
` Oh , sire ! '
pant the messenger , ` fly at once , there be no time to lose .
Foremost of the enemy rid a mad giant at a furious gallop .
He flourish a tree for a club and be wild with anger , for a he go he cry , `` You wait till I get hold of you !
I 'll skin you alive !
I 'll wring your neck !
I 'll break every bone in your body ! ''
Others ride behind , and you will do well to retire before this whirlwind of destruction come upon you . '
Just then out of a cloud of dust in the distance the king saw Moti approach at a hard gallop , look indeed like a giant compare with the little beast he ride , whirl his castor-oil plant , which in the distance might have be an oak tree , and the sound of his revilings and shouting come down upon the breeze !
Behind him the dust cloud move to the sound of the thunder of hoof , whilst here and there flash the glitter of steel .
The sight and the sound struck terror into the king , and , turn his horse , he flee at top speed , think that a regiment of yell giant be upon him ; and all his force follow him as fast a they might go .
One fat officer alone could not keep up on foot with that mad rush , and a Moti come gallop up he fling himself on the ground in abject fear .
This be too much for Moti 's excited pony , who shy so suddenly that Moti go fly over his head like a sky rocket , and alight right on the top of his fat foe .
Quickly regain his foot Moti begin to swing his plant round his head and to shout : ` Where be your men ?
Bring them up and I 'll kill them .
My regiment !
Come on , the whole lot of you !
Where 's your king ?
Bring him to me .
Here be all my fine fellow come up and we 'll each pull up a tree by the root and lay you all flat and your house and town and everything else !
Come on ! '
But the poor fat officer could do nothing but squat on his knee with his hand together , gasp .
At last , when he get his breath , Moti send him off to bring his king , and to tell him that if he be reasonable his life should be spar .
Off the poor man go , and by the time the troop of Moti 's side have come up and arrange themselves to look as formidable a possible , he return with his king .
The latter be very humble and apologetic , and promise never to make war any more , to pay a large sum of money , and altogether do whatever his conqueror wish .
So the army on both side go rejoice home , and this be really the making of the fortune of clumsy Moti , who live long and contrive always to be look up to a a fountain of wisdom , valour , and discretion by all except his relation , who could never understand what he have do to be consider so much wise than anyone else .
A Pushto Story .
The Enchanted Deer A young man be out walk one day in Erin , lead a stout cart-horse by the bridle .
He be think of his mother and how poor they be since his father , who be a fisherman , have be drown at sea , and wonder what he should do to earn a living for both of them .
Suddenly a hand be lay on his shoulder , and a voice say to him : ` Will you sell me your horse , son of the fisherman ? '
and look up he behold a man stand in the road with a gun in his hand , a falcon on his shoulder , and a dog by his side .
` What will you give me for my horse ? '
ask the youth .
` Will you give me your gun , and your dog , and your falcon ? ' '
I will give them , ' answer the man , and he take the horse , and the youth take the gun and the dog and the falcon , and go home with them .
But when his mother hear what he have do she be very angry , and beat him with a stick which she have in her hand .
` That will teach you to sell my property , ' say she , when her arm be quite tired , but Ian her son answer her nothing , and go off to his bed , for he be very sore .
That night he rise softly , and leave the house carry the gun with him . '
I will not stay here to be beat , ' think he , and he walk and he walk and he walk , till it be day again , and he be hungry and look about him to see if he could get anything to eat .
Not very far off be a farm-house , so he go there , and knock at the door , and the farmer and his wife beg him to come in , and share their breakfast .
` Ah , you have a gun , ' say the farmer a the young man place it in a corner .
` That be well , for a deer come every evening to eat my corn , and I can not catch it .
It be fortune that have send you to me . ' '
I will gladly remain and shoot the deer for you , ' reply the youth , and that night he hide himself and watch till the deer come to the cornfield ; then he lift his gun to his shoulder and be just go to pull the trigger , when , behold !
instead of a deer , a woman with long black hair be stand there .
At this sight his gun almost drop from his hand in surprise , but a he look , there be the deer eat the corn again .
And thrice this happen , till the deer run away over the moor , and the young man after her .
On they go , on and on and one , till they reach a cottage which be thatch with heather .
With a bound the deer sprang on the roof , and lay down where none could see her , but a she do so she call out , ` Go in , fisher 's son , and eat and drink while you may . '
So he enter and find food and wine on the table , but no man , for the house belong to some robber , who be still away at their wicked business .
After Ian , the fisher 's son , have eat all he want , he hide himself behind a great cask , and very soon he hear a noise , a of men come through the heather , and the small twig snap under their foot .
From his dark corner he could see into the room , and he count four and twenty of them , all big , cross-looking men .
` Some one have be eat our dinner , ' cry they , ` and there be hardly enough for ourselves . '
` It be the man who be lie under the cask , ' answer the leader .
` Go and kill him , and then come and eat your food and sleep , for we must be off betimes in the morning . '
So four of them kill the fisher 's son and leave him , and then go to bed .
By sunrise they be all out of the house , for they have far to go .
And when they have disappear the deer come off the roof , to where the dead man lay , and she shake her head over him , and wax fell from her ear , and he jump up as well a ever .
` Trust me and eat a you do before , and no harm shall happen to you , ' say she .
So Ian ate and drank , and fell sound asleep under the cask .
In the even the robber arrive very tired , and cross than they have be yesterday , for their luck have turn and they have bring back scarcely anything .
` Someone have eat our dinner again , ' cry they .
` It be the man under the barrel , ' answer the captain .
` Let four of you go and kill him , but first slay the other four who pretend to kill him last night and do n't because he be still alive . '
Then Ian be kill a second time , and after the rest of the robber have eat , they lay down and sleep till morning .
No sooner be their face touch with the sun 's ray than they be up and off .
Then the deer enter and drop the heal wax on the dead man , and he be as well a ever .
By this time he do not mind what befall him , so sure be he that the deer would take care of him , and in the evening that which have happen before happen again -- the four robber be put to death and the fisher 's son also , but because there be no food leave for them to eat , they be nearly mad with rage , and begin to quarrel .
From quarrel they go on to fight , and fought so hard that by and bye they be all stretch dead on the floor .
Then the deer enter , and the fisher 's son be restore to life , and bid him follow her , she run on to a little white cottage where dwelt an old woman and her son , who be thin and dark .
` Here I must leave you , ' say the deer , ` but to-morrow meet me at midday in the church that be yonder . '
And jump across the stream , she vanish into a wood .
Next day he set out for the church , but the old woman of the cottage have go before him , and have stick an enchanted stick call ` the spike of hurt ' in a crack of the door , so that he would brush against it a he step across the threshold .
Suddenly he felt so sleepy that he could not stand up , and throw himself on the ground he sink into a deep slumber , not know that the dark lad be watch him .
Nothing could waken him , not even the sound of sweet music , nor the touch of a lady who bend over him .
A sad look come on her face , a she saw it be no use , and at last she give it up , and lift his arm , write her name across the side -- ` the daughter of the king of the town under the wave . ' '
I will come to-morrow , ' she whisper , though he could not hear her , and she go sorrowfully away .
Then he awake , and the dark lad tell him what have befall him , and he be very grieved .
But the dark lad do not tell him of the name that be write underneath his arm .
On the following morning the fisher 's son again go to the church , determine that he would not go to sleep , whatever happen .
But in his hurry to enter he touch with his hand the spike of hurt , and sink down where he stand , wrap in slumber .
A second time the air be fill with music , and the lady come in , step softly , but though she lay his head on her knee , and comb his hair with a golden comb , his eye open not .
Then she burst into tear , and place a beautifully wrought box in his pocket she go her way .
The next day the same thing befell the fisher 's son , and this time the lady weep more bitterly than before , for she say it be the last chance , and she would never be allow to come any more , for home she must go .
As soon a the lady have depart the fisher 's son awoke , and the dark lad tell him of her visit , and how he would never see her as long a he live .
At this the fisher 's son felt the cold creep up to his heart , yet he know the fault have not be his that sleep have overtake him . '
I will search the whole world through till I find her , ' cry he , and the dark lad laugh a he hear him .
But the fisher 's son take no heed , and off he go , follow the sun day after day , till his shoe be in hole and his foot be sore from the journey .
Nought do he see but the bird that make their nest in the tree , not so much a a goat or a rabbit .
On and on and on he go , till suddenly he come upon a little house , with a woman stand outside it .
` All hail , fisher 's son ! '
say she . '
I know what you be seek ; enter in and rest and eat , and to-morrow I will give you what help I can , and send you on your way . '
Gladly do Ian the fisher 's son accept her offer , and all that day he rest , and the woman give him ointment to put on his foot , which heal his sore .
At daybreak he get up , ready to be go , and the woman bid him farewell , say : ' I have a sister who dwell on the road which you must travel .
It be a long road , and it would take you a year and a day to reach it , but put on these old brown shoe with hole all over them , and you will be there before you know it .
Then shake them off , and turn their toe to the know , and their heel to the unknown , and they will come home of themselves . '
The fisher 's son do a the woman tell him , and everything happen just a she have say .
But at part the second sister say to him , a she give him another pair of shoe : ` Go to my third sister , for she have a son who be keeper of the bird of the air , and send them to sleep when night come .
He be very wise , and perhaps he can help you . '
Then the young man thank her , and go to the third sister .
The third sister be very kind , but have no counsel to give him , so he eat and drink and wait till her son come home , after he have send all the bird to sleep .
He think a long while after his mother have tell him the young man 's story , and at last he say that he be hungry , and the cow must be kill , a he want some supper .
So the cow be kill and the meat cook , and a bag make of it red skin .
` Now get into the bag , ' bid the son , and the young man get in and take his gun with him , but the dog and the falcon he leave outside .
The keeper of the bird draw the string at the top of the bag , and leave it to finish his supper , when in fly an eagle through the open door , and pick the bag up in her claw and carry it through the air to an island .
There be nothing to eat on the island , and the fisher 's son think he would die of food , when he remember the box that the lady have put in his pocket .
He open the lid , and three tiny little bird fly out , and flap their wing they ask , ` Good master , be there anything we can do for thee ? '
` Bear me to the kingdom of the king under the wave , ' he answer , and one little bird fly on to his head , and the others perch on each of his shoulder , and he shut his eye , and in a moment there he be in the country under the sea .
Then the bird fly away , and the young man look about him , his heart beat fast at the thought that here dwell the lady whom he have seek all the world over .
He walk on through the street , and presently he reach the house of a weaver who be stand at his door , rest from his work .
` You be a stranger here , that be plain , ' say the weaver , ` but come in , and I will give you food and drink . '
And the young man be glad , for he know not where to go , and they sit and talk till it grow late .
` Stay with me , I pray , for I love company and be lonely , ' observe the weaver at last , and he point to a bed in a corner , where the fisher 's son throw himself , and sleep till dawn .
` There be to be a horse-race in the town to-day , ' remark the weaver , ` and the winner be to have the king 's daughter to wife . '
The young man tremble with excitement at the news , and his voice shook a he answer : ` That will be a prize indeed , I should like to see the race . '
` Oh , that be quite easy -- anyone can go , ' reply the weaver . '
I would take you myself , but I have promise to weave this cloth for the king . '
` That be a pity , ' return the young man politely , but in his heart he rejoice , for he wish to be alone .
Leaving the house , he enter a grove of tree which stand behind , and take the box from his pocket .
He raise the lid , and out fly the three little bird .
` Good master , what shall we do for thee ? '
ask they , and he answer , ` Bring me the fine horse that ever be see , and the grand dress , and glass shoe . '
` They be here , master , ' say the bird , and so they be , and never have the young man see anything so splendid .
Mounting the horse he ride into the ground where the horse be assemble for the great race , and take his place among them .
Many good beast be there which have win many race , but the horse of the fisher 's son leave them all behind , and he be first at the win post .
The king 's daughter wait for him in vain to claim his prize , for he go back to the wood , and get off his horse , and put on his old clothes , and bid the box place some gold in his pocket .
After that he go back to the weaver 's house , and tell him that the gold have be give him by the man who have win the race , and that the weaver might have it for his kindness to him .
Now a nobody have appear to demand the hand of the princess , the king order another race to be run , and the fisher 's son rode into the field still more splendidly dress than he be before , and easily distance everybody else .
But again he leave the prize unclaimed , and so it happen on the third day , when it seem a if all the people in the kingdom be gather to see the race , for they be fill with curiosity to know who the winner could be .
` If he will not come of his own free will , he must be bring , ' say the king , and the messenger who have see the face of the victor be send to seek him in every street of the town .
This take many day , and when at last they find the young man in the weaver 's cottage , he be so dirty and ugly and have such a strange appearance , that they declare he could not be the winner they have be search for , but a wicked robber who have murder ever so many people , but have always manage to escape .
` Yes , it must be the robber , ' say the king , when the fisher 's son be lead into his presence ; ` build a gallows at once and hang him in the sight of all my subject , that they may behold him suffer the punishment of his crime . '
So the gallows be build upon a high platform , and the fisher 's son mount the step up to it , and turn at the top to make the speech that be expect from every doom man , innocent or guilt .
As he speak he happen to raise his arm , and the king 's daughter , who be there at her father 's side , saw the name which she have write under it .
With a shriek she spring from her seat , and the eye of the spectator be turned towards her .
` Stop !
stop ! '
she cry , hardly know what she say .
` If that man be hang there be not a soul in the kingdom but shall die also . '
And run up to where the fisher 's son be stand , she take him by the hand , say , ` Father , this be no robber or murderer , but the victor in the three race , and he loose the spell that be lay upon me . '
Then , without wait for a reply , she conduct him into the palace , and he bath in a marble bath , and all the dirt that the fairy have put upon him disappear like magic , and when he have dress himself in the fine garment the princess have send to him , he look a match for any king 's daughter in Erin .
He go down into the great hall where she be await him , and they have much to tell each other but little time to tell it in , for the king her father , and the prince who be visit him , and all the people of the kingdom be still in their place expect her return .
` How do you find me out ? '
she whisper a they go down the passage .
` The bird in the box tell me , ' answer he , but he could say no more , a they step out into the open space that be crowd with people .
There the prince stop . '
O king ! '
she say , turn towards them , ` if one of you be kill to-day , the rest would fly ; but this man put his trust in me , and have his head cut off three time .
Because he have do this , I will marry him rather than one of you , who have come hither to wed me , for many king here seek to free me from the spell , but none could do it save Ian the fisher 's son . '
From ` Popular Tales of the West Highlands . '
A Fish Story Perhaps you think that fish be always fish , and never live anywhere except in the water , but if you go to Australia and talk to the black people in the sandy desert in the centre of the country , you would learn something quite different .
They would tell you that long , long ago you would have meet fish on the land , wander from place to place , and hunt all sort of animal , and if you consider how fish be make , you will understand how difficult this must have be and how clever they be to do it .
Indeed , so clever be they that they might have be hunt still if a terrible thing have not happen .
One day the whole fish tribe come back very tire from a hunt expedition , and look about for a nice , cool spot in which to pitch their camp .
It be very hot , and they think that they could not find a more comfortable place than under the branch of a large tree which grow by the bank of a river .
So they make their fire to cook some food , right on the edge of a steep bank , which have a deep pool of water lie beneath it at the bottom .
While the food be cook they all stretch themselves lazily out under the tree , and be just drop off to sleep when a big black cloud which they have never notice spread over the sun , and heavy drop of rain begin to fall , so that the fire be almost put out , and that , you know , be a very serious thing in savage country where they have no match , for it be very hard to light it again .
To make matter bad , an icy wind begin to blow , and the poor fish be chill right through their body .
` This will never do , ' say Thuggai , the old of the fish tribe .
` We shall die of cold unless we can light the fire again , ' and he bid his son rub two stick together in the hope of kindle a flame , but though they rub till they be tire , not a spark could they produce .
` Let me try , ' cry Biernuga , the bony fish , but he have no good luck , and no more have Kumbal , the bream , nor any of the rest .
` It be no use , ' exclaim Thuggai , at last .
` The wood be too wet .
We must just sit and wait till the sun come out again and dry it . '
Then a very little fish indeed , not more than four inch long and the young of the tribe , bow himself before Thuggai , say , ` Ask my father , Guddhu the cod , to light the fire .
He be skilled in magic more than most fish . '
So Thuggai ask him , and Guddhu strip some piece of bark off a tree , and place them on top of the smouldering ash .
Then he kneel by the side of the fire and blew at it for a long while , till slowly the feeble red glow become a little strong and the edge of the bark show sign of curl up .
When the rest of the tribe saw this they press close , keep their back towards the piercing wind , but Guddhu tell them they must go to the other side , a he want the wind to fan his fire .
By and by the spark grow into a flame , and a merry crackling be hear .
` More wood , ' cry Guddhi , and they all run and gather wood and heap it on the flame , which leap and roar and sputter .
` We shall soon be warm now , ' say the people one to another .
` Truly Guddhu be great ' ; and they crowd round again , close and closer .
Suddenly , with a shriek , a blast of wind sweep down from the hill and blow the fire out towards them .
They spring back hurriedly , quite forget where they stand , and all fell down the bank , each tumble over the other , till they roll into the pool that lay below .
Oh , how cold it be in that dark water on which the sun never shone !
Then in an instant they felt warm again , for the fire , drive by the strong wind , have follow them right down to the bottom of the pool , where it burn as brightly a ever .
And the fish gather round it a they have do on the top of the cliff , and find the flame as hot a before , and that fire never go out , like those upon land , but keep burning for ever .
So now you know why , if you dive deep down below the cold surface of the water on a frosty day , you will find it comfortable and pleasant underneath , and be quite sorry that you can not stay there .
Australian Folk Tale .
The Wonderful Tune .
Maurice Connor be the king , and that 's no small word , of all the piper in Munster .
He could play jig and reel without end , and Ollistrum 's March , and the Eagle 's Whistle , and the Hen 's Concert , and odd tune of every sort and kind .
But he know one far more surprising than the rest , which have in it the power to set everything dead or alive dancing .
In what way he learn it be beyond my knowledge for he be mighty cautious about tell how he come by so wonderful a tune .
At the very first note of that tune the shoe begin shake upon the foot of all how heard it -- old or young , it matter not -- just a if the shoe have the ague ; then the foot begin go , go , go from under them , and at last up and away with them , dance like mad , whisk here , there , and everywhere , like a straw in a storm -- there be no halt while the music last .
Not a fair , nor a wedding , nor a feast in the seven parish round , be count worth the speaking of without ` blind Maurice and his pipe . '
His mother , poor woman , use to lead him about from one place to another just like a dog .
Down through Iveragh , Maurice Connor and his mother be take their round .
Beyond all other place Iveragh be the place for stormy coast and steep mountain , a proper a spot it be a any in Ireland to get yourself drown , or your neck break on the land , should you prefer that .
But , notwithstanding , in Ballinskellig Bay there be a neat bit of ground , well fit for diversion , and down from it , towards the water , be a clean smooth piece of strand , the dead image of a calm summer 's sea on a moonlight night , with just the curl of the small wave upon it .
Here be be that Maurice 's music have bring from all part a great gathering of the young men and the young woman ; for 't be not every day the strand of Trafraska be stir up by the voice of a bagpipe .
The dance begin ; and a pretty a dance it be a ever be dance .
` Brave music , ' say everybody , ` and well do , ' when Maurice stop .
` More power to your elbow , Maurice , and a fair wind in the bellow , ' cry Paddy Dorman , a hump-backed dancing master , who be there to keep order . ''
Tis a pity , ' say he , ` if we 'd let the piper run dry after such music ; ` twould be a disgrace to Iveragh , that do n't come on it since the week of the three Sundays . '
So , a well become him , for he be always a decent man , say he , ` Did you drink , piper ? ' '
I will , sir , ' say Maurice , answer the question on the safe side , for you never yet know piper or schoolmaster who refuse his drink .
` What will you drink , Maurice ? '
say Paddy .
` I 'm no way particular , ' say Maurice ; ' I drink anything , bar raw water ; but if it 's all the same to you , Mister Dorman , may be you would n't lend me the loan of a glass of whisky . '
` I 've no glass , Maurice , ' say Paddy ; ` I 've only the bottle . '
` Let that be no hindrance , ' answered Maurice ; ` my mouth just hold a glass to the drop ; often I 've try it sure . '
So Paddy Dorman trust him with the bottle -- more fool be he ; and , to his cost , he find that though Maurice 's mouth might not hold more than the glass at one time , yet , owe to the hole in his throat , it take many a filling .
` That be no bad whisky neither , ' say Maurice , hand back the empty bottle .
` By the holy frost , then ! '
say Paddy , '' ti but cold comfort there 's in that bottle now ; and 't be your word we must take for the strength of the whisky , for you 've leave u no sample to judge by ' ; and to be sure Maurice have not .
Now I need not tell any gentleman or lady that if he or she be to drink an honest bottle of whisky at one pull , it be not at all the same thing a drink a bottle of water ; and in the whole course of my life I never know more than five men who could do so without be the worse .
Of these Maurice Connor be not one , though he have a stiff head enough of his own .
Do n't think I blame him for it ; but true be the word that say , ` When liquor 's in sense be out ' ; and puff , at a breath , out he blast his wonderful tune .
'T be really then beyond all belief or tell the dancing .
Maurice himself could not keep quiet ; stagger now on one leg , now on the other , and roll about like a ship in a cross sea , try to humour the tune .
There be his mother , too , move her old bone as light a the young girl of them all ; but her dancing , no , nor the dancing of all the rest , be not worthy the speak about to the work that be go on down upon the strand .
Every inch of it cover with all manner of fish jumping and plunge about to the music , and every moment more and more would tumble in and out of the water , charm by the wonderful tune .
Crabs of monstrous size spun round and round on one claw with the nimbleness of a dancing master , and twirl and toss their other claw about like limb that do not belong to them .
It be a sight surprising to behold .
But perhaps you may have heard of Father Florence Conry , a pleasant a man a one would wish to drink with of a hot summer 's day ; and he have rhyme out all about the dancing fish so neatly that it would be a thousand pity not to give you his verse ; so here they be in English : The big seal in motion , Like wave of the ocean , Or gouty foot prance , Came head the gay fish , Crabs , lobster , and cray-fish , Determined on dancing .
The sweet sound they follow , The gasp cod swallow 'd -- 'T be wonderful , really ; And turbot and flounder , ` Mid fish that be rounder , Just caper 'd a gaily .
John-dories come trip ; Dull hake , by their skipping , To frisk it seem 'd give ; Bright mackrel go spring , Like small rainbow wing Their flight up to heaven .
The whiting and haddock Left salt water paddock This dance to be put in ; Where skate with flat face Edged out some old plaice ; But sol keep their footing .
Sprats and herring in power Of silvery shower All number out-numbered ; And great ling so lengthy Was there in such plenty The shore be encumber 'd .
The scallop and oyster Their two shell do roister , Like castanets flit ; While limpet move clearly , And rock very nearly With laughter be split .
Never be such a hullabaloo in this world , before or since ; 't be a if heaven and earth be come together ; and all out of Maurice Connor 's wonderful tune !
In the height of all these doings , what should there be dance among the outlandish set of fish but a beautiful young woman -- as beautiful a the dawn of day !
She have a cock hat upon her head ; from under it her long green hair -- just the colour of the sea -- fell down behind , without hindrance to her dancing .
Her teeth be like row of pearl ; her lip for all the world look like red coral ; and she have a shin gown pale green a the hollow of the wave , with little row of purple and red seaweed settle out upon it ; for you never yet saw a lady , under the water or over the water , who have not a good notion of dress herself out .
Up she dance at last to Maurice , who be fling his foot from under him as fast a hop -- for nothing in this world could keep still while that tune of his be go on -- and say she to him , chant it out with a voice as sweet a honey : I 'm a lady of honour Who live in the sea ; Come down , Maurice Connor , And be marry to me .
Silver plate and gold dish You shall have , and shall be The king of the fish , When you 're marry to me .
Drink be strong in Maurice 's head , and out he chant in return for her great civility .
It be not every lady , may be , that would be after make such an offer to a blind piper ; therefore 't be only right in him to give her as good a she give herself , so say Maurice : I 'm oblige to you , madam : Off a gold dish or plate , If a king , and I have 'em , I could dine in great state .
With your own father 's daughter I 'd be sure to agree , But to drink the salt water Would n't do so with me !
The lady look at him quite amaze , and swing her head from side to side like a great scholar , ` Well , ' say she , ` Maurice , if you 're not a poet , where be poetry to be find ? '
In this way they keep on at it , frame high compliment ; one answer the other , and their foot go with the music as fast a their tongue .
All the fish kept dancing , too ; Maurice hear the clatter and be afraid to stop playing lest it might be displease to the fish , and not know what so many of them may take it into their head to do to him if they get vexed .
Well , the lady with the green hair keep on coax Maurice with soft speech , till at last she over persuade him to promise to marry her , and be king over the fish , great and small .
Maurice be well fit to be their king , if they want one that could make them dance ; and he surely would drink , bar the salt water , with any fish of them all .
When Maurice 's mother saw him with that unnatural thing in the form of a green-haired lady a his guide , and he and she dance down together so lovingly to the water 's edge , through the thick of the fish , she call out after him to stop and come back .
` Oh , then , ' say she , ` a if I be not widow enough before , there he be go away from me to be marry to that scaly woman .
And who know but 't be grandmother I may be to a hake or a cod -- Lord help and pity me , but 't be a mighty unnatural thing !
And my be 't be boil and eat my own grandchild I 'll be , with a bit of salt butter , and I not know it !
Oh , Maurice , Maurice , if there 's any love or nature leave in you , come back to your own ould mother , who rear you like a decent Christian ! '
Then the poor woman begin to cry and sob so finely that it would do anyone good to hear her .
Maurice be not long get to the rim of the water .
There he keep play and dance on a if nothing be the matter , and a great thundering wave come in towards him ready to swallow him up alive ; but a he could not see it , he do not fear it .
His mother it be who saw it plainly through the big tear that be roll down her cheek ; and though she saw it , and her heart be ache as much a ever mother 's heart ache for a son , she keep dance , dance all the time for the bare life of her .
Certain it be she could not help it , for Maurice never stop play that wonderful tune of his .
He only turn his ear to the sound of his mother 's voice , fear it might put him out in his step , and all the answer he make back be , ` Whisht with you mother -- sure I 'm go to be king over the fish down in the sea , and for a token of luck , and a sign that I 'm alive and well , I 'll send you in , every twelvemonth on this day , a piece of burn wood to Trafraska . '
Maurice have not the power to say a word more , for the strange lady with the green hair , see the wave just upon them , cover him up with herself in a thing like a cloak with a big hood to it , and the wave curling over twice as high a their head , burst upon the strand , with a rush and a roar that might be hear as far a Cape Clear .
That day twelvemonth the piece of burn wood come ashore in Trafraska .
It be a queer thing for Maurice to think of send all the way from the bottom of the sea .
A gown or a pair of shoe would have be something like a present for his poor mother ; but he have say it , and he keep his word .
The bit of burn wood regularly come ashore on the appoint day for as good , ay , and good than a hundred year .
The day be now forget , and may be that be the reason why people say how Maurice Connor have stop send the luck-token to his mother .
Poor woman , she do not live to get as much a one of them ; for what through the loss of Maurice , and the fear of eat her own grandchild , she die in three week after the dance .
Some say it be the fatigue that kill her , but whichever it be , Mrs. Connor be decently bury with her own people .
Seafaring people have often hear , off the coast of Kerry , on a still night , the sound of music come up from the water ; and some , who have have good ear , could plainly distinguish Maurice Connor 's voice sing these word to his pipe -- Beautiful shore , with thy spread strand , Thy crystal water , and diamond sand ; Never would I have part from thee , But for the sake of my fair ladie .
From ` Fairy Tales and Traditions of the South of Ireland . '
The Rich Brother and the Poor Brother There be once a rich old man who have two son , and a his wife be dead , the elder live with him , and help him to look after his property .
For a long time all go well ; the young man get up very early in the morning , and work hard all day , and at the end of every week his father count up the money they have make , and rub his hand with delight , a he saw how big the pile of gold in the strong iron chest be become .
` It will soon be full now , and I shall have to buy a large one , ' he say to himself , and so busy be he with the thought of his money , that he do not notice how bright his son 's face have grow , nor how he sometimes start when he be speak to , a if his mind be far away .
One day , however , the old man go to the city on business , which he have not do for three year at least .
It be market day , and he meet with many people he know , and it be get quite late when he turn into the inn yard , and bid an ostler saddle his horse , and bring it round directly .
While he be wait in the hall , the landlady come up for a gossip , and after a few remark about the weather and the vineyard she ask him how he like his new daughter-in-law , and whether he have be surprise at the marriage .
The old man star a he listen to her .
` Daughter-in-law ?
Marriage ? '
say he . '
I do n't know what you be talk about !
I 've get no daughter-in-law , and nobody have be marry lately , that I ever heard of . '
Now this be exactly what the landlady , who be very curious , want to find out ; but she put on a look of great alarm , and exclaim : ` Oh , dear !
I hope I have not make mischief .
I have no idea -- or , of course , I would not have speak -- but ' -- and here she stop and fumble with her apron , a if she be greatly embarrass .
` As you have say so much you will have to say a little more , ' retort the old man , a suspicion of what she mean dart across him ; and the woman , nothing loth , answer a before .
` Ah , it be not all for buy or sell that your handsome son have be come to town every week these many month past .
And not by the short way , either !
No , it be over the river he ride , and across the hill and past the cottage of Miguel the vine-keeper , whose daughter , they say , be the pretty girl in the whole country side , though she be too white for my taste , ' and then the landlady pause again , and glance up at the farmer , to see how he be take it .
She do not learn much .
He be look straight before him , his teeth set .
But a she cease to talk , he say quietly , ` Go on . '
` There be not much more to tell , ' reply the landlady , for she suddenly remember that she must prepare supper for the hungry men who always stop at the inn on market day , before start for home , ` but one fine morning they both go to the little church on top of the hill , and be marry .
My cousin be servant to the priest , and she find out about it and tell me .
But good-day to you , sir ; here be your horse , and I must hurry off to the kitchen . '
It be lucky that the horse be sure-footed and know the road , for his bridle hung loose on his neck , and his master take no heed of the way he be go .
When the farm-house be reach , the man lead the animal to the stable , and then go to look for his son . '
I know everything -- you have deceive me .
Get out of my sight at once -- I have do with you , ' he stammer , choke with passion a he come up to the young man , who be cut a stick in front of the door , whistle gaily the while .
` But , father -- ' ` You be no son of mine ; I have only one now .
Begone , or it will be the bad for you , ' and a he speak he lift up his whip .
The young man shrink back .
He fear l his father should fall down in a fit , his face be so red and his eye seem burst from his head .
But it be no use staying : perhaps next morning the old man might listen to reason , though in his heart the son felt that he would never take back his word .
So he turn slowly away , and walk heavily along a path which end in a cave on the side of his hill , and there he sit through the night , thinking of what have happen .
Yes , he have be wrong , there be no doubt of that , and he do not quite know how it have come about .
He have mean to have tell his father all about it , and he be sure , quite sure , that if once the old man have see his wife , he would have forgive her poverty on account of her great beauty and goodness .
But he have put it off from day to day , hop always for a good opportunity , and now this be the end !
If the son have no sleep that night , no more have the father , and as soon a the sun rise , he send a messenger into the great city with order to bring back the younger brother .
When he arrive the farmer do not waste word , but inform him that he be now his only heir , and would inherit all his land and money , and that he be to come and live at home , and to help manage the property .
Though very pleased at the thought of become such a rich man -- for the brother have never care much for each other -- the young would rather have stay where he be , for he soon get tire of the country , and long for a town life .
However , this he keep to himself , and make the best of thing , work hard like his brother before him .
In this way the year go on , but the crop be not so good a they have be , and the old man give order that some fine house he be build in the city should be leave unfinished , for it would take all the saving to complete them .
As to the elder son , he would never even hear his name mention , and die at last without ever see his face , leave to the young , a he have promise , all his land , as well a his money .
Meanwhile , the son whom he have disinherit have grow poorer and poorer .
He and his wife be always look out for something to do , and never spend a penny that they could help , but luck be against them , and at the time of his father 's death they have hardly bread to eat or clothes to cover them .
If there have be only himself , he would have manage to get on somehow , but he could not bear to watch his child become weak day by day , and swallow his pride , at length he cross the mountain to his old home where his brother be live .
It be the first time for long that the two men have come face to face , and they look at each other in silence .
Then tear rise in the eye of the elder , but wink them hastily away , he say : ` Brother , it be not needful that I should tell you how poor I be ; you can see that for yourself .
I have not come to beg for money , but only to ask if you will give me those unfinished house of yours in the city , and I will make them watertight , so that my wife and child can live in them , and that will save our rent .
For a they be , they profit you nothing . '
And the young brother listen and pity him , and give him the house that he ask for , and the elder go away happy .
For some year thing go on a they be , and then the rich brother begin to feel lonely , and think to himself that he be get old , and it be time for him to be marry .
The wife he choose be very wealthy , but she be also very greedy , and however much she have , she always want more .
She be , besides , one of those unfortunate people who invariably fancy that the possession of other people must be good than their own .
Many a time her poor husband regret the day that he have first see her , and often her meanness and shabby way put him to shame .
But he have not the courage to rule her , and she only get bad and bad .
After she have be marry a few month the bride want to go into the city and buy herself some new dress .
She have never be there before , and when she have finish her shopping , she think she would pay a visit to her unknown sister-in-law , and rest for a bit .
The house she be seek be in a broad street , and ought to have be very magnificent , but the carved stone portico enclose a mean little door of rough wood , while a row of beautiful pillar lead to nothing .
The dwelling on each side be in the same unfinished condition , and water trickle down the wall .
Most people would have consider it a wretched place , and turn their back on it as soon a they could , but this lady saw that by spend some money the house could be make as splendid a they be originally intend to be , and she instantly resolve to get them for herself .
Full of this idea she walk up the marble staircase , and enter the little room where her sister-in-law sat , make clothes for her child .
The bride seem full of interest in the house , and ask a great many question about them , so that her new relation like her much good than they expect , and hop they might be good friend .
However , as soon a she reach home , she go straight to her husband , and tell him that he must get back those house from his brother , a they would exactly suit her , and she could easily make them into a palace as fine a the king 's .
But her husband only tell her that she might buy house in some other part of the town , for she could not have those , a he have long since make a gift of them to his brother , who have live there for many year past .
At this answer the wife grow very angry .
She begin to cry , and make such a noise that all the neighbour hear her and put their head out of the window , to see what be the matter .
` It be absurd , ' she sob out , ` quite unjust .
Indeed , if you come to think of it , the gift be worth nothing , a when her husband make it he be a bachelor , and since then he have be marry , and she have never give her consent to any such thing . '
And so she lament all day and all night , till the poor man be nearly worried to death ; and at last he do what she wish , and summon his brother in a court of law to give up the house which , he say , have only be lend to him .
But when the evidence on both side have be hear , the judge decide in favour of the poor man , which make the rich lady more furious than ever , and she determine not to rest until she have gain the day .
If one judge would not give her the house another should , and so time after time the case be try over again , till at last it come before the high judge of all , in the city of Evora .
Her husband be heartily tire and ashamed of the whole affair , but his weakness in not put a stop to it in the beginning have get him into this difficulty , and now he be force to go on .
On the same day the two brother set out on their journey to the city , the rich one on horseback , with plenty of food in his knapsack , the poor one on foot with nothing but a piece of bread and four onion to eat on the way .
The road be hilly and neither could go very fast , and when night fell , they be both glad to see some light in a window a little distance in front of them .
The light turn out to have be place there by a farmer , who have plan to have a particularly good supper a it be his wife 's birthday , and bid the rich man enter and sit down , while he himself take the horse to the stable .
The poor man ask timidly if he might spend the night in a corner , add that he have bring his own supper with him .
Another time permission might have be refuse him , for the farmer be no lover of humble folk , but now he give the elder brother leave to come in , point out a wooden chair where he could sit .
Supper be soon serve , and very glad the young brother be to eat it , for his long ride have make him very hungry .
The farmer 's wife , however , would touch nothing , and at last declare that the only supper she want be one of the onion the poor man be cook at the fire .
Of course he give it to her , though he would gladly have eat it himself , a three onion be not much at the end of a long day 's walk , and soon after they all go to sleep , the poor man make himself as comfortable a he could in his corner .
A few hour later the farmer be arouse by the cry and groan of his wife .
` Oh , I feel so ill , I 'm sure I 'm go to die , ' wept she .
` It be that onion , I know it be .
I wish I have never eat it .
It must have be poison . '
` If the man have poison you he shall pay for it , ' say her husband , and seize a thick stick he run downstairs and begin to beat the poor man , who have be sound asleep , and have nothing to defend himself with .
Luckily , the noise arouse the young brother , who jump up and snatch the stick from the farmer 's hand , say : ` We be both go to Evora to try a law-suit .
Come too , and accuse him there if he have attempt to rob you or murder you , but do n't kill him now , or you will get yourself into trouble . '
` Well , perhaps you be right , ' answer the farmer , ` but the sooner that fellow have his desert , the good I shall be please , ' and without more word he go to the stable and bring out a horse for himself and also the black Andalusian mare ridden by the rich man , while the poor brother , fear more ill-treatment , start at once on foot .
Now all that night it have rain heavily , and do not seem likely to stop , and in some place the road be so thick with mud that it be almost impossible to get across it .
In one spot it be so very bad that a mule laden with baggage have get stick in it , and tug a he might , his master be quite unable to pull him out .
The muleteer in despair appeal to the two horseman , who be carefully skirt the swamp at some distance off , but they pay no heed to his cry , and he begin to talk cheerfully to his mule , hop to keep up his spirit , declare that if the poor beast would only have a little patience help be sure to come .
And so it do , for very soon the poor brother reach the place , bespatter with mud from head to foot , but ready to do all he could to help with the mule and his master .
First they set about find some stout log of wood to lay down on the marsh so that they could reach the mule , for by this time his frantic struggle have break his bridle , and he be deeply in than ever .
Stepping cautiously along the wood , the poor man contrive to lay hold of the animal 's tale , and with a desperate effort the mule manage to regain his foot on dry ground , but at the cost of leave his tail in the poor man 's hand .
When he saw this the muleteer 's anger know no bound , and forget that without the help give him he would have lose his mule altogether , he begin to abuse the poor man , declare that he have ruin his beast , and the law would make him pay for it .
Then , jump on the back of the mule , which be so glad to be out of the choke mud that he do not seem to mind the loss of his tail , the ungrateful wretch rode on , and that even reach the inn at Evora , where the rich man and the farmer have already arrive for the night .
Meanwhile the poor brother walk wearily along , wonder what other dreadful adventure be in store for him . '
I shall certainly be condemn for one or other of them , ' think he sadly ; ` and after all , if I have to die , I would rather choose my own death than leave it to my enemy , ' and as soon a he enter Evora he look about for a place suitable for carry out the plan he have make .
At length he find what he seek , but a it be too late and too dark for him to make sure of success , he curl himself up under a doorway , and sleep till morning .
Although it be winter , the sun rise in a clear sky , and it ray felt almost warm when the poor man get up and shake himself .
He intend it to be the day of his death , but in spite of that , and of the fact that he be leave his wife and child behind him , he felt almost cheerful .
He have struggle so long , and be so very , very tired ; but he would not have mind that if he could have prove his innocence , and triumph over his enemy .
However , they have all be too clever for him , and he have no strength to fight any more .
So he mount the stone step that lead to the battlement of the city , and stop for a moment to gaze about him .
It happen that an old sick man who live near by have beg to be carry out and to be lay at the foot of the wall so that the beam of the rise sun might fall upon him , and he would be able to talk with his friend a they pass by to their work .
Little do he guess that on top of the battlement , exactly over his head , stand a man who be take his last look at the same sun , before go to his death that await him .
But so it be ; and a the steeple opposite be touch by the golden light , the poor man shut his eye and sprang forward .
The wall be high , and he fly rapidly through the air , but it be not the ground he touch , only the body of the sick man , who roll over and die without a groan .
As for the other , he be quite unhurt , and be slowly rise to his foot when his arm be suddenly seize and hold .
` You have kill our father , do you see ?
do you see ? '
cry two young men , ` and you will come with u this instant before the judge , and answer for it . '
` Your father ?
but I do n't know him .
What do you mean ? '
ask the poor man , who be quite bewilder with his sudden rush through the air , and could not think why he should be accuse of this fresh crime .
But he get no reply , and be only hurry through the street to the court-house , where his brother , the muleteer , and the farmer have just arrive , all as angry a ever , all talk at once , till the judge enter and order them to be silent . '
I will hear you one by one , ' he say , and motion the young brother to begin .
He do not take long to state his case .
The unfinished house be his , leave him with the rest of the property by his father , and his brother refuse to give them up .
In answer , the poor man tell , in a few word , how he have beg the house from his brother , and produce the deed of gift which make him their owner .
The judge listen quietly and ask a few question ; then he give his verdict .
` The house shall remain the property of the man to whom they be give , and to whom they belong .
And a you , ' he add , turn to the young brother , ` brought this accusation know full well it be wicked and unjust , I order you , besides lose the house , to pay a thousand pound damage to your brother . '
The rich man hear the judge with rage in his heart , the poor man with surprise and gratitude .
But he be not safe yet , for now it be the turn of the farmer .
The judge could hardly conceal a smile at the story , and inquired if the wife be dead before the farmer leave the house , and receive for answer that he be in such a hurry for justice to be do that he have not wait to see .
Then the poor man tell his tale , and once more judgment be give in his favour , while twelve hundred pound be order to be pay him .
As for the muleteer , he be inform very plainly that he have prove himself mean and ungrateful for the help that have be give him , and a a punishment he must pay to the poor man a fine of fifty pound , and hand him over the mule till his tail have grow again .
Lastly , there come the two son of the sick man .
` This be the wretch who kill our father , ' they say , ` and we demand that he should die also . '
` How do you kill him ? '
ask the judge , turn to the accuse , and the poor man tell how he have leap from the wall , not know that anyone be beneath .
` Well , this be my judgment , ' reply the judge , when they have all speak : ` Let the accused sit under the wall , and let the son of the dead man jump from the top and fall on him and kill him , and if they will not to this , then they be condemn to pay eight hundred pound for their false accusation . '
The young men look at each other , and slowly shake their head .
` We will pay the fine , ' say they , and the judge nod .
So the poor man ride the mule home , and bring back to his family enough money to keep them in comfort to the end of their day .
Adapted from the Portuguese .
The One-Handed Girl An old couple once live in a hut under a grove of palm tree , and they have one son and one daughter .
They be all very happy together for many year , and then the father become very ill , and felt he be go to die .
He call his child to the place where he lay on the floor -- for no one have any bed in that country -- and say to his son , ' I have no herd of cattle to leave you -- only the few thing there be in the house -- for I be a poor man , a you know .
But choose : will you have my blessing or my property ? '
` Your property , certainly , ' answer the son , and his father nod .
` And you ? '
ask the old man of the girl , who stand by her brother . '
I will have blessing , ' she answer , and her father give her much blessing .
That night he die , and his wife and son and daughter mourn for him seven day , and give him a burial accord to the custom of his people .
But hardly be the time of mourn over , than the mother be attack by a disease which be common in that country . '
I be go away from you , ' she say to her child , in a faint voice ; ` but first , my son , choose which you will have : blessing or property . '
` Property , certainly , ' answer the son .
` And you , my daughter ? ' '
I will have blessing , ' say the girl ; and her mother give her much blessing , and that night she die .
When the day of mourn be end , the brother bid his sister put outside the hut all that belong to his father and his mother .
So the girl put them out , and he take them away , save only a small pot and a vessel in which she could clean her corn .
But she have no corn to clean .
She sit at home , sad and hungry , when a neighbour knock at the door .
` My pot have crack in the fire , lend me yours to cook my supper in , and I will give you a handful of corn in return . '
And the girl be glad , and that night she be able to have supper herself , and next day another woman borrow her pot , and then another and another , for never be know so many accident a befell the village pot at that time .
She soon grow quite fat with all the corn she earn with the help of her pot , and then one even she pick up a pumpkin seed in a corner , and plant it near her well , and it spring up , and give her many pumpkin .
At last it happen that a youth from her village pass through the place where the girl 's brother be , and the two met and talk .
` What news be there of my sister ? '
ask the young man , with whom thing have go badly , for he be idle .
` She be fat and well-liking , ' reply the youth , ` for the woman borrow her mortar to clean their corn , and borrow her pot to cook it in , and for al this they give her more food than she can eat . '
And he go his way .
Now the brother be fill with envy at the word of the man , and he set out at once , and before dawn he have reach the hut , and saw the pot and the mortar be stand outside .
He sling them over his shoulder and depart , pleased with his own cleverness ; but when his sister awoke and sought for the pot to cook her corn for breakfast , she could find it nowhere .
At length she say to herself , ` Well , some thief must have steal them while I sleep .
I will go and see if any of my pumpkin be ripe . '
And indeed they be , and so many that the tree be almost break by the weight of them .
So she eat what she want and take the others to the village , and give them in exchange for corn , and the woman say that no pumpkin be as sweet a these , and that she be to bring every day all that she have .
In this way she earn more than she need for herself , and soon be able to get another mortar and cooking pot in exchange for her corn .
Then she think she be quite rich .
Unluckily someone else think so too , and this be her brother 's wife , who have hear all about the pumpkin tree , and send her slave with a handful of grain to buy her a pumpkin .
At first the girl tell him that so few be leave that she could not spare any ; but when she find that he belong to her brother , she change her mind , and go out to the tree and gather the large and the ripest that be there .
` Take this one , ' she say to the slave , ` and carry it back to your mistress , but tell her to keep the corn , a the pumpkin be a gift . '
The brother 's wife be overjoy at the sight of the fruit , and when she taste it , she declare it be the nice she have ever eat .
Indeed , all night she think of nothing else , and early in the morning she call another slave -LRB- for she be a rich woman -RRB- and bid him go and ask for another pumpkin .
But the girl , who have just be out to look at her tree , tell him that they be all eaten , so he go back empty-handed to his mistress .
In the evening her husband return from hunt a long way off , and find his wife in tear .
` What be the matter ? '
ask he . '
I send a slave with some grain to your sister to buy some pumpkin , but she would not sell me any , and tell me there be none , though I know she let other people buy them . '
` Well , never mind now -- go to sleep , ' say he , ` and to-morrow I will go and pull up the pumpkin tree , and that will punish her for treat you so badly . '
So before sunrise he get up and set out for his sister 's house , and find her cleaning some corn .
` Why do you refuse to sell my wife a pumpkin yesterday when she want one ? '
he ask .
` The old one be finish , and the new one be not yet come , ' answer the girl .
` When her slave arrive two day ago , there be only four leave ; but I give him one , and would take no corn for it . ' '
I do not believe you ; you have sell them all to other people .
I shall go and cut down the pumpkin , ' cry her brother in a rage .
` If you cut down the pumpkin you shall cut off my hand with it , ' exclaim the girl , run up to her tree and catch hold of it .
But her brother follow , and with one blow cut off the pumpkin and her hand too .
Then he go into the house and take away everything he could find , and sell the house to a friend of his who have long wish to have it , and his sister have no home to go to .
Meanwhile she have bath her arm carefully , and bound on it some heal leaf that grow near by , and wrap a cloth round the leaf , and go to hide in the forest , that her brother might not find her again .
For seven day she wander about , eat only the fruit that hung from the tree above her , and every night she climb up and tuck herself safely among the creeper which bind together the big branch , so that neither lion nor tiger nor panther might get at her .
When she wake up on the seventh morning she saw from her perch smoke come up from a little town on the edge of the forest .
The sight of the hut make her feel more lonely and helpless than before .
She long desperately for a draught of milk from a gourd , for there be no stream in that part , and she be very thirsty , but how be she to earn anything with only one hand ?
And at this think her courage fail , and she begin to cry bitterly .
It happen that the king 's son have come out from the town very early to shoot bird , and when the sun grow hot he leave tired . '
I will lie here and rest under this tree , ' he say to his attendant .
` You can go and shoot instead , and I will just have this slave to stay with me ! '
Away they go , and the young man fell asleep , and sleep long .
Suddenly he be awaken by something wet and salt fall on his face .
` What be that ?
Is it rain ? '
he say to his slave .
` Go and look . '
` No , master , it be not rain , ' answer the slave .
` Then climb up the tree and see what it be , ' and the slave climb up , and come back and tell his master that a beautiful girl be sit up there , and that it must have be her tear which have fall on the face of the king 's son .
` Why be she cry ? '
inquire the prince . '
I can not tell -- I do not dare to ask her ; but perhaps she would tell you . '
And the master , greatly wonder , climb up the tree .
` What be the matter with you ? '
say he gently , and , a she only sob louder , he continue : ` Are you a woman , or a spirit of the wood ? ' '
I be a woman , ' she answer slowly , wipe her eye with a leaf of the creeper that hung about her .
` Then why do you cry ? '
he persist . '
I have many thing to cry for , ' she reply , ` more than you could ever guess . '
` Come home with me , ' say the prince ; ` it be not very far .
Come home to my father and mother .
I be a king 's son . '
` Then why be you here ? '
she say , open her eye and star at him .
` Once every month I and my friend shoot bird in the forest , ' he answer , ` but I be tire and bid them leave me to rest .
And you -- what be you do up in this tree ? '
At that she begin to cry again , and tell the king 's son all that have befall her since the death of her mother . '
I can not come down with you , for I do not like anyone to see me , ' she end with a sob .
` Oh !
I will manage all that , ' say the king 's son , and swing himself to a low branch , he bid his slave go quickly into the town , and bring back with him four strong men and a curtained litter .
When the man be go , the girl climb down , and hide herself on the ground in some bush .
Very soon the slave return with the litter , which be place on the ground close to the bush where the girl lay .
` Now go , all of you , and call my attendant , for I do not wish to say here any longer , ' he say to the men , and as soon a they be out of sight he bid the girl get into the litter , and fasten the curtain tightly .
Then he get in on the other side , and wait till his attendant come up .
` What be the matter , O son of a king ? '
ask they , breathless with run . '
I think I be ill ; I be cold , ' he say , and sign to the bearer , he draw the curtain , and be carry through the forest right inside his own house .
` Tell my father and mother that I have a fever , and want some gruel , ' say he , ` and bid them send it quickly . '
So the slave hasten to the king 's palace and give his message , which trouble both the king and the queen greatly .
A pot of hot gruel be instantly prepared , and carry over to the sick man , and as soon a the council which be sit be over , the king and his minister go to pay him a visit , bear a message from the queen that she would follow a little later .
Now the prince have pretend to be ill in order to soften his parent 's heart , and the next day he declare he felt well , and , get into his litter , be carry to the palace in state , drum be beat all along the road .
He dismount at the foot of the step and walk up , a great parasol be hold over his head by a slave .
Then he enter the cool , dark room where his father and mother be sit , and say to them : ' I saw a girl yesterday in the forest whom I wish to marry , and , unknown to my attendant , I bring her back to my house in a litter .
Give me your consent , I beg , for no other woman please me a well , even though she have but one hand ! '
Of course the king and queen would have prefer a daughter-in-law with two hand , and one who could have bring rich with her , but they could not bear to say ` No ' to their son , so they tell him it should be a he choose , and that the wedding feast should be prepare immediately .
The girl could scarcely believe her good fortune , and , in gratitude for all the kindness show her , be so useful and pleasant to her husband 's parent that they soon love her .
By and bye a baby be bear to her , and soon after that the prince be send on a journey by his father to visit some of the distant town of the kingdom , and to set right thing that have go wrong .
No sooner have he start than the girl 's brother , who have waste all the rich his wife have bring him in recklessness and folly , and be now very poor , chance to come into the town , and a he pass he hear a man say , ` Do you know that the king 's son have marry a woman who have lose one of her hand ? '
On hear these word the brother stop and ask , ` Where do he find such a woman ? '
` In the forest , ' answer the man , and the cruel brother guess at once it must be his sister .
A great rage take possession of his soul a he think of the girl whom he have try to ruin be after all so much good off than himself , and he vow that he would work her ill .
Therefore that very afternoon he make his way to the palace and ask to see the king .
When he be admit to his presence , he kneel down and touch the ground with his forehead , and the king bid him stand up and tell wherefore he have come .
` By the kindness of your heart have you be deceive , O king , ' say he .
` Your son have marry a girl who have lose a hand .
Do you know why she have lose it ?
She be a witch , and have wed three husband , and each husband she have put to death with her art .
Then the people of the town cut off her hand , and turn her into the forest .
And what I say be true , for her town be my town also . '
The king listen , and his face grow dark .
Unluckily he have a hasty temper , and do not stop to reason , and , instead of send to the town , and discover people who know his daughter-in-law and could have tell him how hard she have work and how poor she have be , he believe all the brother 's lying word , and make the queen believe them too .
Together they take counsel what they should do , and in the end they decide that they also would put her out of the town .
But this do not content the brother .
` Kill her , ' he say .
` It be no more than she deserve for dare to marry the king 's son .
Then she can do no more hurt to anyone . '
` We can not kill her , ' answer they ; ` if we do , our son would assuredly kill u .
Let u do a the others do , and put her out of the town .
And with this the envious brother be force to be content .
The poor girl love her husband very much , but just then the baby be more to her than all else in the world , and as long a she have him with her , she do not very much mind anything .
So , take her son on her arm , and hang a little earthen pot for cook round her neck , she leave her house with it great peacock fan and slave and seat of ivory , and plunge into the forest .
For a while she walk , not know whither she go , then by and bye she grow tired , and sit under a tree to rest and to hush her baby to sleep .
Suddenly she raise her eye , and saw a snake wriggling from under the bush towards her . '
I be a dead woman , ' she say to herself , and stay quite still , for indeed she be too frighten to move .
In another minute the snake have reach her side , and to her surprise he speak .
` Open your earthen pot , and let me go in .
Save me from sun , and I will save you from rain , ' and she open the pot , and when the snake have slip in , she put on the cover .
Soon she behold another snake come after the other one , and when it have reach her it stop and say , ` Did you see a small grey snake pas this way just now ? '
` Yes , ' she answer , ` it be go very quickly . '
` Ah , I must hurry and catch it up , ' reply the second snake , and it hasten on .
When it be out of sight , a voice from the pot say : ` Uncover me , ' and she lift the lid , and the little grey snake slide rapidly to the ground . '
I be safe now , ' he say .
` But tell me , where be you go ? ' '
I can not tell you , for I do not know , ' she answer . '
I be just wander in the wood . '
` Follow me , and let u go home together , ' say the snake , and the girl follow his through the forest and along the green path , till they come to a great lake , where they stop to rest .
` The sun be hot , ' say the snake , ` and you have walk far .
Take your baby and bathe in that cool place where the bough of the tree stretch far over the water . '
` Yes , I will , ' answer she , and they go in .
The baby splash and crow with delight , and then he give a spring and fell right in , down , down , down , and his mother could not find him , though she search all among the reed .
Full of terror , she make her way back to the bank , and call to the snake , ` My baby be go !
-- he be drown , and never shall I see him again . '
` Go in once more , ' say the snake , ` and feel everywhere , even among the tree that have their root in the water , l perhaps he may be hold fast there . '
Swiftly she go back and felt everywhere with her whole hand , even put her finger into the tiny cranny , where a crab could hardly have take shelter .
` No , he be not here , ' she cry .
` How be I to live without him ? '
But the snake take no notice , and only answer , ` Put in your other arm too . '
` What be the use of that ? '
she ask , ` when it have no hand to feel with ? '
but all the same she do a she be bid , and in an instant the wounded arm touch something round and soft , lie between two stone in a clump of reed .
` My baby , my baby ! '
she shout , and lift him up , merry and laughing , and not a bit hurt or frighten .
` Have you find him this time ? '
ask the snake .
` Yes , oh , yes ! '
she answer , ` and , why -- why -- I have get my hand back again ! '
and from sheer joy she burst into tear .
The snake let her weep for a little while , and then he say -- ` Now we will journey on to my family , and we will all repay you for the kindness you show to me . '
` You have do more than enough in give me back my hand , ' reply the girl ; but the snake only smile .
` Be quick , l the sun should set , ' he answer , and begin to wriggle along so fast that the girl could hardly follow him .
By and bye they arrive at the house in a tree where the snake live , when he be not travel with his father and mother .
And he tell them all his adventure , and how he have escape from his enemy .
The father and mother snake could not do enough to show their gratitude .
They make their guest lie down on a hammock woven of the strong creeper which hang from bough to bough , till she be quite rested after her wandering , while they watch the baby and give him milk to drink from the cocoa-nuts which they persuade their friend the monkey to crack for them .
They even manage to carry small fruit tie up in their tail for the baby 's mother , who felt at last that she be safe and at peace .
Not that she forget her husband , for she often think of him and long to show him her son , and in the night she would sometimes lie awake and wonder where he be .
In this manner many week pass by .
And what be the prince do ?
Well , he have fall very ill when he be on the furthest border of the kingdom , and he be nurse by some kind people who do not know who he be , so that the king and queen heard nothing about him .
When he be well he make his way home again , and into his father 's palace , where he find a strange man stand behind the throne with the peacock 's feather .
This be his wife 's brother , whom the king have take into high favour , though , of course , the prince be quite ignorant of what have happen .
For a moment the king and queen star at their son , a if he have be unknown to them ; he have grow so thin and weak during his illness that his shoulder be bow like those of an old man .
` Have you forget me so soon ? '
he ask .
At the sound of his voice they give a cry and run towards him , and pour out question a to what have happen , and why he look like that .
But the prince do not answer any of them .
` How be my wife ? '
he say .
There be a pause .
Then the queen reply : ` She be dead . '
` Dead ! '
he repeat , step a little backwards .
` And my child ? '
` He be dead too . '
The young man stand silent .
Then he say , ` Show me their graf . '
At these word the king , who have be feel rather uncomfortable , take heart again , for have he not prepare two beautiful tomb for his son to see , so that he might never , never guess what have be do to his wife ?
All these month the king and queen have be tell each other how good and merciful they have be not to take her brother 's advice and to put her to death .
But now , this somehow do not seem so certain .
Then the king lead the way to the courtyard just behind the palace , and through the gate into a beautiful garden where stand two splendid tomb in a green space under the tree .
The prince advance alone , and , rest his head against the stone , he burst into tear .
His father and mother stand silently behind with a curious pang in their soul which they do not quite understand .
Could it be that they be ashamed of themselves ?
But after a while the prince turn round , and walk past them in to the palace he bid the slave bring him mourning .
For seven day no one saw him , but at the end of them he go out hunting , and help his father rule his people .
Only no one dare to speak to him of his wife and son .
At last one morning , after the girl have be lie awake all night thinking of her husband , she say to her friend the snake : ` You have all show me much kindness , but now I be well again , and want to go home and hear some news of my husband , and if he still mourn for me ! '
Now the heart of the snake be sad at her word , but he only say : ` Yes , thus it must be ; go and bid farewell to my father and mother , but if they offer you a present , see that you take nothing but my father 's ring and my mother 's casket . '
So she go to the parent snake , who weep bitterly at the thought of lose her , and offer her gold and jewel as much a she could carry in remembrance of them .
But the girl shake her head and push the shin heap away from her . '
I shall never forget you , never , ' she say in a broken voice , ` but the only tokens I will accept from you be that little ring and this old casket . '
The two snake look at each other in dismay .
The ring and the casket be the only thing they do not want her to have .
Then after a short pause they speak .
` Why do you want the ring and casket so much ?
Who have tell you of them ? '
` Oh , nobody ; it be just my fancy , ' answer she .
But the old snake shake their head and reply : ` Not so ; it be our son who tell you , and , a he say , so it must be .
If you need food , or clothes , or a house , tell the ring and it will find them for you .
And if you be unhappy or in danger , tell the casket and it will set thing right . '
Then they both give her their blessing , and she pick up her baby and go her way .
She walk for a long time , till at length she come near the town where her husband and his father dwelt .
Here she stop under a grove of palm tree , and tell the ring that she want a house .
` It be ready , mistress , ' whisper a queer little voice which make her jump , and , look behind her , she saw a lovely palace make of the fine wood , and a row of slave with tall fan bow before the door .
Glad indeed be she to enter , for she be very tired , and , after eat a good supper of fruit and milk which she find in one of the room , she fling herself down on a pile of cushion and go to sleep with her baby beside her .
Here she stay quietly , and every day the baby grow taller and strong , and very soon he could run about and even talk .
Of course the neighbour have a great deal to say about the house which have be build so quickly -- so very quickly -- on the outskirt of the town , and invent all kind of story about the rich lady who live in it .
And by and bye , when the king return with his son from the war , some of these tale reach his ear .
` It be really very odd about that house under the palm , ' he say to the queen ; ' I must find out something of the lady whom no one ever see .
I daresay it be not a lady at all , but a gang of conspirator who want to get possession of my throne .
To-morrow I shall take my son and my chief minister and insist on get inside . '
Soon after sunrise next day the prince 's wife be stand on a little hill behind the house , when she saw a cloud of dust come through the town .
A moment afterwards she hear faintly the roll of the drum that announce the king 's presence , and saw a crowd of people approach the grove of palm .
Her heart beat fast .
Could her husband be among them ?
In any case they must not discover her there ; so just bid the ring prepare some food for them , she run inside , and bound a veil of golden gauze round her head and face .
Then , take the child 's hand , she go to the door and wait .
