In a few minute the whole procession come up , and she step forward and beg them to come in and rest .
` Willingly , ' answer the king ; ` go first , and we will follow you . '
They follow her into a long dark room , in which be a table cover with gold cup and basket fill with date and cocoa-nuts and all kind of ripe yellow fruit , and the king and the prince sit upon cushion and be serve by slave , while the minister , among whom she recognise her own brother , stand behind .
` Ah , I owe all my misery to him , ' she say to herself .
` From the first he have hat me , ' but outwardly she show nothing .
And when the king ask her what news there be in the town she only answer : ` You have ride far ; eat first , and drink , for you must be hungry and thirsty , and then I will tell you my news . '
` You speak sense , ' answer the king , and silence prevail for some time longer .
Then he say : ` Now , lady , I have finish , and be refresh , therefore tell me , I pray you , who you be , and whence you come ?
But , first , be seat . '
She bow her head and sit down on a big scarlet cushion , draw her little boy , who be asleep in a corner , on to her knee , and begin to tell the story of her life .
As her brother listen , he would fain have leave the house and hidden himself in the forest , but it be his duty to wave the fan of peacock 's feather over the king 's head to keep off the fly , and he know he would be seize by the royal guard if he try to desert his post .
He must stay where he be , there be no help for it , and luckily for him the king be too much interested in the tale to notice that the fan have cease moving , and that fly be dance right on the top of his thick curly hair .
The story go on , but the story-teller never once look at the prince , even through her veil , though he on his side never move his eye from her .
When she reach the part where she have sit weep in the tree , the king 's son could restrain himself no longer .
` It be my wife , ' he cry , spring to where she sit with the sleep child in her lap .
` They have lie to me , and you be not dead after all , nor the boy either !
But what have happen ?
Why do they lie to me ?
and why do you leave my house where you be safe ? '
And he turn and look fiercely at his father .
` Let me finish my tale first , and then you will know , ' answer she , throw back her veil , and she tell how her brother have come to the palace and accuse her of be a witch , and have try to persuade the king to slay her .
` But he would not do that , ' she continue softly , ` and after all , if I have stay on in your house , I should never have meet the snake , nor have get my hand back again .
So let u forget all about it , and be happy once more , for see !
our son be grow quite a big boy . '
` And what shall be do to your brother ? '
ask the king , who be glad to think that someone have act in this matter bad than himself .
` Put him out of the town , ' answer she .
From ` Swaheli Tales , ' by E. Steere .
The Bones of Djulung In a beautiful island that lie in the southern sea , where chain of gay orchid bind the tree together , and the day and night be equally long and nearly equally hot , there once live a family of seven sister .
Their father and mother be dead , and they have no brother , so the eldest girl rule over the rest , and they all do a she bid them .
One sister have to clean the house , a second carried water from the spring in the forest , a third cook their food , while to the young fell the hard task of all , for she have to cut and bring home the wood which be to keep the fire continually burn .
This be very hot and tiring work , and when she have feed the fire and heap up in a corner the stick that be to supply it till the next day , she often throw herself down under a tree , and go sound asleep .
One morning , however , a she be stagger along with her bundle on her back , she think that the river which flow past their hut look so cool and invite that she determine to bathe in it , instead of take her usual nap .
Hastily pile up her load by the fire , and thrust some stick into the flame , she run down to the river and jump in .
How delicious it be dive and swim and float in the dark forest , where the tree be so thick that you could hardly see the sun !
But after a while she begin to look about her , and her eye fell on a little fish that seem make out of a rainbow , so brilliant be the colour he flash out . '
I should like him for a pet , ' think the girl , and the next time the fish swam by , she put out her hand and catch him .
Then she run along the grassy path till she come to a cave in front of which a stream fell over some rock into a basin .
Here she put her little fish , whose name be Djulung-djulung , and promise to return soon and bring him some dinner , she go away .
By the time she get home , the rice for their dinner be ready cook , and the eldest sister give the other six their portion in wooden bowl .
But the young do not finish hers , and when no one be look , steal off to the fountain in the forest where the little fish be swim about .
` See !
I have not forget you , ' she cry , and one by one she let the grain of rice fall into the water , where the fish gobble them up greedily , for he have never taste anything so nice .
` That be all for to-day , ' she say at last , ` but I will come again to-morrow , ' and bid him good-bye she go down the path .
Now the girl do not tell her sister about the fish , but every day she save half of her rice to give him , and call him softly in a little song she have make for herself .
If she sometimes felt hungry , no one knew of it , and , indeed , she do not mind that much , when she saw how the fish enjoy it .
And the fish grow fat and big , but the girl grow thin and weak , and the load of wood felt heavier every day , and at last her sister notice it .
Then they take counsel together , and watch her to see what she do , and one of them follow her to the fountain where Djulung live , and saw her give him all the rice she have save from her breakfast .
Hastening home the sister tell the others what she have witness , and that a lovely fat fish might be have for the catching .
So the eldest sister go and catch him , and he be boil for supper , but the young sister be away in the wood , and do not know anything about it .
Next morning she go as usual to the cave , and sing her little song , but no Djulung come to answer it ; twice and thrice she sang , then throw herself on her knee by the edge , and peer into the dark water , but the tree cast such a deep shadow that her eye could not pierce it .
` Djulung can not be dead , or his body would be float on the surface , ' she say to herself , and rise to her foot she set out homewards , feel all of a sudden strangely tire .
